<b class="custom-color">UPTIMIZE Foundry</b> empowers all Merck users
from all functional roles to use data at scale to transform the way that they operate within a collaborative ecosystem. Within <b class="custom-color">UPTIMIZE Foundry</b>, there are tools to manage the challenges of data management and integration.

<b class="custom-color">UPTIMIZE Foundry</b>  is a powerful, fast and central platform with fully integrated workflows. It offers powerful analysis tools, easy to create reports and dashboards for your analysis work.  

<b class="custom-color">UPTIMIZE Foundry</b>  is a large-scale data integration platform, built by Palantir, around five core ideas:<br><br>

<ld-tabs>
  <ld-tablist>
    <ld-tab selected><b class="custom-color">1.</b> Data integration</ld-tab>
    <ld-tab><b class="custom-color">2. </b>   Data Scale</ld-tab>
    <ld-tab><b class="custom-color">3. </b>   Data Synthesis</ld-tab>
    <ld-tab><b class="custom-color">4. </b>   Data Lineage</ld-tab>
    <ld-tab><b class="custom-color">5. </b>   Collaboration</ld-tab>
    
  </ld-tablist>
  <ld-tabpanellist>
    <ld-tabpanel>
      <ld-typo style="margin-top: 1rem">
         <b class="custom-color">UPTIMIZE Foundry</b> is a single, central platform where you can integrate all kinds of data. Over time, organizations can incrementally increase the business-critical data in <b class="custom-color">UPTIMIZE Foundry</b> so that consumers can access the data wherever and whenever they need it in one place. Please note the data integration via automated data connections is mainly managed by the Sector Data Offices.
      </ld-typo>
    </ld-tabpanel>
    <ld-tabpanel>
      <ld-typo style="margin-top: 1rem">
        It enables you to analyze data at a large scale, as you can take advantage of the power of <b class="custom-color">UPTIMIZE Foundry's</b> distributed computing cluster.
      </ld-typo>
    </ld-tabpanel>
    <ld-tabpanel>
      <ld-typo style="margin-top: 1rem">
        Because the data lives in a shared infrastructure, <b class="custom-color">UPTIMIZE Foundry</b> enables you to easily combine and analyze data from different sources and systems in minutes.
      </ld-typo>
      </ld-tabpanel>
     <ld-tabpanel>
      <ld-typo style="margin-top: 1rem">
        <b class="custom-color">UPTIMIZE Foundry</b> keeps track of the relationships between datasets and the logic for transforming one dataset into another. This makes it easy to keep all of your data and reports "fresh" and enables you to define useful data visualizations, keeping them up to date without a single line of code.</ld-typo>
    </ld-tabpanel>
        <ld-tabpanel>

       Because <b class="custom-color">UPTIMIZE Foundry</b> is a shared environment, it fosters collaboration. You no longer have five different versions of an Excel report being sent over email. Because your report lives in <b class="custom-color">UPTIMIZE Foundry</b>, your teammates can always see the latest version of your data analysis and visualizations.</ld-typo>

# Data Ingestion & Enhancement Process Overview

The data ingestion process is driven by the data needs of the use cases from various value streams. Users can raise the following requests for the ingestions via [Data Treasury](https://palantir.mcloud.merckgroup.com/workspace/module/view/latest/ri.workshop.main.module.10e9a51d-489e-4610-b6ce-e93a1bc66912/home):

- [Data Ingestion Request (DIR)](./DIR-DER/) where, new data is connected to the associated source and ingested into the lake.
- [Data Enhancement Request (DER)](./DIR-DER/) where, the existing data items are enhanced with additional columns.
- [Data related Issues](https://palantir.mcloud.merckgroup.com/workspace/issues-app/) raised by the users related to DIRs, DERs or data are also handled by the team.

| **Teams Involved**  |**Activities:**|**Process**|
|:--------------------------------------------------------------------|:----------------------------|:----|
|Data Steward team  | Data Ingestions |Evaluate the data needs of the Use Case
| Data Ingestion team  | Data Enhancements<br>Data Pipeline development|Identify the connection types, credentials, and details<br>Establish the Connection<br>Ingest the data

---

# DIR and DER Workflow Lifecycle

Below you will find information that will show and walk you through the journey of a Data Ingestion Approval Request (DIR) and a Data Enhancement Approval Request (DER).  It will also provide you with a high level explanation of  each workflow status, Owner and general actions.

### <span style="color:#0F69AF">**Legend of Terms**</span>

- SDO Data Steward = S_DS    
- Data Ingestion Request = DIR
- SDO Product Owner = S_PO
- SDO Data Engineer = S_DE
- Data Owner = DO   
- Business Data Steward = B_DS
- Data Ingestion Request = DIR
- Data Enhancement Request = DER
- Data Treasury Item = DTI                  

## Ingestion Journey

<span style="color:#0F69AF">**Driving the DIR through the Ingestion Journey:** From Request to Ingestion to Business Impact</span>

![Picture 1](https://docs.uptimize.merckgroup.com/docs-assets/foundry/Foundry/Data_IngestionEnhancement/DIR_and_DER_Workflow_Lifecycle/Picture1.png)

## DIR Action Steps

<span style="color:#0F69AF">Below shows the Data **ingestion** lifecycle flow of the DIR and the action steps which trigger the movement from one status to another status.</span>

![Picture 2](https://docs.uptimize.merckgroup.com/docs-assets/foundry/Foundry/Data_IngestionEnhancement/DIR_and_DER_Workflow_Lifecycle/DIR_Workflow.png)

## DER Action Steps

<span style="color:#0F69AF">Below shows the Data **enhancement** lifecycle flow of the DER and the action steps which trigger the movement from one status to another status.</span>

![Picture 3](https://docs.uptimize.merckgroup.com/docs-assets/foundry/Foundry/Data_IngestionEnhancement/DIR_and_DER_Workflow_Lifecycle/Picture3.png)

## DIR / DER Workflow Status, Owner & Action

<span style="color:#0F69AF">The information below explains the actions needed by the respective owners of each DIR and DER workflow status.</span>

## Requested - Any User

- Creates a request for Data ingestion or Data enhancement - driven by a Use Case when required data doesn't exist
- Includes as much detail about the data being requested, i.e. tables & fields (if known), data source, provide sample reports and/or files


## Assessment - SDO Data Steward

- Ensures DIR / DER has clear and concise requirements
- Ensures critical fields/data are provided
- Coordinate alignment/clarification meetings, if needed
- Support from the S_PO as needed

## Pending Approval - SDO Data Steward

- Confirms the critical elements that have been provided (Use Case, Data Context Boundaries, Source, DO,  B_DS and IT Responsible) 

- **Note:** <span style="color:pink">Action N/A for DER</span>

## Approved for Ingestion/Enhancement - Data Owner

- You as a Data Owner accept the data ownership through the upcoming ingestion process.
- You will conduct a final business review of the ingestion scope and outcome.
- You also have the option to ask for more details or to reject the DIR (cancel the request).
- Your approval will initiate subsequent Data Office prioritization and resource assignment.

(The DO is the primary owner; B_DS is the back up and an S_DS can act as a Firefighter)

## Ingestion/Enhancement in Progress - SDO Data Steward or Engineer

- Accepts workload and resource ownership

- SDO or other Engineer starts technical development

- Project Structure must be created, and core team access granted

## Ingested/Enhanced - SDO Data Steward or Engineer

- Starts formal data verification by Business Data Steward 

- Metadata can be loaded, dataset to be created in ontology project folder

## Verified - Business Data Steward

- Completes data verification and communicate to S_DS
- Dataset Schema is correct & Metadata prep (date vs text vs string)
- Business transformation rules are correct
- Build schedule is executed as defined
- Data Content is correct (Target matches Source)
- DIR/DER status = Verified

## In Data Treasury - SDO Data Steward

- DIR/DER status = Verified > Trigger for SDO Data Steward to create the Data Treasury Item (DTI)
- Creation of the Data Treasury Completeness Check (DTCC)
- Data is formally cataloged in Data Lake
- **Note:**<span style="color:pink"> This action does not create a new DTI  </span>

(The S_DS is the primary owner; For ACE, the Operational Excellence team as a Firefighter)

## Archived - SDO Data Steward or Data Owner

- Assessed and decision made ingestion is not needed, due to one of the following reasons: 

  - Existing data is available to solve requirement
  - Review with requester drove solution to another path
(B_DS is the back up)

## Rejected - Data Owner

- The Business Data Owner gained more information to drive decision it is not needed or wanted
(The S_DS can act as a Firefighter)

---

# Data Connections

Data Connection is the first step to data ingestion. It includes collection and aggregation of details related to Sources and Agents that would be required in-order to establish connection from Palantir to the relevant source system for data ingestion. Below are the recommended naming conventions to be followed.

## Agents

Naming Convention: agnt:`sector-name`-`sourcetype`-`sourcesystemname|alias|databasename`-`env[optional]`

Where,

- sector-name represents one of the data office like `hc, el, ls, mgf, global`

- source-type represents the type of the source like `oracle, sap, sftp, api, s3 etc`

- source-system-name represents either the physical source name, or an alias or db name which uniquely identify the source.

- env is optional represents the environment where the physical data resides like dev, test, val, prod etc.

Example:
```
agnt:hc-oracle-d44 

agnt:hc-sap-dcb 

agnt:ls-infa-deda-dev 

agnt:el-s3-bckt-1ury7yc4ydjf3 

agnt:mgf-api-weather.gov 
```
Additional details on agents can be found [here](https://wiki.merckgroup.com/confluence/display/DAP/Agents)

Note: Currently we use shared agents such as mcloud-agent, mcloud-agent-2, dev-agent etc. An agent can support connection between different sources and source types.

## Data Source
To make it easier to review the purpose of a data source as well as the underlying technology that has been used a data source should follow the naming convention below: `sector`-`name`-`is`-`sink`-`source`-`type`-`system`-`name`-`environment[optional]`

Where,

- **sector-name** is one of `hc, el, ls, mgf, global`

- **is-sink** indicates whether this source is used for data externalization. This is only added to sources that are used for outgoing connections and is always the constant `sink`.

- **source-type** represents the Foundry plugin used in this source,

- **system-name** is a string representing the source system. The system name string shouldn't be longer than 20 characters as a rule of thumb and shouldn't contain dashes/hyphens/minus signs (-). Note: in limited cases where the system name is the same as the source type (e.g. aera), this portion can be left out.

- **environment** is a string representing the environment in which the data resides like prod, dev, stage etc. env . Should
be used only to disambiguate between multiple environments for the same source system. I.e. if there are production and development environments, do append appropriate suffixes such as `-prod` and `-dev`. Conversely, if this information is redundant or there is only a single environment, omit the environment name.

You can use the following regular expression to check for compliance (Python named group syntax is being used):
```
^(?P<sector-name>(el|hc|ls|mgf|global))(?P<is-sink>-sink)?-(?P<source-type>[a-z][a-z0-9]*)-(?P<system-name>[^-]+)(-(?P<environment>.+))?

```

In order to have a trade-off between stating full magritte plugin names and succintness, use the following mapping table to determine source types:

| **Source Type**|**Magritte Plugin**|
|:--------------------------------------------------------------------|:---------------|
|jdbc  | JDBC
|sap  | magritte-sap-source
|osipi  | osisoft-pi-web-connector
|rest| magritte-rest-v2
|ftp|FTP / FTPS
|sftp|magritte-sftp
|s3|s3
|sap|sap-connector

Examples:
- `hc-aera`
- `mgf-rest-trackwise-eq`
- `el-jdbc-alice-prod`
- `el-sink-s3-athinia`

## SAP Systems

Naming for SAP systems warrants an extra explanation as there is a substantial complexity in how they are set up and it is not obvious how to comply with the above rules.

*Sector name* and *source type* are analogous to the other sources: Shared connections start with the `global` sector name, whereas sector specific connections start with the relevant abbreviation. In case the sap-connector is used that connects to the NetWeaver component of an SAP installation, the source type is `sap`. If a connection to a Hana database is established `jdbc` is used.

The *system name* is determined by the overarching name of the SAP instance. E.g., `lean`, `quattro`, `next`, `tempoeu`, or `emerald`. This name is also used for "bolton" components that are specific to the ERP instance. E.g. the LEAN GTS component only gets the system name `lean` and *not* `lean_gts`. Disambiguation in these cases is done via the environment tag. For SAP components that are not part of a larger installation, but may rather be shared instances, the name of the component is used. For example, the global MDG system simply has the system name `mdg`.

Finally, the *environment* is the technical system identifier to which the connection is being established. E.g. `P01` for the Tempo EU production system. In case connections to more than one SAP client number are required, this number is added as a suffix to the name: `hc-sap-lean-dla-100` and `hc-sap-lean-dla-300`.

The reason for this naming scheme is to:

- Reflect the necessary technical information to uniquely identify a connection using the environment.
- Quickly filter down to a group of connections belonging to the same SAP system.
- Make the sometimes opaque technical names (P75 vs. P80) less prone to mix-ups.

## TODO
- How to indicate SAP Clients? See proposal above
- What about the AIM platform? <sector>-sap-aim-?cb, or rather el-sap-quattrobi-pcb / mgf-sap-mc4f-pcb?

Examples
- `hc-sap-lean-pla` (main LEAN production instance)
- `hc-sap-lean-ple` (LEAN GTS production instance)
- `global-sap-mdg-qcm` (MDG quality instance)
- `el-sap-quattro-qp1` (main Quattro production instance)
- `el-sap-s4-ht3` (Versum S4 test instance #3)
- `hc-sap-lean-dla-300` (LEAN development instance, client number 300)

Additional details on Data Source can be found [here](https://wiki.merckgroup.com/confluence/display/DAP/Inbound+Interface+Governance#:~:text=Foundry%20Sources/Syncs-,Data%20Connection%20Sources,-When%20a%20user)

## Data Sync
Naming Convention: `sub-source-system/dataset-name/report-name`

Syncs can have any name as long as the name differentiates the sync from the other syncs under the same Source.

Example:
```

ever-wf-capa-action, 

in-market-sales, 

customer-data 
```

For some source types such as SharePoint, SFTP, etc. We might need to create service users (S-MUID) to ingest data from these sources. In some cases S-MUID will also be used to schedule jobs. Please refer to the document for S-MUID creation [here](https://wiki.merckgroup.com/confluence/display/DAP/Service+User+Creation). For additional details on Agents, Sources and Syncs please refer to the [link](https://wiki.merckgroup.com/confluence/display/DAP/Inbound+Interface+Governance).

## Merck Proxy
Whenever a data source connection connects to an internet-based source system, the Merck Proxy needs to be used. REST APIs of cloud systems (e.g. SaaS) or external data providers are prominent examples of such internet based systems.


Below are some of Merck Proxies used and their purpose.

| **Proxy**|**Purpose**|
|:--------------------------------------------------------------------|:---------------|
| http://wsaproxy.eu.merckgroup.com:8080 | New Merck Proxy, to be used by default
| http://proxy.eu.merckgroup.com:8080  | Deprecated proxy, will be shutdown by IT at some point

Example

```
url: 'http://wsaproxy.eu.merckgroup.com:8080' 

username: ONE\SVC-{S-userid} e.g. ONE\SVC-S119250  

password: '{{password}}' 

```

## Outbound Interfaces

Please refer to [Data Externalization](https://palantir.mcloud.merckgroup.com/workspace/documentation/product/engineering-guidelines-staging/howto_data_externalization_requests).

# Data Treasury Price Tag

### Introduction
DTI Price tag is part of the Cost Transparency initiative and aims to complement the main development in this line, the Use Case price tag. The objective of this development is to capture the cost of most Foundry projects that are not included in the Use Case price tag and help data owners get insights on the cost of their ingestion and processing pipelines. 

DTI price tags cover only Foundry Costs, DTI is a concept inherent to Foundry. For a given DTI, we display the cost of the ontology project where the core dataset lives. Additionally, if there are other projects in the pipeline (data-source and transform) following the same name convention as the ontology one, they are also considered for the cost calculations.

### Overview of DTI Price Tag Feature
![detailedoverview](/assets/data-treasury-price/DTI price_tag Overview.png)
In the DTI Overview page, a tag is displayed, indicating the cost of that DTI in Foundry for the latest full month we have data for (please take in mind that data gets updated monthly, and that it might take a couple of days to have it ready once the month is ended). By clicking on the tag, a detailed view of the costs and its evolution through time is showed.

### Detailed Overlay Information
![overlay](/assets/data-treasury-price/DTI-overview.png)
The DTI price tag details overlay consists of three sections detailed below

### Overview
![overview](/assets/data-treasury-price/dti-detailed-overview.png)
This section displays the total cost by month for this DTI. We have a radio button allowing the user to select the currency they want to show the data (EUR or USD), and a selector of how many months in the past we want to be displayed (if we input a bigger number than number of months than the ones we have data for, all available data will be displayed).
The height of the bars corresponds to the total Foundry cost in the selected currency for that month in the ontology project for the DTI and the data-source and transform ones in case they are considered.
Users have the option to segment the bars by other variables, and see the specific amount of the total cost of each month that goes to each category:
-	Project Type: segment by cost of ontology, transform and data-source projects.
-	Cost Category: segment by category of the costs: compute, storage or ontology.
-	Foundry Service: segment by the specific Foundry service generating the costs (this is one level more granular than the cost category segmentation).

### Foundry Service Cost
![servicecost](/assets/data-treasury-price/dti-service-cost.png)
This tab shows the distribution of costs for a chosen month and dimension. Users can choose the currency (USD or EUR) in which they want the data to be displayed, and the month the data will refer to. There are four different dimensions they can choose: cost category, Foundry service, project name and project type. For each of them, a graph gets displayed with the cost amount for each specific value in the dimension for the chosen month.
"Cost Category" and "Foundry Service" allow you to understand which Foundry services and applications have the higher or lower costs, while "Project Name" and "Project Type "ones provide insights how costs are distributed across the different stages of the ingestion pipeline. Please note that only DTI specific projects are considered for transform and data-source. General ingestion and transform projects that end up in more than one DTI are not yet considered.

### DTI Cost Segment
![costsegment](/assets/data-treasury-price/dti-cost-segment.png)
This tab allows users to select one month and see a comparison of the current DTI's costs against other DTIs in the platform. DTIs are partitioned into several categories depending on the total cost segment for the selected month. The graph displays a histogram with all the DTIs in that segment, highlighting the one the current DTI belongs to. With this, DTI owners can understand if the consumption of its DTI is high or low, and in case of high costs they can go to other tabs and see why these costs are that high (identify parts of the pipeline or services consuming the most).

### Conclusion
The DTI Price tag feature is the perfect complement for Use Case Proce tag. It gives transparency on how much it costs to ingest and make available the data we are using in Use Cases and helps identifying pain points in the ingestion implementations that can be growing the platform costs.

## Browse this section to learn about Advanced Data Ingestion topics in UPTIMIZE Foundry.

# Health Checks & Monitoring

### Mandatory Health Checks:

This section addresses the health checks that the team has identified as the Global Standard for all datasets across Data Treasury datasets.

Below is the minimal set of checks to be configured for all datasets. Only those `highlighted below` are currently considered as **Global** and **recommended** standard checks.
The others can be applied as the Data Engineer and feel needed.

| **Category**    |**Health Check**|
|:--------------------------------------------------------------------|:---------------|
| Status | `Build status` A collection of the status of all jobs contained while ingestion/ transformation. Use of build status alerts the data engineers and data stewards of a failure in the pipeline.
| Time  | `Time since last updated`The time since the last successful build happened. Configure this to match the schedule upstream for Raw datasets (e.g., if a data-set updates on daily then this health-check should reflect this)

### Optional Health Checks:

These checks are Optional as needed, not applicable to all datasets and are to be determined by the Data Steward and Business Data Steward. Please apply these health checks wherever possible to monitor data health to the best possible.

| **Category**    |**Health Check**|
|:--------------------------------------------------------------------|:---------------|
| Time | **Data Freshness -** Compares the latest transaction on a dataset against the maximum value of a timestamp column.<br><br>**Dependency -** Only applicable in cases where columns that represent a Create_Date Or update_date are available.<br><br>**Build duration -** Build duration is the time taken for the completion of the transform/ingest. This should be configured based on reference build durations available on the history of builds.
| Content  | **Primary key -** If you know the dataset has a primary key that is supposed to be unique, set this check. This check will also trigger on any NULL values within this column.<br><br>**Dependency -** Only for datasets with unique keys.<br><br>**Null percentage -** Set this on columns that contain critical data, e.g. we should set this on columns that contain territory codes, ship-to clusters, amounts which are being aggregated by dashboard users.<br><br>**Dependency -** Only for very specific columns
| Size| **Row count -** The rules for row count depend on the nature of the dataset. Hard rules shall be defined (e.g., row count always must be above the previous count) that refresh meaningful patterns of the regular dataset.
|Schema|**Schema -** Set this on any parsed dataset to monitor any changes in columns (e.g., removed or added) and data types (e.g., Date > String)

Beyond this, there are more nuanced Content health-checks that may be suitable to your dataset. Make sure you are watching the dataset so that you can be notified when a health check fails.

### Best Practices to configure Global Health Checks:

Here are the set of general guidelines as best practices on how to configure the mandatory health checks. Depending on the dataset and the business requirements, these may be adjusted by the Data ingestion Engineer or Data Steward.

| **Category**    |**Health Check**|
|:--------------------------------------------------------------------|:---------------|
| Status |**Build status**<br><br>This HC should escalate to critical after a certain number of failures. The rule for the number of consecutive failures shall be dependent on the update schedule of the pipeline:<br><br>**- Daily:** Create a critical issue after 3 consecutive failures<br><br>**- Weekly/Monthly:** Create a critical issue after 1 consecutive failure 
| Time  | **Time since last updated**<br><br>Configure this HC to match the corresponding update frequency of the pipeline, by looking at the schedules defined at the Raw level. Define thresholds by editing the severity for `Moderate` and `Critical` failures, which will be dependent on the update frequency of the pipeline. Make sure to ignore empty transactions.<br><br>**Build Duration**Use the initial build as your first rule to set up the definition. This check is more a performance than a health check and can be refined over time. It will allow us to sensor historically how long builds have taken to complete and identify performance issues.
| Size| **Row count -**The correct set-up for this HC depends on the individual dataset. Check the following options in their order:<br><br>**- Option 1:** In the cases where data should only be growing (e.g. Master Data tables), check the result to always be equal to or greater than the previous successful result. Use the plus/minus functionality to set a meaningful value for tolerance if needed. <br><br>**- Option 2:** If Option 1 is not applicable, understand if hard-set thresholds can be defined. Set thresholds to define extreme scenarios, such as Row count "is less than or equal to 1" to understand if datasets contain of empty records.
|Schema|**Schema -**<br><br>Set up schema checks only on parsed datasets (do not implement them for Raw datasets that are still delimited). This check will apply across all columns and their data types. There are four different schema check types available, choose the most appropriate one applicable. The fourth one is to be the default setting. This should always create an issue:<br><br>**EXACT_MATCH_ORDERED_COLUMNS:** This will flag failures if any column order, column names or data types are changing.<br><br>**EXACT_MATCH_UNORDERED_COLUMNS:** This will flag failures if any column names or data types are changing, will ignore column order.<br><br>**COLUMN_ADDITIONS_ALLOWED:** This will flag failures if any column names or data types are changing. New columns are allowed, but columns from the original rule set up can not be missing.<br><br>**COLUMN_ADDITIONS_ALLOWED_STRICT (default):** Similar to `COLUMN_ADDITIONS_ALLOWED` but will always add new columns to the HC going forward - whenever a column was added, it cannot be missing going forward.

---

# Secure Data Ingestion

### Secure Data Ingestion

This section addresses the required steps to assure a secure data ingestion.

For general recommendations, please check the Foundry documentation:

- [Securing a Data Foundation](https://palantir.mcloud.merckgroup.com/docs/foundry/security/securing-a-data-foundation/)
- [Permission best practices for Data Connections](https://palantir.mcloud.merckgroup.com/docs/foundry/data-connection/permissions/#best-practices)
  - -> *Option 2: Place each Agent in its own Project*. shall be used

Additionally, the following aspects shall be checked:

#### Agents

- Agents shall be placed in an appropriate network location and zone. Since agents don't store data permanently and rather act as application server for data movement, they can be placed in the internal network zone, even when connecting to data sources and DBs in the confidential network zone. However, they shall not be place in public network zone or de-militarized zone.
- In general, all guidance as per the Merck IT/OT Security standard (Mango ID 20419427) and data center zoning annex (Mango ID 20185748) shall be followed.

#### Sources

- For data sources, connections from the data connection agent to the source systems and DBs shall encrypted by default, if possible. For JDBC, details for how to configure this should be specified in the documentation of the respective JDBC driver. For REST API sources, HTTPS shall be used.

---

# Data Externalization

Data and logic in Foundry are portable to third party and external applications in different ways using data replications processes. The technical options to choose depends on technical and functional conditions of the dataset or the usecase in foundry.

The technical options are used depending on technical and functional conditions such as

 1. the use case
 2. the way the third party and external applications are able to access Foundry
 3. online or offline access on the data (query data in real time vs. export/import)
 4. size and update frequency of the data

## Platform Manifesto for Outbound

1. Use Case is the source for the data
2. Pull over Push - external applications need to pull the data as we don't want to tightly couple Foundry to external applications
3. Access on Foundry to be established by the external application
4. Merck Data Security & Governance regulations need to be applied on the external applications
5. Data Owner need to approve export to external application

This section explains in detail about the below topics:

1. [Architecture Overview](https://palantir.mcloud.merckgroup.com/workspace/documentation/product/engineering-guidelines/howto_data_externalization_architecture_overview)
2. [Connection Types](https://palantir.mcloud.merckgroup.com/workspace/documentation/product/engineering-guidelines/howto_data_externalization_connection_types)
3. [Process](https://palantir.mcloud.merckgroup.com/workspace/documentation/product/engineering-guidelines/howto_data_externalization_process)
4. [Approver Groups](https://palantir.mcloud.merckgroup.com/workspace/documentation/product/engineering-guidelines/howto_dxr_approver_groups)

---

# Architecture Overview
[DXR Form](https://palantir.mcloud.merckgroup.com/workspace/module/view/latest/ri.workshop.main.module.4979a13c-ab89-42b8-be9b-30916a06a6dd) - This form allows you to `create an externalization request` for a Foundry Use Case with datasets that you want to use in an external third-party application. Only the Owners of a Use Case in the status **Proof of Value Development** or **Industrialization** can request an externalization. The responsible team of the Sector Data Office will be notified of your submission. A request is needed to decide about the creation of a firewall whitelist for non-Merck systems that otherwise cannot access Foundry. For this, the responsible persons performing the changes on the outbound interfaces will be notified.

![Architecture](https://docs.uptimize.merckgroup.com/docs-assets/foundry/Foundry/Data_Externalization/Architecture_Overview/dxr_architecture.png)

# Connection Types

## Cross System Connection

Merck's Palantir Foundry stack is hosted in the AWS region eu-central-1 in the the Palantir Cloud (PCloud). In order to connect from any external application to the Pcloud endpoint the following needs to be considered:

- Cloud to PCloud If you try to connect another Cloud based system to PCloud please provide the IP addresses to the SDO/MDO approvers, as the IP need to be allowlisted in order to allow the access. The allowlist is maintained in on [Foundry](https://palantir.mcloud.merckgroup.com/workspace/data-integration/code/repos/ri.stemma.main.repository.ba507d68-92fd-4648-acd6-338562a7a4e4/contents/refs%2Fheads%2Fmaster/transforms-python/src/myproject/datasets/final_allow_list.py) and IPs are only added if a Security Assessment of the external system is completed.

- Merck to PCloud If your system is an internal Merck system on-premise or in the data center extension (mCloud):

  - Check if your server or application can reach [Palantir](https://palantir.mcloud.merckgroup.com/) by opening a browser. In case its not working,
  - Check any Firewall blocks with the IT -> Open a Firewall request with IT

  ## Available Interfaces
Provided below are the different types of interfaces, that can be used based on the requirement of the usecase:

1. ODBC/JDBC Connector
2. Data Connection Export Plugin
3. Foundry SFDC connector
4. Data Proxy Query API
5. Data Proxy Datasets API
6. Phonograph2 API
7. Ontology API

## Authentication
We strongly encourage you to go through the [Authentication documentation](https://www.palantir.com/docs/foundry/api/general/overview/authentication/) to understand Foundry APIs authentication scheme.

Irrespective of which Interface you use to connect to Foundry:

For productive integrations, request a third party application for your use case via Foundry Issue. Do not use a personal Foundry token.

## SDKs / Libraries

For Python access the best option is to use [foundry_local](https://palantir.mcloud.merckgroup.com/workspace/data-integration/code/repos/ri.stemma.main.repository.45d3dd73-0efa-4459-a50b-04d8d9eb79ea/contents/refs%2Fheads%2Fmaster), a library developed at Merck. [Here](https://docs.uptimize.merckgroup.com/lab/data/how-to-read-and-write-data/) is a good high level usage documentation of foundry_local.

## ODBC/JDBC Connector:

**Description:**

- Palantir offers ODBC and JDBC drivers for connecting to Palantir Foundry with client applications.
- Those drivers can be used for any application supports those protocols for ex. BI tools like Tableau or Qlik.

## Documentation:

- [SQL Connectitivity & BI Tools integration](https://www.palantir.com/docs/foundry/analytics-connectivity/overview)
- [ODBC & JDBC Driver details and download](https://www.palantir.com/docs/foundry/analytics-connectivity/odbc-jdbc-drivers/#overview)
- [Connecting Tableau to Foundry Video](https://mdigital.sharepoint.com/sites/Tableau_Knowledge_Base/SitePages/Data%20-%20Foundry.aspx)

## Usecase :

- Query tabular data
- Mainly used to connect BI tools on Foundry for data visualization/analytics, but also to query datasets for external applications
- Best support for "SELECT * FROM" queries (Direct read in Arrow Format offers fast performance)

## Limits/Considerations:

- OFFSET and FETCH not supported, not fully SQL Standard compatible
- Beside Tableau, all installation and configuration need to be done by end-user
- Tableau: SSO via Oauth will be rolled out soon, once necessary Tableau server version is updated.

## Install the driver

- Foundry ODBC driver is now published as a Featured App on Merck Software Center, and is available for Windows users as convenient self-serve installation.

![Featured](https://docs.uptimize.merckgroup.com/docs-assets/foundry/Foundry/Data_Externalization/connection_types/odbc_featured_app.png)

- In order to enable secure and seamless user experience and to avoid manually generating and entering Foundry tokens, an OAuth client ID is already pre-configured as a property in the driver.
```
    - authMethod = OauthFlow
    - oauthClientId = <PRE-CONFIGURED CLIEND ID>
```

![Pre Configuration](https://docs.uptimize.merckgroup.com/docs-assets/foundry/Foundry/Data_Externalization/connection_types/odbc_pre_configuration.png)

**Checklist for JDBC Connectior:**

- Ensure you read the documentation - download the files and place the files in your server/client - create a token in Foundry user settings for creating an initial connection PoC.
- Replace in the jdbc url with the token you generated - Configure [OAuth](https://palantir.mcloud.merckgroup.com/docs/foundry/analytics-connectivity/odbc-jdbc-drivers/#usage-guides) for productive integrations (see chapter Athentication above). Check also that you have a valid token as the token has an expire date. **For productive usage, use a third party application**.
- Check if you can reach the Foundry endpoint (https://palantir.mcloud.merckgroup.com) from your server/client.
- The connection string format is different between ODBC and JDBC, but the [parameters](https://palantir.mcloud.merckgroup.com/docs/foundry/analytics-connectivity/odbc-jdbc-drivers/#usage-guides) you can specify are the same. The formats are:
   - ODBC - Driver=FoundrySqlDriver;baseUrl=<FOUNDRY_URL>;pwd=<YOUR_TOKEN>;optionalParamOne=ABC;optionalParamTwo=XYZ
   - JDBC - jdbc:foundrysql://<FOUNDRY_URL>?password=<YOUR_TOKEN>&optionalParamOne=ABC&optionalParamOne=XYZ
   - Some JDBC clients may ask for the driver class to be specified explicitly. The implementation class is com.palantir.foundry.sql.jdbc.FoundryJdbcDriver
- You can test the connector by querying an public sample dataset (`dialect=SPARK`):

```
SELECT * FROM `/Global/Foundry Training/Examples/Slate/Tutorials and References/Tutorials/Getting Started Data/Asteriods` LIMIT 10
```

If you have selected `dialect=ANSI` you can use:
```
SELECT * FROM "/Global/Foundry Training/Examples/Slate/Tutorials and References/Tutorials/Getting Started Data/Asteriods" LIMIT 10
```
- For querying a dataset, you need to reference the dataset by its Foundry path or RID like
```
SELECT * FROM "<REPLACE_WITH_FOUNDRY_DATASET_PATH>"
```

or
```
SELECT * FROM "<REPLACE_WITH_FOUNDRY_RID>"
```
## Data Connection Export Plugin:
### Description:

- The export task plugin allows exporting data from Foundry to various external data sources like (FileSystem on the agent, SFTP, S3, ABFS, HDFS, JDBC)
- An export task can be scheduled with the Foundry scheduler based on events such as "parent dataset updated"

### Documentation:

- [Export Task](https://palantir.mcloud.merckgroup.com/docs/foundry/data-connection/export-tasks)

### Usecase :

- Export of data for further consumption of other processes
- Scheduled as part of pipeline run

### Limits/Considerations:

- Centrally governed by MDO/SDOs, eeds to be approved by governance teams before use
- External system needs to be configured and network reachable
- Only export to Merck network targets possible (or proxy required)
- JDBC by default not standard - needs to be evaluated and approved

## Foundry SFDC connector:

### Description:

- The SFDC connector supports both ingestions from SFDC to Foundry and writeback from Foundry to SFDC via Webhooks.
- The writeback option is currently not enabled for Merck as shown below:

![Connector](https://docs.uptimize.merckgroup.com/docs-assets/foundry/Foundry/Data_Externalization/connection_types/dxr_sfdc_connector.png)



### Documentation:

- [Foundry SFDC Connector demo video summarizing its capabilities](https://view.highspot.com/viewer/601028046a3b1130ba8cc1a5)

### Usecase :

- Update objects in SFDC like Lead, Opportunity, Status of an Order or Customer value

### Limits/Considerations:

- Write back needs additional effort and approval and we recommend it only updating single objects in SFDC like status of an customer or an workflow

## Making API Calls:

### Description:

- Foundry is providing different kind of API's for different purposes.
- [Here](https://palantir.mcloud.merckgroup.com/docs/foundry/api/general/overview/introduction) is an good overview about how to do the basics you need to begin developing against Foundry, including the [URL base for API calls](https://palantir.mcloud.merckgroup.com/docs/foundry/api/general/overview/introduction/), various [authorization considerations](https://palantir.mcloud.merckgroup.com/docs/foundry/api/general/overview/authentication), and a few [examples](https://palantir.mcloud.merckgroup.com/docs/foundry/api/general/overview/getting-started) you can start with:

API call examples using curl from the command line. Expose the foundry token as environment variable:
```
TOKEN=eyJwbG50...
```

Data Proxy SQL Query:

```
curl 'https://palantir.mcloud.merckgroup.com/foundry-data-proxy/api/dataproxy/query?defaultBranchId=master&dialect=ansi' \
-H "authorization: Bearer $TOKEN" \
-H 'content-type: application/json' \
--data-binary '{"query":"SELECT name FROM (SELECT * FROM \"/Global/Foundry Training/Data/Derived/meteor/meteor_duplicate\") as t LIMIT 500"}' \
--compressed
```

Compass getRessource to get structure of an folder:

```
curl --location --request GET 'https://palantir.mcloud.merckgroup.com/compass/api/resources/ri.compass.main.folder.87710242-62b8-4604-a12f-88594031d47d' \
--header "authorization: Bearer $TOKEN" \
--header 'content-type: application/json'
```

## Data Proxy API:
**Description:**

- The DataProxy supports reading and writing single files as well as querying datasets with a FoundrySchema via SparkSQL.
- It can also be used to download files directly. Downloading files directly would first require that you retrieve the list of files in the dataset's view, for which you can use the **Catalog API**.

### Documentation:

- Data Proxy API usage guide
- Data PRoxy API docs
- Catalog API

### Usecase :

- Direct query access on data esp. for smaller queries with fast performance (query API)
- Download files in a dataset directly for downstream processing.

### Limits/Considerations:

- Data proxy Query API is not guaranteed to scale well. So, for larger results (>10MM rows), you may start seeing instability, timeouts or failed calls.
- Data proxy Dataset API requires user to download complete dataset and process offline for filtering etc.

## Phonograph2 API:
### Description:

- Phonograph2 is a service that allows near real-time CRUD and search operations on rows of Foundry Datasets through its API. With higher latency, an output writeback Dataset representing the edited version of the original Dataset can be built to be consumed by other Foundry Platform services, like Contour and Authoring.
- Data can be synced Phonograph and queries run against elastic search which provide a stable and fast query execution.
- Phonograph2 can be used for writebacks of data into Foundry
- The Ontology API with underlying object storage service v2 is the successor of the phonograph2 API. There is a risk that the phonograph2 API will be deprecated.

### Documentation:

- [Phonograph2 / Object API](https://www.palantir.com/docs/foundry/api/ontology-resources/objects/object-basics)

### Usecase :

- Direct query access on datasets synced to phonograph2 with consistant performance
- Query patterns that can benefit from elasticsearch query patterns.
- Writeback into Foundry for further processing as dataset

### Limits/Considerations:

- Syncing datasets to phonograph2 increases cost for storage 10x times compared to the dataset storage.
- phonograph2 API has a stable and fast performance vs. the Data Proxy API on small but also larger query sets,
- Each query is limited to 10k rows, therefore not recommended for big datasets.
- The data needs to be synced before using it.

### Phonograph2 to get all rows from an table :

```
curl --location --request POST 'https://palantir.mcloud.merckgroup.com/phonograph2/api/search/tables' \
--header "authorization: Bearer $TOKEN" \
--header 'content-type: application/json' \
-d '{"tableRids":["ri.phonograph2.main.table.0bfad3dd-94cd-4a9f-b954-3be1852dce85"],"filter":{"type":"matchAll","matchAll":{}},"sort":[{"ds_name.raw":{"order":"asc"}},{"checkName.raw":{"order":"asc"}}]}'
```
## Ontology API:

### Description:

- New-ish API to query everything related to the ontology layer in Foundry.
- Part of the new Palantir API.
- Allows to perform CRUD operations in the ontolgoy through calling Actions.
- Only data available in the ontology layer accessible.

### Documentation:

- [Ontology API](https://www.palantir.com/docs/foundry/api/ontology-resources/ontology/ontology-basics/)

### Usecase :

- Direct query access on datasets synced to phonograph2 with consistant performance
- Query patterns that can benefit from elasticsearch query patterns.
- Writeback into Foundry for further processing as dataset

### Limits/Considerations:

- Syncing datasets to ontology increases cost for storage 10x times compared to the dataset storage.
- ontology API has a stable and fast performance vs. the Data Proxy API on small but also larger query sets.
- Not much experience within Merck to use this API.
- The data needs to be synced before using it.

**Ontology API call to list objects (limited to 1 object) :**

```
curl \
--header "Authorization: Bearer $TOKEN" \
"https://palantir.mcloud.merckgroup.com/api/v1/ontologies/ri.ontology.main.ontology.00000000-0000-0000-0000-000000000000/objects/Merckemployee?pageSize=1"
```

## Connector Comparisons:

Provided below is the comparison of pros and cons of the various connector options :


| Connector Options| Usecase  | Pros     | Cons     |
| :---             | :---     | :---     | :---     |
| ODBC/JDBC Connector  | 1. Analytics - Tableau or other analytics/data querying tool to connect to Foundry data.<br> <br> 2. Any 3rd Party applications that support ODBC/JDBC driver  | 1. Native Connectors <br> <br> 2. Easy to use for PULL <br>  <br> 3. Tableau Foundry by Palantir connector optimized for Tableau Usage  | 1. Only for tabular data <br> <br>  2. Technical Knowledge required for installation/configuration                                  
| Data Proxy Query API | Query datasets with basic Spark SQL syntax | 1. Direct Access with one simple REST API call<br> <br>   2. Fast for small queries<br> <br> 3. Possibility to filter down data| 1. No query performance guarantee as running on SPARK <br> <br> 2.  timeout for complex queries
| Data Proxy Datasets API | Upload / Download files of datasets | 1. Direct Access with REST API<br> <br>  2. Full Data Export via Catalog API file listing | 1. Need to download whole dataset and query offline 
| Data Connection Export Plugin | Export data - Export to S3, HDFS, SFTP (or JDBC targets - only on request) | 1. Standard Foundry-way to export datasets <br> <br>  2. Exports in underlying dataset format (usually parquet) <br> <br> 3. Can be scheduled as part of pipeline   | 1. Tightly coupling of Foundry to external system <br> <br> 2. Export can be slow and additional step <br> <br> 3. Only export to Merck network targets possible or proxy required <br> <br> 4. Dependency on central team to maintain |
| Foundry SFDC connector | Update data - Webhook API for update single objects | Official way forward from Palantir | 1. Only applies to Foundry Actions  <br> <br> 2. Only applies to special systems like SFDC <br> <br> 3. Not designed to insert data <br> <br> 4. Still new|
| Phonograph2 API | Insert / Update data - Communicating with the phonograph directly on elastic search for queries | 1. Sync directly to Phonograph  <br> <br> 2. Customized response <br> <br> 3. Fast update of objects <br> <br> 4. Consistent query performance| 1. Pagination for results with more than 10k rows <br> <br> 2. Customized response needs to build in objects before <br> <br> 3. Duplicate data in elasticsearch, high costs |
| Ontology API | CRUD calls on Ontology   | 1. Easy access to Ontology data  <br> <br> 2. Official way forward from Palantir <br> <br> 3. Fast update of objects <br> <br> 4. Consistent query guarantees | 1. Pagination for results with more than 10k rows  <br> <br>  2. Duplicate data in object storage service, high costs|



There are already some successful established connections to Qlik (ODBC), DBVisualizer (JDBC), PowerBI, Tableau and Tableau Prep, EasyMorph (ODBC).

Provided below are some 3rd party support documents beside the general overview.

- [KNIME Connection](https://wiki.merckgroup.com/confluence/display/AKB/Interfaces?preview=/276530053/276530930/KNIME%20Connection.docx)
- [DBeaver Connection](https://wiki.merckgroup.com/confluence/display/AKB/Interfaces?preview=/276530053/276530929/DBeaver%20Connection.docx)
- [XLS Connection](https://wiki.merckgroup.com/confluence/display/AKB/Interfaces?preview=/276530053/276530928/XLS%20Connection.docx)

# Process

This section provides details on the data Externalization process in Foundry.

## Operational Process:

1. User clicks on the yellow `Request data export` button from the Overview tab of the Use Case Object view.

![Data Export](https://docs.uptimize.merckgroup.com/docs-assets/foundry/Foundry/Data_Externalization/Process/Request_data_export.png)

2. User fills the DXR Form.

3. A new object is created. The sector of the DXR is obtained from the sector of the Use Case that is linked to the DXR.

4. The members of the approver group of the sector are notified.

5. The Approvers are responsible for processing the request according to the process in place *(TODO link to the process when it's finalized)*

6. If the request is approved or rejected:

   - The approver has to press the Approve or Reject button in the DXR's Object View.

![Status](https://docs.uptimize.merckgroup.com/docs-assets/foundry/Foundry/Data_Externalization/Process/Request_status.png)

   - This updates the status of the DXR and notifies the user who created the DXR.

7. If the request is lacking some crucial information that would help the Approvers in understanding the purpose of the externalizations:
   - The approver has to press the Request more info button in the DXR's Object View and let the user know what's missing in the Comments sections of the Form that pops up


![Info](https://docs.uptimize.merckgroup.com/docs-assets/foundry/Foundry/Data_Externalization/Process/Request_info.png)


   - This updates the status of the DXR and notifies the user who created the DXR.

   - The user then has to go to the object view and click on the **Modify** button which will allow them to modify some properties of the request.

8. If for some reason the DXR needs to be deleted (e.g. it was a test request) a member of the `dxr-admins group` can delete it via the **Delete** or the **Bulk delete** actions.

---

<img src="https://docs.uptimize.merckgroup.com/docs-assets/snowflake/accelerator/fast_snowflake.png" style="float: left;" width="150"/>

# Welcome to the dashboarding Accelerator
Data Lake technology is optimized for collecting raw or unrefined data captured from diverse array of sources to support a range of different processing styles and approaches, including machine learning and batch-oriented workloads. Data Lakes aren't typically optimized for performance especially for end user reports provided by Tableau or PowerBI accessing data in the data lake.

To meet the increasing performance requirements and to deliver a modern data infrastructure to enable analytics use cases with high end reporting we created the Accelerator, an in-house solution leveraging SNOWFLAKE for fast dashboarding applications. 

## When to use the Accelerator

Every time you need speed on live connections on UPTIMIZE Foundry data with your external visualization tool like Tableau to boost the performance of the provided dashboards. 
 
See here some examples from Tableau where the Accelerator can help you: 
- Foundry by Palantir live connection is too slow esp. if you handle more than 1.5MM rows within a complex dashboard
- Tableau extract is not sufficient
    - Refresh time take too long (ex. 300MM rows will take more than the 2hrs limit on the Tableau Server)
    - Refresh schedule on the Tableau Server doesn't fit (ex. you don't know the exact time on refresh the data in Foundry)
- Data updated often during the day on different times and the Tableau extract can only be schedule once a day
- You have different datasets in Foundry on different level of granularity and can't create a joined dataset in Foundry as it will explode -the data

## Prerequisites
Here's the list of things you need to have to start using the accelerator
1. A Foundry use case, with at least one Foundry project linked to it.
2. A dataset located in a project of the Foundry use case
3. Owner permission on the Foundry use case

## Who to request a data export to the Accelerator

1. Go to your the use case portal, select your use case and click on ```more > request data export```

<img src="https://docs.uptimize.merckgroup.com/docs-assets/snowflake/accelerator/button_request_sync.png" alt="drawing" width="600"/>

2. Select the ```UPTIMIZE Snowflake``` option

<img src="https://docs.uptimize.merckgroup.com/docs-assets/snowflake/accelerator/button_export_snowflake.png" width="600"/>

3. copy-paste the **rid** of your dataset. Make sure the dataset is located in one of your snowflake's project. If the data you want to export is in another project, please make a copy of the dataset in your project and export the copy. 

<img src="https://docs.uptimize.merckgroup.com/docs-assets/snowflake/accelerator/forme_accelerator.png" width="600"/>

4. Briefly explain the reasons for this export and select the ```Sync to Accelerator``` option

5. Submit your request and you're all done !

6. After submitting, you will be redirected to the request, were you can track the approval status.

> **warning** Make sure your dataset has no special characters and no space in its name (except _ and -). 
> If you fail to do so, your sync request will not be processed and you will receive a notification e-mail inviting you to rename your dataset. Once you have renamed your dataset, an additional delay of 24h might occure for your request to be processed.

> **Notes**
> - After submitting, you will be redirected to the request, were you can track the approval status.
> - Once the request is created, you will receive an confirmation e-mail with a link to the Foundry request and a second e-mail once the request is approved.

## Data access
### Data access from MTableau

To access your data from Tableau, please refer to the [dedicated documentation](https://mdigital.sharepoint.com/sites/Tableau_Knowledge_Base/SitePages/Data-Snowflake.aspx?OR=Teams-HL&CT=1701782345163&clickparams=eyJBcHBOYW1lIjoiVGVhbXMtRGVza3RvcCIsIkFwcFZlcnNpb24iOiIyOC8yMzExMDIyNDcwNSIsIkhhc0ZlZGVyYXRlZFVzZXIiOmZhbHNlfQ%3D%3D).

## Data access from PowerBI

To access your data from PowerBI Server, you can refer to the [dedicated documentation](https://docs.uptimize.merckgroup.com/snowflake/data-consumption/dashboarding/power-bi/).
In addition, for the server name, you must use ```merckgroup-accelerator-nreg-all.snowflakecomputing.com```
and for the warehouse you must select one of the following option based on the sector in which your data belongs to:

* Life Science -> ```LS_DASHBOARDING_WH```
* Enabeling Functions -> ```EF_DASHBOARDING_WH```
* Health Care -> ```HC_DASHBOARDING_WH```
* Electronics -> ```EL_DASHBOARDING_WH```

## Permission management
On top of the access to the Tableau project, you must ensure that the viewers and contributors of the dashboard have access to the data.
To do this, simply make sure that the dashboard users and contributors have access to the dataset *on Foundry* and this will allow them to access to the same data on Snowflake.
When a person is granted or revoked permissions on the data in Foundry, the changes should be applied on the accelerator *within 2h*.

## Performance managment

Snowflake is fast enough so please don't consider creating an extract. In case of you experience any performance issue please reach out to the Snowflake support. 
There are still options on the Snowflake account to scale it up by providing a higher warehouse or spin up a multi-cluster.

## Deletion and pause of sync request

You can Pause or archive your sync request by editing the existing request form. 
Pausing the sync will cause the data to stay on the accelerator but not be synched with the Foundry dataset anymore.
Archiving the request will delete the data from the accelerator all together. 
To access your sync request form, you can use the link sent in the confirmation e-mail. Otherwise
you can access it from the Foundry ontology.

## Some things to be aware of

Here are a couple of restrictions/behaviours you should be aware of:
- Not all types of dataset names are supported. Make sure your dataset has no special characters in its name, except _ and - and white spaces. (```Table```, ```Table 2```, ```Table-3``` are allowed but not ```2Table%```)
- All column names supported by Foundry are allowed
- The accelerator will convert dashes (-) and white spaces to underscores (_) in the dataset name
- When the dataset is modified, you can expect the changes to be visible in the accelerator after 30 minutes
- You will find a link to your request form in the confirmation e-mail. This will be useful for editing your request form.
- If you want to sync 2 datasets with the same name and from the same project, their display name will append the first 5 characters of their RID to differentiate them (e.g ```SALES_DATA_34G6D9```)


# FAQ

### Who can I reach out to for support ?
For any support, please open a SNOW ticket on the service ```Snowflake``` and category ```Uptimize Snowflake```

### When will the data be available after posting my request ?
The export request will first require to be approved by the corresponding SDO. 
Once the request has been approved, the data will be ready to use within 2 hours.

### When I update my data in Foundry, how fast does it sync to the accelerator ?
Depending on the size of your data, we see updates lasting from 5 minutes (<2GB) to 30 minutes (>100GB). 
Those performances will also depend on various factors like network traffic, data partitionning, etc.

### I would like to also do some processing on Snowflake with my data, how can I do this ?
We also enable the export of Foundry datasets on Use Case Snowflake accounts. You can read all you need to know about it [here](https://docs.uptimize.merckgroup.com/snowflake/data-ingestion/data-ingestion-automated/foundry/).

---

# Data Provisioning

The documentation covers the new Data Provisioning 2.0 process, which replaces the old Data Provisioning process.

## Introduction

Data provisioning (DP) enables Business Data Owners/Stewards to grant users access to filtered subsets of a dataset, known as Slices. These Slices are created based on specific filtering dimensions such as country, plant code, and material product group SBU identifier.

For a use case requesting access to a dataset with Data Provisioning, the requestor will choose a pre-defined slice from the access request form.

Once the access request is approved by one of: Business Data Owner, Business Data Steward, Deputy Data Owners, Deputy Data Stewards, Slice Owner or Slice Steward, a filtered version of the dataset from the DTI (defined by the selected slice) is automatically provisioned into the use case project and scheduled according to the DTI schedule.

![High Level Process](https://docs.uptimize.merckgroup.com/docs-assets/foundry/Images/data-provisioning/HighLevelProcess.png)

The 4 steps are: 

1. Prerequisite for DTI Setup: The Data Provisioning property of the Data Treasury Item object has to be "Yes".
2. Slices may be created by either the Business Data Owner, Business Data Steward, Deputy Data Owners, Deputy Data Stewards, or the SDO Data Steward.
3. Every time a Use Case requests access to this DTI, the requestor of the DTI has to select the slice that should be provisioned to this Use Case.
4. An automated script is responsible for delivering the data to the project of the Use Case that requested access.

## BPMN Process

The BPMN process shows all the tasks and responsibilities if data provisioning is yes or no. It also describes what to do if there is no slice configuration.


![BPMN Process](https://docs.uptimize.merckgroup.com/docs-assets/foundry/Images/data-provisioning/240422_LJ_BPMN_Data_Provisioning_V2_Provision.png)

## What is a slice and who manages it?
 
 
1.	A slice is a filtered subset of the datasets contained within a DTI. 
2.	For each of the datasets within the DTI, filter conditions and dropped columns can be defined (dataset configuration).
3.	Slices can be managed by the Business Data Owner, Business Data Steward, Deputy Data Owners, Deputy Data Stewards, and the SDO Data Steward of the DTI.
4.	Ownership of a slice can be delegated to a dedicated Owner/Steward.
5.	Once nominated, slice Owner/Stewards can also manage access to their slices.



## How to review the slices available for a DTI? 

When accessing a DTI in the [Data Treasury](https://palantir.mcloud.merckgroup.com/workspace/module/view/latest/ri.workshop.main.module.10e9a51d-489e-4610-b6ce-e93a1bc66912) app, a Provisioning Slices tab is available for you to review the list of slices:


![Available Slice](https://docs.uptimize.merckgroup.com/docs-assets/foundry/Images/data-provisioning/HowtoFindAvailableSlices.png)

## Access Request for DTI with Data Provisioning

 
1.	When requesting access to a DTI with Data Provisioning, you will see a list of available slices in the dropdown list. Select the one you need. 
2.	Once you submit your access request, the approval workflow will start. 


 ![Request Access](https://docs.uptimize.merckgroup.com/docs-assets/foundry/Images/data-provisioning/requestaccess.png)


<ld-notice headline="What to do if no slice match your needs" mode="warning">
If no slice matches your needs, leave the slice selection empty and provide the details of the desired slice configuration in the reason field of the request form. 
The DTI Owner will review the request, create the desired slice and update the access request with the newly created slice.
</ld-notice>

## Result of the Data Provisioning into a Use Case project

>**Note** This section presents the default setup, please get in touch with your SDO for sector-specific customization. 

Once your access request has been approved by the slice owner, an automated script will run to provision the DTI slice into the use case project. 

By default, the provisioned datasets will land in the `data` folder of the project and will be named according to the following naming convention: 
 `DTI_NAME - Dataset_Name`.
 
![Result in use case](https://docs.uptimize.merckgroup.com/docs-assets/foundry/Images/data-provisioning/result_in_usecase.png)

- Health Checks are automatically set up
- Scheduling is automatically added based on the DTI Datasets refresh

The requestor, the DTI owner and the slice owner will be notified by email of the successful provisioning. 

## Multiple Slices Provisioning

If a use case requests multiple slices from the same DTI, the result in the use case project will be the union of the slices: 

>**Note** The union of slices will not happen if there is request with a slice that is provisioning full data. To get the full dataset, you will need to revoke the other requests having slices with filters. If not, the data will be union of the slices with filters.

<!---
![Result in use case](https://docs.uptimize.merckgroup.com/docs-assets/foundry/Images/data-provisioning/multislice.png)
-->
![Result in use case](/assets/data-provisioning/multislice_2.png)

## Cross Sector Data Provisioning

When a Use Case requests access to a Data Provisioning-enabled DTI from a different sector, as an Approver, you need to take one of the following actions to ensure the request does not get stuck due to missing permissions:

1. **Grant Access:** Reach out to your SDAO Admins to ensure the requestor sector TPA user is added to viewer group of DTI project.
2. **Reject the Request:** Reject the request and ask the user to create a Use Case in the same sector as your DTI and provision the data to that Use Case.

| Sector             | Data Provisioning TPA Name                |
|--------------------|--------------------------------------------|
| Life Science       | LS Data Provisioning 2.0               |
| Healthcare         | TPA-hc-hdd-data-provisioning            |
| Electronics        | TPA-EL-DO-Data Provisioning             |
| Enabling Functions | Group Functions Provisioning 2.0       |

# How to create a DTI slice
 
The Slice management application can be accessed from the Data Treasury using this [link](https://palantir.mcloud.merckgroup.com/workspace/module/view/latest/ri.workshop.main.module.10e9a51d-489e-4610-b6ce-e93a1bc66912/slice-management): 

![Slice Management](https://docs.uptimize.merckgroup.com/docs-assets/foundry/Images/data-provisioning/slice_management_1.png)

The steps to create a slice are: 

1. [Create a Slice](https://docs.uptimize.merckgroup.com/foundry/foundry-data/data-provisioning/slice-management/#creating-a-slice)
2. [Configure the datasets](https://docs.uptimize.merckgroup.com/foundry/foundry-data/data-provisioning/slice-management/#configuring-a-dataset-for-the-selected-slice)
3. [Activate the slice](https://docs.uptimize.merckgroup.com/foundry/foundry-data/data-provisioning/slice-management/#activating-a-slice)

## Creating a Slice

1.	On the left side of the application, you will see the list of DTIs for which you can configure slices. You can use the filtering options to narrow down the list.
2.	Once you have selected a DTI, you will see a list of slices that have already been configured for it.
3.	To create a slice, click on the 'Create Slice' button. You will be prompted to give the slice a name, description, and an owner. By default, the owner of the slice is the DTI owner, but this can be changed to any other employee.
4.	Once you have named the slice, it's status will be 'Configuration in Progress', which means you can start configuring the datasets within the DTI.
 
### Updating Slice Parameters

If you want to update the slice parameters, such as the name, description, or ownership, click on 'Update Slice Parameters' under the 'Manage Slice' menu and update the relevant fields.

<ld-notice headline="Data Governance for Slices" mode="warning"> 
When creating a slice, the Owner is, by default, the DTI Owner. Slice Ownership can optionally be transferred to any Merck employee. Additionally, a slice steward can also be defined.
</ld-notice>

Here is a summary of the permissions for the different roles: 
* Slice management: 
    *	The DTI owner and steward can manage all slices.
    *	The slice owner and steward can manage their slice only (optional).
*	DTI Access Request Approval: 
    *	The DTI owner and steward can approve all access requests.
    *	The slice Owner and Steward can approve access requests for their slices only (optional).</ld-notice>


## Configuring a Dataset for the Selected Slice




To start configuring the datasets, click on the 'Add Slice Dataset Configuration' button. 

![Slice Configuration 1](/assets/data-provisioning/slice_dataset_configuration_1.png)
![Slice Configuration 2](/assets/data-provisioning/slice_dataset_configuration_2.png)

1.	Select the dataset of interest in the drop-down list. (If you do not see any dataset entries, please refresh your browser.)
2.	Define the columns to be dropped by selecting them in the drop column box. If you don't define any columns, all columns of the dataset will be provisioned.
3.	You can also manage filters by defining a list of columns with associated values for the dataset to be filtered on within the slice. It is important to follow the specified spelling in order to ensure the readability of the configuration through code. If you don't define filter conditions, the dataset will be provisioned without filters.
4.	Set the Filter operation to Include/Exclude based on whether to include/exclude the filter values from the selected column to filter on. To set filter values, you can either select the values or manually enter the values in the form of a comma separated list like ["value 1", "value 2", ..."value N"]. Use the toggle button to select your preffered mode of entry. The manual option is particularly helpful in cases where -
      * The number of unique values for the column to be filtered on is greater than the limit of values that can be displayed in dropdown
      * The values to be included or excluded are not currently present in the data but can be present in the future
5.  You can also copy the configuration from one dataset to other datasets in the DTI. If you need to do so, one you have set the drop columns and filters, select "Yes" for "Do you want to copy this configuration to addtional datasets?" and select the dataset(s) you want to copy the configuration to before submitting.
6.	Once you have made your changes, click on 'Submit', the configured dataset will appear on the right pane. 
7.	If you want to configure additional datasets or override the configuration of a dataset that has already been configured, click again on the 'Add Slice Data Set Configuration' button. 
8.  If you want to be able to provision a dataset entirely, without any filters or drop columns, leave both fields empty and submit the action. Beware that this may expose sensitive information so this should be done with extreme care and consideration.


If you configure a dataset that has already been configured for this slice, your new configuration will replace the existing one. The older configuration will have the status "Inactive" and can be seen by selecting "All configurations" button in the right panel.

## Guidelines & Precautions
  - Configure all the datasets you would like to provision. Not configured datasets will not be provisioned.
  - If the filters being applied on the column(s) of first dataset is not present in any of the additional datasets, then the provisioning of these datasets will FAIL. Only copy the configuration after you have verified the presence of the column across all datasets being configured. If an improperly configured slice is provisioned, you need to unprovision all requests from this slice before setting the slice to "Inactive".
  - For all provisioning requests, do not move the provisioned datasets in the Use Case project folder until the ARO has reached "Done" status to let the automation complete. Moving the dataset before this will likely lead to missing schedules for the provisioned datasets.
  - For deletion of datasets, use the "Revoke" action to ensure all provisioned resources are cleaned up efficiently.


## Activating a Slice

1.	Once you have finished configuring the slice, you can move it to an 'Active' status by clicking on 'Activate Slice' under 'Manage Slice' menu.
> **Warning** After activating the slice, you cannot change the slice parameters (description or owner/steward) and cannot change it's configuration anymore!
2.	Once the slice is active, it becomes visible to end users in the DTI access request and can be chosen for provisioning.
 
>**Important Note** Only **Active** slices will be visible for the users to request access.

<ld-notice headline="Access Request without Slice: Create the Required Slice and Update the Access Request" mode="warning">
If you receive an access request without slice selected, you will not be able to approve it. Instead, review the reason for request field and create the required slice. Once the slice is active, modify the access request by selecting the newly created slice and proceed with the approval process.
</ld-notice>

---

# Slice Deactivation and Unprovisioning

To ensure data provisioning pipelines don't break, an Active slice **cannot** be deleted. 

- As DTI owner, if you want to prevent requests to a specific slice, you can [deactivate](https://docs.uptimize.merckgroup.com/foundry/foundry-data/data-provisioning/unprovisioning/#deactivating-a-slice) it.


- To stop the provisioning of an existing slice within an use case, the DTI owner can unprovision the slice per use case by [revoking the access request](https://docs.uptimize.merckgroup.com/foundry/foundry-data/data-provisioning/unprovisioning/#unprovisioning-process).


## Deactivating a Slice

1.	In the slice management application, select the active slice and click 'Deactivate' under the 'Manage Slice' menu.
2.	If you deactivate a slice, the slice will no longer be visible to users in the access request for the DTI.


>**Important Note #1**
>
>Please note that once a slice is deactivated, it cannot be reactivated.

>**Important Note #2**
>
>Deactivating a slice will **not** impact the already provisioned use cases for this slice.


## Unprovisioning Process

 If you want to unprovision a slice from a use case, simply revoke the corresponding access request. 

![Revoke AR](https://docs.uptimize.merckgroup.com/docs-assets/foundry/Images/data-provisioning/revokeAR.png)

 The automated script will remove the provisioning logic and the scheduling within the use case project. The requestor, the DTI owner and the slice owner will be notified by email of the successful unprovisioning.

<ld-notice headline="Datasets in use case projects are not deleted" mode="warning"> 
By default, the datasets within the use case are not deleted to not break potential downstream pipelines. This behavior can however be modified by the SDAO admins. Please reach out to your SDAO for more details.
</ld-notice>

---

# Monitoring 

Primary resource for monitoring is the Workshop App [Data Provisioning 2.0 - Status Log](https://palantir.mcloud.merckgroup.com/workspace/module/view/latest/ri.workshop.main.module.918d31af-a745-4a0c-a8d3-ccaa3769727f/page)

You can monitor the Data Provisioning Status by

- *Status*: Here you can check all existing provisionings and their status and configuration. By default this view only shows provisionings that are currently "in progress" or with critical errors. This is the primary view to ensure that no provisionings are "stuck".
- *Use Case*: Here you can check the provisioning status and properties towards a specific target, e.g. a Use Case Project associated with a specific Use Case.
- *Data Treasury Item*: Here you can check the different provisioning status based on a source DTI, e.g. where is the data from this DTI provisioned to and what is the status and the configuration.
- *Request*: Check filed provisioning requests and see their status

**Important:** Make sure you select the proper Business Sector in the dropdown at the top of the app.

![Data Provisioning 2.0 - Status Log](https://docs.uptimize.merckgroup.com/docs-assets/foundry/Images/data-provisioning/DP2_Log.png)
