# Landing Page

Whether you are a new or an experienced user, the landing page streamlines your journey within UPTIMIZE Foundry. For new users, it helps you navigate and kick-start their Foundry experience. It also provides easy and quick access to User Documentation, Communities & Support, and Sector-specific Resources for both new and experienced users.

![New Landing Page in UPTIMIZE Foundry](https://docs.uptimize.merckgroup.com/docs-assets/foundry/Images/landing_page/home_may_9_24.png)
**Fig 1:** Screenshot of the New Landing Page in UPTIMIZE Foundry 

The page is accessed via the UPTIMIZE Foundry home page (VPN Needed): (https://palantir.mcloud.merckgroup.com/workspace/home/) 

**Note:** Be sure to update any bookmarks to https://palantir.mcloud.merckgroup.com/. If you use "https://palantir.mcloud.merckgroup.com/workspace/home/" in your browser history or your bookmark to access Foundry, you will still see the OLD landing page

The Foundry Landing Page consists of a **header**, **two main blocks**, and a **footer**:
![Header](https://docs.uptimize.merckgroup.com/docs-assets/foundry/Images/landing_page/header.png) 
**Fig 2:** Foundry Landing Page "Header"

**The Header:**  
- UPTIMIZE branding and colors 
- Notification Icon (checkmark): 
   - Provides status of any pending user access requests for your review 


**"Get Started on your Data Journey":**
- It is divided into four steps or sections:  
  - Learn 
  - Get Connected 
  - Get Inspired 
  - Create Impact 

![Data journey](https://docs.uptimize.merckgroup.com/docs-assets/foundry/Images/landing_page/journey_may_9_24.png)
**Fig 3:** Foundry Landing Page "Data Journey" 

**Note:** When you hover over the dark blue cards of the Data Journey, an 'i' will appear in the upper right corner of the respective card. Hovering over the "i" you will notice when the card turns over, revealing a brief description of what this card is all about. By clicking on the cards, you will be forwarded to the respective EVA or UPTIMIZE pages. 

## **Find more details on each step below:** 

**Learn**

If you are new to UPTIMIZE Foundry, start familiarizing yourself with the **broad learning opportunities** available at Merck. To get first hands-on experience, you can register for one of our UPTIMIZER Base Camps and start your learning journey there. You will find further information about all available training courses simply by clicking on the EVA Learn card. 

The <i>Tool Overview</i> helps you to get an overview of **all available tools** and when to use them.


**Get Connected:** 

Once you have started learning about UPTIMIZE Foundry, it is useful to get connected with other users and experts. To find existing communities, please have a look at the community overview in the Quick Access Menu below the User Journey. **<i>Insider tip</i>:** make sure to join the **Ensemble Data & Digital Community** to benefit from others' experiences and stay up to date with new Foundry feature releases!  


**Get Inspired!:** 

Check out our **Inspiration Engine** and the **Use Case Portal** to see what others are working on! This might help you to either come up with a promising use case yourself, or you might find an existing use case that fits one of your own challenges. 

1. In case you find an existing use case that looks interesting to you and might potentially support your own challenge or task, **request access** to that specific use case.  
2. If you do not find an existing one, you can also **create a new use case** to work on.  
3. Once you have access to or created a new use case, it is time to think about your data! In the **Data Treasury** you can browse through already ingested data. If you find useful data or data sets, you can request access via the Use Case Access Request card. 
4. If there is no data yet to use for your own use case, you need to request data ingestion. To do so, please click on the **Data Ingestion Request** card. 
5. If you need to enhance the existing with additional data, you also do that via the **Data Ingestion Request**. 



Happy Impact Creation! As soon as you either have access to Data Treasury Items or your own data is ingested, have a look at the Tool Overview again to find the **right tools** for your use case analysis. 


**"Quick Access Menu":** 

Contains links to additional documentation or the already mentioned community overview, but also important links relevant to your respective business sector. 

![Quick Access Menu](https://docs.uptimize.merckgroup.com/docs-assets/foundry/Images/landing_page/quick_access_menu.png)
**Fig 4:** Foundry Landing Page "Quick Access Menu" 

**Footer:** 

If you are experiencing any issues with UPTIMIZE Foundry, please use the <i>Foundry Issues App</i>. You will find it at the bottom right corner of the landing page. Any issue can be submitted here, from general questions to technical issues within Foundry. Your ticket will be routed to the respective team. 

![Footer](https://docs.uptimize.merckgroup.com/docs-assets/foundry/Images/landing_page/technical_issue.png)

## **The Sidebar** 

<i>Although not part of the "Landing Page", the sidebar is an important tool for helping you navigate through Foundry.</i>

If you are new to the platform, read on. The sidebar is your constant companion in Foundry and the starting point for navigating around the platform.  
 
Open and collapse the sidebar with the icon in the upper right or with the keyboard shortcut Ctrl+O on Windows or Cmd+O on macOS. 

It has four sections that allow you to navigate to different features and tools within Foundry: 

|||
|:--|:--|
|![home](https://docs.uptimize.merckgroup.com/docs-assets/foundry/Images/landing_page/home.png)|<b>Home:</b> Return to your organization's landing page. <br> <b>Search:</b> Open the Quicksearch dialog. <br> <b>Notifications:</b> View platform and app notifications.|
|![recent](https://docs.uptimize.merckgroup.com/docs-assets/foundry/Images/landing_page/recent.png)|<b>Recent: </b> Quickly navigate to recently accessed resources. <br> <b>Files:</b> Jump to the Projects landing page. <br> <b>Applications:</b> Find and access all Apps in Foundry.|
|![Applications](https://docs.uptimize.merckgroup.com/docs-assets/foundry/Images/landing_page/applications.png)|<b>Applications:</b> Organize and access your favorite apps and objects.|

Learn more [here](https://palantir.mcloud.merckgroup.com/docs/foundry/platform-overview/aip-assist/#sidebar)<br><b>Support:</b> Access Foundry docs, training resources, and help.<br><b>Account:</b> Find account details and review permissions and groups.| 


More on the sidebar can be found in Palantir's user docs [here](https://palantir.mcloud.merckgroup.com/docs/foundry/learning-core-01/02/#-task-introduction).

# Data Treasury

The data treasury is a core application, hosting Merck's data assets.

* <b class="custom-color">Data Treasury</b> is the application that helps users find available data sets sourced from data systems across Merck making data findable, accessible, interoperable and reusable to drive decision making.
* <b class="custom-color">Data assets</b> (Foundry terminology) are organized by <b>busines sector</b> and data assets <b>categories</b>, e.g. Customer, HR, Finanxe, External etc and are comprised of <b>Data Treasury Items</b>.
* <b class="custom-color">Data Treasury Items (DTIs)</b>, again a Foundry terminology, is a term for a curated dataset immediately accessible in your Foundry use case.  

## DTI Roles

In a nutshell, the SDAOs are responsible to ingest data and create data treasury items. This is carried out by data stewards.

Use Case owners can then subsequently use data in their use cases.

* **Viewer group**: Use case editors of consuming use cases are automatically added to the DTI viewer group.
* **Editor group**: User in this group can **edit** all the content in the respective DTIs. These are SDAO members.

## How to access existing data

If the data that you are intested in exists already in Data treasury, you can raise a data access request (DAR) in Foundry.

## How to get new data

If the data is already partially available, you can raise a data enhancement request. If it does not exist at all, you can raise a data ingestion request.

---

# Use Case

A **Use Case**, sometimes called a Data & Analytics solution, answers a business challenge by analzying data. It drives business objectives and is usually characterized by four main steps: 

* Ingestion
* Preparation
* Modelling
* Impact


## Use Case Owner Roles


| Role | Description |
| -- | -- |
| **Business owner** | The Business Owner can be responsible for sponsoring the project, communicating and defining the business problem and solution, defining the overall vision of the Use Case, working together with the Use Case team on a continuous basis to provide feedback and define further requirements as the business needs.|
| **Product Owner** | This role owns the vision of the product to be built. The role is responsible for the overall Use Case development and implementation, partnering with the development team. The Product Owner is the main contact at Merck for this Use Case and is responsible for approving and administering access to working results of this Use Case.|
| **Technical Lead** | his stakeholder is responsible for overseeing the technical implementation of the Use Case and will be an expert on all technical aspects of the Use Case. |

## Use Case user groups

**Viewer group**: Users in this group can **view** all the content in the respective use case project.

**Editor group**: User in this group can **edit** all the content in the respective use case project.


## Value Types

A case may have one or more value types which describe how the use case is impacting business:

* Compliance
* Cost Saving
* Margin Improvement
* Process Optimization
* Quality Improvement
* Revenue

## Self-Serve or SDAO-led

Use cases which are developed independently on the platform without the involvement of a Sector Data & AI Office (SDAO) are considered as **self-serve**. You might describe it as DIY (do-it-yourself) mode of working. If you need technical/development support by one of the SDAOs, please select 'No'.

This means, that your use case is **SDAO-led** and therefore the SDAO provides the main resources to implement an analytics solution.


## GxP or non-GxP?

GxP is a collection of quality guidelines and regulations created to ensure that bio/pharmaceutical products are safe, meet their intended use, and adhere to quality processes during manufacturing, control, storage, and distribution. 

Some use cases may require enhanced GxP governance in Foundry and therefore are located in a different environment in Foundry, called GxP-org. Non-GxP use cases, which are the large majority of use cases in UPTIMIZE are located in the non-GxP org.

For more information on GxP, please refer to the [Foundry GxP](https://docs.uptimize.merckgroup.com/foundry/foundry-gxp/) page. 

## Use Case Outcome

A Use Case outcome is a `Product` which was created as part of the Use Case and represents one of the Use Case deliverables. Outcomes appear in the outcome section on the use case details. An outcome can be a Slate Application, a Workshop Module, a Contour Report and any other solution being used by a broader group.

---

# Roles & Responsibilities

UPTIMIZE Foundry is Merck's central data & analytics platform for **all Merck employees** regardless if they are coming from business functions or are technical experts. 

## User groups

The main responsibility groups in Foundry regarding use cases and DTIs are

| Group | Description |
| -- | -- |
| Owners | These are typically the product, technical or business owner of a use case. They have full rights and see all details of their use case.|
| Editors | They are contributors to the projects and may work on them.|
| Viewers | They can only view dashboards, but not make any changes.|
| Discoverer | They see metadata, but cannot access files or outcomes. |
| Admin | As sector or platform admins, they also have full control of a use case/DTI for governance purposes.|

Use case owners may use the functionality of `presets` to define combinations of groups and projects outcomes so that Foundry users may specifically request access to e.g. an outcome/folder as viewer.

## Sector Data & AI Offices

The Sector Data & AI Offices (SDAOs) are the first points of contact for Merck employees working with Foundry. 

## Platform Team

There is a dedicated developer team called **Foundry Wizzards** within UPTIMIZE who are in charge of developing the platform. Main responsibilites include:

* Enablement of Foundry users and their use cases 
* Management of the core apps, that is Use Case Portal and Data Treasury.
* Providing Merck-interal support.
* Platform Governance such as Access Management.
* Interaction with other UPTIMIZE platforms and apps. 

The platform team can be reached via the <a href="https://palantir.mcloud.merckgroup.com/workspace/issues-app/">Issue App</a> for a very specific issue or question.

For larger issues (e.g. Foundry not reachable, major outage etc.) feel free to post in the MS Team [Foundry user community](https://teams.microsoft.com/l/team/19%3Aa1464290282642f1bdd5af154cc8a1aa%40thread.skype/conversations?groupId=35e1aa5a-f62f-4250-88bb-55618501f343&tenantId=db76fb59-a377-4120-bc54-59dead7d39c9).

## Community

UPTIMIZE Foundry has more than 21.000 active users each month and is continuing to grow further. The user community is quite in the MS Teams channels: Both beginners and experts can raise questions and usually, the community replies within hours if not minutes. 

### UPTIMIZE Foundry Teams Channel

Join our growing [Foundry user community](https://teams.microsoft.com/l/team/19%3Aa1464290282642f1bdd5af154cc8a1aa%40thread.skype/conversations?groupId=35e1aa5a-f62f-4250-88bb-55618501f343&tenantId=db76fb59-a377-4120-bc54-59dead7d39c9) to get your questions answered by fellow Foundry enthusiasts at Merck.

There are sub-channels for various platform apps and topics such as Contour, AIP or VS Code.
Beginners welcome!

### Office hours
There are virtual **Open Office Hours** to answer all your Foundry questions:

* <ld-icon name="calendar"></ld-icon> Every Wednesday: 9 AM CEST on [MS Teams](https://palantir.mcloud.merckgroup.com/blobster/api/salt/ri.blobster.main.blob.70857a17-c4d6-4617-89be-12c709b4853f).

# Ontology

In Foundry, the concept ontology is a structured framework that defines and organizes the relationships between various entities, concepts, and data elements within a given domain. It serves as a semantic model that helps users understand the context and meaning of data by establishing clear definitions and connections among different data points.

## Key Features of Concept Ontology in Palantir Foundry:

1. **Semantic Relationships**: The ontology defines various types of relationships (e.g., associative, hierarchical) between concepts, enhancing the understanding of how different data elements interact.

1. **Standardization**: By providing a common vocabulary and framework, the concept ontology promotes consistency in data usage across different teams and applications.

1. **Data Integration**: It facilitates the integration of diverse data sources by mapping them to the ontology, making it easier to analyze and derive insights from disparate datasets.

1. **Enhanced Data Discovery**: Users can leverage the ontology for improved data discovery, enabling them to find relevant data more efficiently based on the relationships and definitions provided.

1. **Support for Analytics**: The structured nature of the ontology supports advanced analytics and machine learning by providing a clear understanding of the data landscape.

Overall, the concept ontology in Palantir Foundry is crucial for creating a unified, understandable, and actionable view of data, enabling organizations to make informed decisions based on comprehensive insights.



You can find out more in the official [Palantir documentation](https://www.palantir.com/docs/foundry/ontologies/ontologies-overview/).

## Merck's Setup

In UPTIMIZE Foundry, we have two major ontologies:

* **Merck**: This is our production ontology. Only authorized users with special training have edit rights.
* **Playground**: This ontology is reserved for training purposes. By signing up to a training, users may get edit access to this ontology.

## Apps in Foundry

Ontologies can be viewed and edited in [Ontology Manager](https://palantir.mcloud.merckgroup.com/workspace/ontology/home/discover).

# Use Case Portal

## Overview
The Use Case Portal is the one-stop-shop for tracking work in UPTIMIZE across the global Merck Organization. Start exploring existing Use Cases by Business Sector, create a new Use Case or request access to an existing one. The Use Case Portal does not only serve as a portfolio management tool but also as a governance tool, it provides transparency in the Merck Organization over the way the Use Case is implemented on the platform.
If the use case should be supported by one of the Sector Data Offices, the quality of the description of the Use Case impacts its prioritization. Using the Use Case Portal the relevant people can track the ideation process and execution of building the use case pipeline and deliverables using the `use case` object, and finally list the `use case outcomes`.

### Use Case Portal Ontology
The Use Case Portal is mainly based in one object type: the [Use Case](https://palantir.mcloud.merckgroup.com/workspace/documentation/product/use-case-portal/use_case). The instances of these objects complement their information with links with other object types, such as the ones representing Global Business Unit or Business Functions or the specifically defined [Use Case Outcomes](https://palantir.mcloud.merckgroup.com/workspace/documentation/outcomes.md) to represent all the outputs and products derived from the Use Case concept. Also during the [creation](https://palantir.mcloud.merckgroup.com/workspace/documentation/howto_usecase.md) and [edit](https://palantir.mcloud.merckgroup.com/workspace/documentation/howto_usecase.md) processes Temporal or Draft Use Cases are created to make it easy for User to submit new information.

### Use Case Portal User Interface
The Use Case Portal 2.0 is implemented as a Workshop module and it consists of three main pages which you can switch using the toolbar on top of the view.

1. **Personal View:** this is this entry point to the portal and shows personalized list of all Use Cases the user owns (as a Product/Business Owner or Tech Lead) or the user has access to/requested access for. It allows user to manage the Use Cases they use more easily by showing summarized information. You can learn more about this view [here](https://palantir.mcloud.merckgroup.com/workspace/documentation/product/use-case-portal/howto_manage_your_use_cases).
2. **Search View:** allows the user to explore all Use Cases at Merck and find specific Use Cases by name or configuring many other search options. You can find detailed information about searching for Use Cases [here](https://palantir.mcloud.merckgroup.com/workspace/documentation/product/use-case-portal/howto_search_use_cases).
3. **Create new Use Case View:** before creating a new Use Case, the user can explore and get information about Use Cases similar to the one that the user is about to create and complete the full creation process for a Use Case. You can learn more [here](https://palantir.mcloud.merckgroup.com/workspace/documentation/howto_use_cases.md).

### Concept of a Use Case
The Use Case object represent a use case in execution and allows for monitoring the use case status, mapping to the projects used for building the use case and the use case outcomes.

A Use Case has several properties that provide different information. There are properties that define the Use Case itself, such as its name or description, the responsible owners for the Use Case or the status in the [lifecycle of Use Cases](https://docs.uptimize.merckgroup.com/foundry/use-case-portal/use-case-lifecycle/). Please note that based on the sector, the information requested for a Use Case varies.

Apart from this information, which is stored as properties of the object, Use Cases also have other linked objects that provide extra information and establish a relationship between Use Cases and other concepts, such as the Use Case Outcomes, Projects, Business Functions...

Users can execute actions on Use Cases such as requesting access, editing the status of the Use Case (Use Case Owners only!) or defining new Use Case Outcomes. The ability to execute these actions depends on the level of ownership you have for a specific Use Case (for example, if you are not the owner of an Use Case you cannot update its status). To find out what permissions are required depending on the Use Case, please see the "How to" tutorials included in this documentation.

You can explore all these properties, linked objects and actions from the Use Case Portal, by managing your own Use Cases in the Personal tab, seraching for existing Use Cases using the Search page or creating new ones in the Create New Use Case page.

### Concept of a Use Case Outcome (Product)
A Use Case outcome is a Product which was created as part of the Use Case and represents one of the Use Case deliverables. Outcomes appear in the outcome section on the use case details. An outcome can be a Slate Application, a Workshop Module, a Contour Report and any other solution being used by a broader group.

For more information on how to create and view Use Case outcomes see How to create outcomes.

### How to create a Use Case
To create a new Use Case you need to go to the Create New Use Case tab in the Use Case Portal 2.0. The new Use Case is created by clicking on the button placed on the bottom right part of the page.

Before creating your use case we encourage you to enter your use case description in the text area available in the same page. This will prevent you from creating a Use Case for something someone else has already been working on. If what you find is not exactly what you were thinking about and you want to proceed with your own use case you can use the ideas for the similar use cases to inspire you.

If you decide to go on and create your own Use Case, you will start the process by clicking the Create your own Use Case button on the same page and selecting the Business Sector your Use Case is related to.

Once the sector is selected, by cliking on Start Use Case creation process you will be moved to a new view where you will have to complete a three steps process asking you for different information related to the Use Case depending on the specific sector and inputs in previous steps.

1. **General Information**: at this step you have to provide details about the problem that you try to solve with your use case and who are the responsible owners of it.
2. **Status Information**: all new Use Cases are created in Ideation status (check the lifecycle status of Use Cases) so in this step you will be required to submit details about this phase.
3. **Review and Confirm**: you will see a summary with all the fields that you have fulfilled just to check that everything is correct before submiting the creation of the use case. If you want to change the input of any field you can navigate back to the corresponding step by clinking on it on the progress bar.

You can navigate to previous steps using the progress bar and advance to the next one clicking on the Next step button. Note that navigating back when you have not already submitted the information of the current step will lose the values for the fields populated on that step, so it is better to first complete the step you are in and after advancing to the next one navigate back to the one you wanted to edit.

Populate as many fields of the Use Case Creation as you are able to - you can always revisit this at a later date. NB: it can take up to 30 minutes for a Use Case to appear in teh Use Case portal once the form has been submitted.

#### Saving draft Use Cases
Having the creation of a New Use Case splitted into steps allows you to quit the process at any moment and save your progress for later. For example, if you have submitted the general information for your Use Case and you are unsure about what is the Business impact (information required for Ideation phase), you can save your progress and continue later. To do so, once you complete the first step (the one asking you for general information) you will see a Save and Exit button as well as a trash one.

By clicking the first of them, the information of the steps already completed will be saved for later. By clicking the trash button, nothing will be saved.

When you save Use Cases for later, you will see a banner in the toolbar of the New Use Case page informing you about the number of draft Use Cases that are pending to complete (see the first image). By clicking on it you'll see a dteailed list of that draft Use Cases, where you can remove some of them (using the checkboxes and the trash button) or continue the creation process of any of them by directly clicking on their names.

### How to Edit an existing Use Case
Use Cases that are already created can be edited to update the mandatory fields, add information to non-mandatory fields or to change the status information. This is a task that only can be done by any of the three owners of the Use Case (Business Owner, Product Owner or Technical Lead).

If you are one of the three owners of the Use Case, the use case stage gate options (Move to Planning, Move to Proof of Value Development, Move to Industrialization) will be available when you access the Use Case from your personal area in the Use Case Portal 2.0, next to the "More" menu. In additon to that, you will find the options in the "More" menu to Discard or Decommission your Use Case or put the Use Case on Hold.

The Use Case Property View allows you to see all your use case properties at a glance. Additionally, it allows you to edit the use case properties independent from the Use Case status. You can now easily update Use Case properties without going through all the phases of the use case again. If you are one of the Use Case owners, you will see an "Edit" button on each category that will display a form where you can modify any of the properties in that section.

### How to manage your own Use Cases
The Use Case Portal 2.0 contains a dedicated section where you can easily find and manage all your Use Cases. When you access the Use Case Portal 2.0 you land on the Personal page. You can go to it at every moment clicking on the first tab of the toolbar.

There you will have a list on the left with all the Use Cases related to you, that is, Use Cases which:

- You are the Business Owner.
- You are the Product Owner.
- You are the Technical Lead.
- You have access to the Use Case.
- You have requested access to the Use Case and your request is still pending to be approved.

This is a way to easily find the Uses Cases you work more with. By selecting any of these Use Cases you will see some key information about the Use Case and their linked projects and Use Case Outcomes.

If you are one of the three owners of the Use Case you are allowed to take more actions regarding the Use Case, such as editing it or adding Use Case Outcomes.

Also, if you are an owner of the Use Case an it has pending access requests you will see an alert message next to the Use Case Name. Clicking on this will display a list with all the pending Access Requests to the Use Case which you can open and manage the requests.

It is also possible to filter the list with your Use Cases, searching for keywords included in any field of the Use Case and filtering the results depending on the access type.

### How to Search existing Use Cases
The Use Case Portal 2.0 gives you the option to browse the existing Use Cases in the platform and explore all their linked information, as well as requesting access to them.

#### Searching for Use Cases
The Search Use Cases page of the Use Case Portal allows you to serach for specific Use Cases. By typing something on the serach bar you will get all the Use Cases with a name matching your input. The returned Use Cases will be those:

1. Matching the exact name.
2. The beginning of the Use Case name matches your input.
3. The Use Case name contains (at any point) your input.
4. All the tokens in your input are contained in the Use Case name.

Also note that the serach is case-insensitive and that special characters will be removed from your input as well as from the Use Case names to browse.

#### Semantic Search
In addition to keyword matching, the portal now supports **semantic search**.
 
- This uses language model embeddings to understand the meaning of your query.
- It can return Use Cases that are conceptually related, even if they don't share exact words with your input.
- Results are ranked by relevance score, so the most closely related Use Cases appear at the top.


#### Filtering your search
You can filter the results of your serach in two main ways: Using the sector filters on the right or using any filter in the advanced search panel

- Filtering by sector: You can click on any sector card on right and the results of your serach will include only Use Cases of that specific sector. Clicking on a sector card once selected will diselect it.
- Advanced search filters: By opening the advanced serach panel you can filter your search by many fields. The keyword input will serach for Use Cases with any field (it can be a description, a project, an owner...) matching your input. The rest of the filters allow you to select one or more options from the dropdowns to get only results maching those porperties

When you apply filters to your search you will see a summary of them just under the search bar.

You can reset all the filters by clicking on the "Reset" button.
Once you click on one of the serached Use Cases you'll be able to display its Hubble view by clicking on them.

### How to Create Use Case Outcomes
All Outcomes linked to a Use Case appear in a specific section in the bottom left part of the Use Case view in the Personal Page. You can open any of the ocutcomes in Foundry by simply cliking on its names.

In the Use Case outcome section of the Use Case View, there are two buttons available to the owners allowing them to add or remove outcomes from the current Use Case. By clicking on the Add Outcome button it will display a form where you'll be able to submit the needed information for linking an outcome to your Use Case. Once submitted, the outcome name will appear in the mentioned section

Furthermore, you can remove use case outcomes by clicking on Remove Outcome. To do so, click on the "Remove Outcome" button and select the Use Case Product you would like to remove.

### How to set the status of a Use Case
When creating a new Use Case **Ideation** status is set. After that, owners can move it through the different phases providing the needed information using the buttons available in the Use Case View in the Personal page.

Once our Use Case is created, you can change the status and move the Use Case to a different stage of the Use Case Lifecycle. This movement has to be done step by step, so that Use Cases can only be moved to the next status of the lifecycle. To do so, owners will see a button allowing them to move to the next status named "Move to status" (if the Use Case is already in Industrialization status, as this is the last step in the active lifecycle of the Use Case no button will be available). When clicking this button, a form requesting all fields for that status required by your business sector will be dsiplayed, and after completing it the Use Case will me moved to the new status and the Use Case View will display this new status iformation accordingly.

You can move your Use Case to these statuses using this buttons, always following the order:

- **Planning:** Stakeholders are aligning and gathering information on how to implement the Use Case and how it will be measured.
- **Proof of Value Development (POV):** The first version of the Use Case is being developed and built. At the end of the initial Proof of Value (POV) implementation, the Use Case will be assessed for whether it will be continued or decommissioned. In this status, a project folder will be automatically created for and linked to your Use Case.
- **Industrialization:** The Use Case POV has been successful and so the outputs are being continually developed, supported and rolled out to the target user base.

There are three special statuses you can move your Use Case to that won't be available as buttons in the toolbar as previously described. The options to move to any of those statuses will appear under the "More" menu in the personal page, and as the other ones they will only be available to owners. These are the status that these buttons will allow to move your Use Case to:

- **Decommissioned:** The POV or Industrialized Use Case has been discontinued and is no longer being developed or supported.
- **Expired:** The Use Case reaches the "Expired" status after the allowed interval has passed. The interval that a Use Case can remain in each stage is defined by this process. For Ideation and Planning stages, the interval is 6 months. If more time is needed, Use Case Owners can ask for an extension. For Proof of Value (PoV) Development stage, the interval is 12 months. If more time is needed, Use Case Owners can ask for an extension.

# Use Case Lifecycle 

**The Use Case lifecycle** is a process that governs the journey of UPTIMIZE Use Cases and defines the various stages, activities that occur, and timelines for those stages. This process ensures that only high-quality, impactful Use Cases are captured in Foundry.

The Use Case lifecycle provides Use Case Owners, Technical Leads, and Stakeholders with a clear framework to manage each stage of a Use Case from ideation to industrialization and beyond, ensuring quality and efficiency throughout the process.


> **Note:**<br>Up until March 2026, the stage Ideations and Planning are separate. In order to simplify the process, these stages shall be migrated to one joint "Ideations & Planning" stage.


Below you will find guidance on the **Lifecycle stages of a Use Case** and the activities that occur.

![overview](/assets/use-case-lifecycle/lifecycle_of_a_use_case.png)

## Use Case Intake

In order to create a use case, you need to have the following information:

<table style="border-collapse: collapse; width: 100%;">
  <thead>
    <tr>

      <td style="border: 1px solid #ddd; padding: 8px;">There are the following options:<br><br>
        <b>Self-Serve:</b> When you create and manage your own use cases independently, without support from any spoke organization or ACE.<br><br>
        <b>Spoke Use Cases:</b> Developed independently by the Spoke organization without ACE support, the Spoke team is responsible for business engagement, requirement gathering, and solution delivery, with development managed by the Spoke organization e.g use case development led by Process Solution / Science and Lab Solutions Data office.<br><br>
        <b>ACE-Led Use Cases:</b> ACE team develops and manages the solutions. ACE is responsible for business engagement, requirement gathering, prioritization, and delivery oversight, while ACE developers design and implement the solution.<br><br>
        <b>Spoke-Led Use Cases managed by ACE:</b> The Spoke team collaborates with ACE to develop the solution and to manage its delivery. They work with ACE developers to build and implement the solution effectively.<br><br>
        <b>ACE Internal:</b> Internal tagged use cases will not go thru the UC prioritization and UC council.
      </td>
      <td style="border: 1px solid #ddd; padding: 8px;"><b class="custom-color">Yes</b></td>
      <td style="border: 1px solid #ddd; padding: 8px;">LS</td>
    </tr>
  </tbody>
</table>

<ld-notice headline="Tip">
  Always check out the Use Case portal for <b class="custom-color">close-matching existing use cases</b>. There might be a close match that fulfills already 80% of your target. It's a lot more efficient to collaborate on an existing use case than to reinvent the wheel for a small enhancement. 
</ld-notice>

## Ideation & Planning

The Use Case is in very early stages and the idea has been proposed.

![ideation](/assets/use-case-lifecycle/State_Ideation.png)

A [Use Case](https://palantir.mcloud.merckgroup.com/workspace/module/view/latest/ri.workshop.main.module.cfbd54d9-5f5e-4c67-a94d-37fc842812cc/personal) is required for any data-related activity on the platform:

- Data Ingestion
- Data Enhancement
- Data Sharing / Access
- Data Analysis

For Use Cases that are not Self-Serve, they will be assessed by the Sector Data Office (SDO) in terms of value and ease of implementation and prioritized accordingly. For those Use Cases that are Self-Serve, you will drive this assessment within your project team.

Stakeholders are aligning and gathering information on how to implement this Use Case and how it will be measured.

For Use Cases that are not Self-Serve, SDO Product Owners are available for planning exercise, and more SDO involvement can be discussed at this stage. You can again choose to have a project space created at this stage if you did not during Ideation.

At this stage, you must provide:

You have up to 6 months to complete this stage of your Use Case before it expires. If additional time is needed, you can request an extension through the *Request Manager* or the *More* menu. Please note that any extension at this stage will require approval from an SDO.

## Proof of Value Development (PoVD)

The first version of the Use Case is being developed and built. At the end of the PoVD implementation, the Use Case will be assessed for whether it will be continued or decommissioned.

![pov](/assets/use-case-lifecycle/State_PoV.png)

In this stage, a Project Space is created automatically for you (if it wasn't created in earlier stages). You will also have the option to request additional projects, enabling Use Case owners to grant others Editor and Viewer access and request access to external systems like AWS or Snowflake.

You must provide:

<table style="border-collapse: collapse; width: 100%;">
  <thead>
    <tr>
      <th style="border: 1px solid #ddd; padding: 8px; text-align: left; width: 18%;">Field</th>
      <th style="border: 1px solid #ddd; padding: 8px; text-align: left; width: 34%;">Description</th>
      <th style="border: 1px solid #ddd; padding: 8px; text-align: left; width: 7%;">Mandatory</th>

You have up to 12 months to complete this stage of your Use Case before it expires. If you need more time, you can request an extension through the Request Manager or the More menu. Please note that extensions exceeding 3 months at this stage will require approval from an SDO.

## Industrialization

The Use Case POV was successful, and it is being continually developed, supported, and rolled out to the target user base.

![industrialization](/assets/use-case-lifecycle/State_Industrialization.png)

For Use Cases that are not Self-Serve, you may receive additional support from your SDO. There will be high visibility in your Sector's Portfolio to advertise your valuable Use Case to others.

In this stage, you must provide:
