## On Hold

The **On Hold** status represents Use Cases that are temporarily paused due to shifting priorities or resource constraints but may be revisited later.

![on_hold](/assets/use-case-lifecycle/State_On_Hold.png)

Your Use Case can remain in the On Hold status for 6 months.

## Expired

The Use Case reaches the "Expired" status after the allowed interval has passed. The interval that a Use Case can remain in each stage is defined by this process.

![expired](/assets/use-case-lifecycle/State_Expired.png)

- For **Ideation** and **Planning** stages, the interval is 6 months. If more time is needed, Use Case Owners can ask for an extension.
- For **Proof of Value (PoV) Development** stage, the interval is 12 months. If more time is needed, Use Case Owners can ask for an extension.
- For **On Hold** stage, the interval is 6 months. If more time is needed, Use Case Owners can ask for an extension.


### Consequences

Once a Use Case reaches Expired status, it will remain for up to four weeks before being automatically decommissioned.

* During this time, access to Use Case projects will be restricted. 
* Your Use Case's projects will be moved to **Restricted Resource Queue**. In this Restricted Queue, there is only one CPU available, **effectively disabling** all compute in your use case: e.g. your use case schedules, transforms etc. will no longer be able to run. 
* Downstream Use Cases, that is Use Cases consuming data of your use cases, will become incompliant.


If an Expired Use Case has active dependencies from other Use Cases, the **Dependency handling in Decommissioning** feature ensures decommissioning is blocked until consumer Use Case owners confirm or remove the dependency. For detailed instructions, please refer to the [Decommissioning Process](/foundry/use-case-portal/decommissioning-process).



### What to do

If you actually want to continue working on your use case, you can extend your expiry yourself once per state, by clicking on "Self Expiry date extension" (see option 1). This will immediately reset your use case to its previous state and you may continue working and your new expiration date is set to three months from now.

Otherwise, if you do not want to continue your use case, you can start the **decommissioning** process, by clicking on "Decomission Use Case".

![expiry-options](/assets/foundry/uc-expiry-options.png)

Note that without any action from your part, the use case will be automatically decommissioned after four weeks.

Requesting an extension of the Expiry date can be done multiple times per use case stage, however for the second request onwards, these requests need to be approved by your Sector Data & AI office (SDAO). When your use case goes past its expiry date and you already extended it once, then you will get the following options:

![expiry-options2](/assets/foundry/uc-expiry-options2.png)

For a further three months extension, click "Request additional Expiry Date Extension". This will create UPTIMIZE Request - Use Case Expiration Date Extension, which SDAOs can then approve or reject.
Note that this secondary extension will therefore not be immediate and your use case will remain in the expired state until a member of your SDAO approves your extension request.

SDAOs will then get an e-mail notification to either approve or reject this extension. In case they approve the extension, the use case will be reset to its previous lifecycle stage.


n request an extension to the expiry date via the Request Manager. When your Use Case is already expired you need to use the "Request additional Expiry Date Extension" button, since the Request Manager is not available for expired use cases.

### Notifications

Use Case owners will receive email notifications to take action four weeks, two weeks, and one week in advance of the Use Case expiration and again at the same intervals before final decommission.

## Decommissioned

The Use Case is no longer being developed or supported, or no action was taken on the Use during the four-week "Expired" period.

![decommissioned](/assets/use-case-lifecycle/State_Decommissioned.png)

This stage helps users on the platform avoid confusion and prevents unnecessary contact or alerts for an application which is no longer in use.

In this stage, Use Case Owners will be reminded again to take action three days prior to the Use Case being automatically decommissioned:

If there are any downstream use cases: 


### Decommissioning Actions

* **Remove Schedules:** All scheduled tasks and jobs associated with the project's datasets will be removed.
* **Health Checks and Close Issues:** Active Health Checks will be removed, and all Open Issues within the project's datasets will be closed.
* **Trash Datasets**: The project's datasets will be sent to the trash and will be permanently deleted 30 days after being trashed.
* **Remove Branches**: All branches in the code repositories, except for the master branch, will be removed.
* **Reject Pending Access Requests**: Any pending Access Requests (Access Requests and Data Provisioning Access Requests) related to the Use Case will be rejected.
* **Revoke Finished Data Provisioning Access Requests**: Any 'done' Data Provisioning Access Requests will be revoked and an Unprovisioning Request will be sent to stop the provisioning to the UC project folder.
* **Manage Groups**:
  * Process Viewer & Editor Project Groups: Editor project groups will be deleted and their members will be added to the Viewer group.
  * Update Owner Group: All members will be removed from the owner groups, and the Operations Team will be added.
  * Add Global Audit Viewer Group: For auditing purposes.
  * Remove uncompliant Groups: All uncompliant groups will be removed from having access to the projects.

Note that decommisioning is **final** and data cannot be retrieved, when backups are sweeped 30 days later.

---

# Use Case Owner Roles

## Main Roles

### Business Owner
The Business Owner can be responsible for sponsoring the project, communicating and defining the business problem and solution, defining the overall vision of the Use Case, working together with the Use Case team on a continuous basis to provide feedback and define further requirements as the business needs.

### Product Owner
This role owns the vision of the product to be built. The role is responsible for the overall Use Case development and implementation, partnering with the development team. The Product Owner is the main contact at Merck for this Use Case and is responsible for approving and administering access to working results of this Use Case.

### Technical Lead
This stakeholder is responsible for overseeing the technical implementation of the Use Case and will be an expert on all technical aspects of the Use Case. 


### Sponsor (LS-specific)
The Use Case Sponsor is the person who provides funding and resources to enable its success.



## Responsibilities 

The **Business Owner** and **Product Owner** takes on the responsibility to

* assess business continuity plan for the use-case, if the use-case in the UPTIMIZE platform product is not operational. 
* assess business risk for the use-case and feed risks into Group Risk Management process as needed.
* assess whether the information classification (as per Merck Trade Secret Policy (ManGo Doc ID 20390530) ) of the newly created datasets as part of this use-case differ from the original information classification of the used data. Please note: secret data can not be stored on the platform.
* define data retention timelines for the data in scope of this use-case, as per group data retention schedule. Please also see Foundry-specific guidance here. 
* follow the UPTIMIZE HR Data Handling Guidelines and policies.
* ensure that only non-prohibited AI is used, in accordance with the EU AI Act.

The **Technical Owner** takes on responsibility to
* assess IT-security risk for the use case, apply security penetration testing as applicable and feed risks into Group Risk Management process as needed.
* test the use case outcome before go-live (Industrialization Phase).

---

# Use Case Tasks

Use Case tasks provide a structured approach to managing your use case throughout its lifecycle. They break down complex requirements into small, actionable items that guide you through each stage of development and maintenance.



## What are Use Case Tasks?

Tasks are automatically generated to help you track and complete critical activities. The system creates different types of tasks depending on your use case's stage and status:

* **Use Case tasks** -- Complete required fields to progress to the next stage
* **Compliance tasks** -- Address policy, security, and risk management requirements
* **Lifecycle tasks** -- Manage stage transitions and handle expiry notifications
* **Annual review tasks** -- Maintain industrialized use cases post go-live

## Why Use Tasks?

Tasks bring structure and visibility to the use case development process:

* **Transparency** -- See at a glance what needs to be done for each use case
* **Accountability** -- Each task has a designated owner, due date, and clear status
* **Risk reduction** -- Surface compliance and data health issues early in the process
* **Delivery discipline** -- Ensure all prerequisites are met before advancing to the next stage

## How to access Use Case Tasks?

On the Use Case Overview page the number of open Tasks for this use case are shown: see point 1 in the below screenshot. 

<a href="/assets/use-case-lifecycle/UC-Overview-Task.png" target="_blank"><img src="/assets/use-case-lifecycle/UC-Overview-Task.png" width="90%"></a>


### Use Case Tasks Tab

You can then navigate to the tab "Use Case Tasks" (see **(1)** in the below screnshot) to see all tasks assigned to your use case.

<a href="/assets/use-case-lifecycle/UC-Task-Overview.png" target="_blank"><img src="/assets/use-case-lifecycle/UC-Task-Overview.png" width="90%"></a>

Tasks are based on the [use case's complexity](/foundry/use-case-portal/use-case-lifecycle/uc-complexity/). The results of the use case complexity calculations are shown with this banner in **(2)**.

All Use Case Tasks that are linked to preliminary stages need to be completed to move to the next stage: E.g. all Ideation & Planning and PoVD Tasks need to be completed to move to Industrialization.  Once this is done, you can use the transition task in **(3)** to move to the next stage. It is only visible when a transition is possible.

The table in **(4)** shows all open tasks for the use case. You can also look at "Complete" tasks by adding this to the filters on the right-hand side.


### Task Details 

When you click on a Task, an overlay with the Task Details opens:

<a href="/assets/use-case-lifecycle/Task-Detail.png" target="_blank"><img src="/assets/use-case-lifecycle/Task-Detail.png" width="90%"></a>

On the left-hand side **(1)** you may find context and guidance for your task. At the bottom of the left-hand side **(2)**, you see which stage this task belongs to and its current status.

On the right-hand side **(3)**, at the top, you find the task's meta data:

* Priority
* Deadline (if applicable)
* Required status: Mandatory or optional
* Assignee: The current person who is designated to complete the task. Current Task assignees and Use Case Owners may change this to any other User.

Below at **(4)** you find a form where you can carry out the task. Once completed and sent, the task will change status to complete and vanish as open task from the Use Case Task tab.


## Determining Factors

Which tasks appear for a given use case depends on several factors:

| Factor | Description |
|--------|-------------|
| **Sector** | Tasks are configured per sector -- Healthcare, Life Science, Group Functions, and Electronics. A task will only appear if it is enabled for the use case's sector. |
| **Lifecycle Stage** | Tasks are tied to a specific lifecycle stage (e.g., Industrialization). |
| **[Use Case Complexity](/foundry/use-case-portal/use-case-lifecycle/uc-complexity/)** | Tasks can be scoped to Low, Moderate, or High complexity use cases. For example, a task may only apply to High-complexity use cases, while simpler use cases are not required to complete it. |
| **GxP Status** | Some tasks apply only when the use case is GxP-relevant. |
| **Usage of AWS** | Certain tasks are only generated for use cases that leverage AWS infrastructure. |
| **Self-serve / Use Case Led by** | Some tasks are limited to non-self-serve (centrally supported) use cases. |


## Task Examples

The following table shows common tasks you'll encounter for each task type:

| Task Type | Example Tasks |
|-----------|---------------|
| **Use Case Tasks** | - Assign Product Owner and Technical Lead<br>- Confirm PII ITK compliance<br>- Define Business KPI and PoV scope<br>- Read/acknowledge Access Control documentation<br>- Provide link to Business Requirements and Implementation Approach |
| **Compliance Tasks** | - Link compliant Owner/Editor/Viewer groups<br>- Ensure linked DTI and/or DIR is correct<br>- Naming convention compliance and "Not Deprecated" naming<br>- Valid access requests for used DTIs at the UC level |
| **Lifecycle Tasks** | - Move to Proof of Value Development (only when prerequisites are complete)<br>- Move to Industrialization and confirm readiness (health checks, schedules, training)<br>- Address Expiry (renew or decommission according to policy) |
| **Annual Review Tasks** | - Annual review of Health Checks and Build Schedules<br>- Update or confirm Technical Guide and Support Model |


Once a use case reaches the **Industrialization** stage, it enters an ongoing annual review cycle. The system automatically generates review tasks each year to ensure that industrialized use cases remain healthy, well-documented, and cost-effective.


## Task Ownership

Tasks have a default owner (one of the three <a href="/foundry/use-case-portal/use-case-lifecycle/uc-owners">Use Case Owner Roles</a>), but may be delegated to other users.

## Task Completion

Task completion always hinges on the filling of one use case property. You may fill out this on the Task page or in Edit-mode on the Use Case itself -- both will lead to the completion of the task.

## Task Due Dates

Each task comes with a due date that is automatically calculated based on the task type. This ensures timely completion and maintains compliance throughout the use case lifecycle.

### How Due Dates are Determined

Due dates are set differently depending on the task type:

* **Lifecycle tasks** -- Due date aligns with the use case's expiration date
* **Compliance tasks** -- Due date is calculated from the "first detected" timestamp plus a configurable grace period
* **Annual review tasks** -- Due date is based on the industrialization date anniversary plus a configurable completion window (see [Annual Review Tasks](#annual-review-tasks-industrialized-use-cases) above)

### Overdue Tasks

When a task becomes overdue, the use case is automatically flagged as **non-compliant**. This ensures that:

* Delivery readiness is verified before stage transitions
* Risk and data hygiene issues gain early visibility
* Industrialized use cases are properly maintained or decommissioned when no longer active

**Special Case: Using a DTI without Access Request**

For cases where use cases utilize a dataset from a DTI without a valid access request, upon reaching the due date (two weeks from detection), the reference will be automatically remove after **30 days**.

---

# Use Case Complexity

Use case complexity is a classification system that helps prioritize lifecycle tasks and focus effort where it matters most. Each use case is assigned a complexity rating of **Low**, **Moderate**, or **High** based on several key factors.

Certain lifecycle tasks are only required or recommended for higher-complexity use cases, allowing teams to allocate resources efficiently and apply governance proportional to each use case's scope and impact.

## How Complexity is Determined

Use case complexity is calculated based on the following factors:

- **Data breadth**: The number of Data Treasury Items (DTIs) consumed by the use case
- **Audience size**: The total number of users in viewer groups across all projects linked to the use case
- **Monthly operational cost**: The total cost for the second-most-recent month (using the previous complete month to avoid partial data)
- **Special classifications**: Whether the use case is designated as a GxP use case or a non-self-serve use case

As a use case evolves and grows--consuming more data, serving more users, or incurring higher costs--its complexity rating may change automatically, and the relevant lifecycle tasks will update accordingly.

## Complexity Rating Logic

The complexity rating is determined by evaluating each factor independently and then combining the results. If a use case scores "Moderate" in one category, then it is at least "Moderate", then it is considered "Moderate", if it has at least one "High", then it is considered "High", else "Low".

### Data Treasury Items (DTIs) Consumed

| Rating | Criteria |
|--------|----------|
| High | More than 10 DTIs |
| Moderate | 4-10 DTIs |
| Low | 3 or fewer DTIs |

### Viewer Users

The total count of members across all viewer groups for projects linked to the use case:

| Rating | Criteria |
|--------|----------|
| High | More than 50 users |
| Moderate | 21-50 users |
| Low | 20 or fewer users |

### Monthly Operational Cost

Based on the total cost for the second-most-recent month:

| Rating | Criteria |
|--------|----------|
| High | More than $1,000 |
| Moderate | $100-$1,000 |
| Low | Less than $100 |

---

## Introduction

UPTIMIZE Request is a tool and defined process allowing UPTIMIZE Foundry users to create requests for changing Use Case configurations. It also enables the responsible Sector Data Office to manage these incoming requests.

We maintain various types of UPTIMIZE Requests to handle different types of configuration change requests, reflected in so called "Extension Types". Currently, the following extension types are defined:
 - "request project default role change":
 Change the default role given to user on Foundry for a specific Foundry Use Case project (e.g. change default role to "viewer" so that everyone has viewer access to the project). 
 - "request additional compass role":
 Configure a new compass role with elevated permissions. If not already existing, we create a new &lt;project-name&gt;-editor-plus group and configure this group and subgroups to have certain permissions with selected members (e.g. policy setter or repository owner permissions). 

## Where to Manage UPTIMIZE Requests

Both request types, " default role" and "additional compass role," configure the settings of a project linked to a use case. Therefore, we display two new buttons for the use case owners in the selected use case view in our Use Case Portal.

<img src="/assets/uptimize-request/use-case-portal-uptimize-button.png" alt="new buttons in Use Case Portal 2.0" width="90%"/>

The 'Request Manager' button opens a pop-up section where an UPTIMIZE Request can be configured and submitted.

<img src="/assets/uptimize-request/requestmanager-default-role.png" alt="Request Manager - Default Role" width="50%"/>

<img src="/assets/uptimize-request/requestmanager-additionalcompass.png" alt="Request Manager - additional compass role" width="40%"/>

The 'View Existing Requests' button leads to a table view of existing requests.

<img src="/assets/uptimize-request/use-case-portal-2-view-existing.png" alt="Existing Requests" width="90%"/>

*Please note:* The UPTIMIZE Request is continually being enhanced, so additional options will appear in this menu in the future.

## Approved Requests are Processed Automatically

When a UPTIMIZE Request is submitted, the approvers (Sector Data Offices) are determined and stored in the request object based on the business unit of the use case, the requested extension type and the ontology object 'Uptimize Request Approval Group'. The approvers are notified of the new incoming request. Ideally, this request is then approved and awaits the pipeline to process it. 

If the pipeline successfully configures the required platform settings, the request object is moved to 'succeeded' and the requestor is notified. 

In case of any failure during the pipeline execution, the object moves into 'process_failed' and the approvers are notified to investigate the error in the logs.

## Who Can Submit a UPTIMIZE Request

UPTIMIZE Request allow users to modify platform configuration, such as changing the default role or create new compass role with elevated permissions.
Each create action can only be triggered by Use Case Owners (Business Owner, Product Owner and Technical Owner).

## E-Mail Notifications

The notification is defined in the base object actions. 
The 'create,' 'succeed,' and 'process_failed' actions are configured with notifications. While the 'create' and 'process_failed' actions send emails to the approvers prompting action, the 'succeed' email serves as a receipt for the requesting user.

## Extension Type

### Project Default Role Change

The request 'project default role change" empowers Use Case Owners to configure the default role of a Use Case project. When choosing Viewer or Editor the project will become public.
Once the project is public, every user gets access to all resources (e.g. datasets, analysis, dashboards, ...) within this project. Details on the roles can be found here: [Projects & Roles](https://palantir.mcloud.merckgroup.com/docs/foundry/security/projects-and-roles/#roles)

### Additional Compass Role

#### Introduction

The request type 'additional compass role' empowers Use Case Owners to configure new compass roles for a project linked to the Use Case. Based on the sector and its compass role configurations (see [Compass Role Configuration Workshop](https://docs.uptimize.merckgroup.com/foundry/use-case-portal/uptimize-request/#compass-role-configuration-workshop)), a new group is created. This group is then initialized with the requested role(s) and the group setup configuration, derived from the sector configurations.

#### The Concept of Default and Custom Compass Role Sector Configuration

When a new request is generated for a sector-specific Use Case and Project, the system examines the compass role configuration objects to determine if an object is configured for the pair of sector and each of the requested roles. If the specific role included in the request is not configured, the system defaults to creating editor-plus groups for that role-request with the setup defined in the default-configuration object. However, in the presence of a configuration object, the process creates a custom group named &lt;project-name&gt;-&lt;compass-role&gt; and subsequently grants this group requested roles to the project.

<a name="compass-role-configuration-workshop"></a>
#### Compass Role Configuration Workshop
The purpose of the configuration object is to enable the sectors to have distinct setups for different requested roles. A workshop was created for the SDAOs to configure their objects. You can access the workshop [here](https://palantir.mcloud.merckgroup.com/workspace/module/view/latest/ri.workshop.main.module.f8bf0d96-60d8-4944-bdce-1898e96edc05).

<img src="/assets/uptimize-request/configuration_object_workshop.png" alt="Configuration Object Workshop" width="80%"/>

### Custom Multipass Group

#### Introduction

The Uptimize Request Type 'custom multipass group' empowers Use Case Owners to create additional multipass groups with no access level for a project linked to the Use Case . Based on the sector and its custom multipass group configurations (see [Configuration Workshop](https://palantir.mcloud.merckgroup.com/workspace/module/view/latest/ri.workshop.main.module.f8bf0d96-60d8-4944-bdce-1898e96edc05))a new custom group with no access level is created with the naming structure **<use case projectName>-custom-group-<requested suffix>** . This group is then available on the in the use case access request groups for the underlying project with the group setup configuration, derived from the sector configurations.

#### How To Submit a Custom Multipass Group Request For Use Cases

* Use Case owners will be able to request custom multipass groups through the request manager on the Use Case portal [use case portal](https://palantir.mcloud.merckgroup.com/workspace/module/view/latest/ri.workshop.main.module.cfbd54d9-5f5e-4c67-a94d-37fc842812cc/personal). 

  <img src="/assets/uptimize-request/custom_multipass_group_instruction.png" alt="Custom Multipass Group Instruction" width="80%"/>

  1. Select the Use Case project where the group will be used.

  2. Provide the desired suffix for your custom multipass group.

  3. State the reason for the requested custom multipass and submit.

  Note: If the custom multipass group request is approved, the group will be created with the format **<projectName>-custom-group-<suffix>** (e.g: **ls-use-case-ace-custom-group-emea**) and will be available in the list of project groups when requesting access to the linked use case project.

#### How To Submit a Custom Multipass Group Request For DTIs

* DTI owners will be able to request custom multipass groups through the request manager on the Data Treasury [data treasury](https://palantir.mcloud.merckgroup.com/workspace/module/view/latest/ri.workshop.main.module.10e9a51d-489e-4610-b6ce-e93a1bc66912/home). 

  <img src="/assets/uptimize-request/dti_custom_multipass_group_instruction.png" alt="DTI Custom Multipass Group Instruction" width="80%"/>

  1. Select the DTI Ontology project where the group will be used.

  2. Provide the desired suffix for your custom multipass group.

  3. State the reason for the requested custom multipass and submit.

  Note: If the custom multipass group request is approved, the group will be created with the format **<OntologyProjectName>-custom-group-<suffix>** (e.g: **ls-ontology-arehs-custom-group-emea**) and the DTI Owners get a notification.

---

# Use Case Decommission Process 2.0
As part of the Use Case Lifecycle, the final status of a Use Case is 'Decommissioned.' This status indicates that the Use Case is no longer required and has been officially retired from active service. It is no longer maintained or supported for regular operations.

- Prior to July 2024: The decommissioning process was performed manually by the Operations Team, involving a series of specific operations. A comprehensive description of these steps can be found here. These operations would take roughly 30 minutes to complete.
- Starting July 2024: The Use Case Decommission Process 2.0 is fully automated. Use Case owners will simply execute an Ontology action, and all steps will be carried out automatically, leveraging Foundry API with API Extender and Ontology to automate the decommission tasks and the logging of the operations. The Ontology action is available in UC summary view by UC owners, who can review, accept, and execute the action that will perform all operations tasks (presented below), log results, and send a notification with the result of the operation.

## How to Decommission a Use Case?
As a Use Case Owner, the process will change very little:  
1.   Navigate to the summarized view of the Use Case in the Use Case Portal  
2.   Click on the 'more' blue button on the right  
3.   Click on "Decommission Use Case"

![capture1](/assets/use-case-decommission/img1.png)

After clicking on "Decommission Use Case", an Action Form will be displayed:

-   List of the operations that will be executed
-   "Decommission Use Case" confirmation button
-   Remove markings warning
-   Reason For Decommissioning input field
-   Decommissioned Date field

![capture2](/assets/use-case-decommission/action-form3.png)

![capture3](/assets/use-case-decommission/action-form2.png)

When filling all fields and clicking in 'Decommossion Use Case' it will execute all the actions mentioned in the warning section which are:  
1.  **Remove Schedules:** All scheduled tasks and jobs associated with the project's datasets will be removed.  
2.  **Health Checks and Close Issues:** Active Health Checks will be removed, and all Open Issues within the project's datasets will be closed.  
3.  **Trash Datasets:** The project's datasets will be sent to the trash and will be permanently deleted 30 days after being trashed.  
4.  **Remove Branches:** All branches in the code repositories, except for the master branch, will be removed.  
5.  **Reject Pending Access Requests:** Any pending Access Requests (Access Requests and Data Provisioning Access Requests) related to the Use Case will be rejected.  
6.  **Revoke Finished Data Provisioning Access Requests:** Any 'done' Data Provisioning Access Request will be revoked and an Unprovisioning Request will be sent to stop the provisioning to the UC project folder.  
7.  **Manage Groups:**  
    -   **Process Viewer & Editor Groups:** Editor project group will be deleted and their members will be added to the Viewer group.  
    -   **Update Owner Group:** All members will be removed from the owner groups, and the Operations Team will be added.
    -   **Add Global Audit Viewer Group:** As viewer for auditing purposes. 
    -   **Remove uncompliant Groups:** All uncompliant groups will be removed from having access to the projects.
As such, please expect to take a while (around 30 seconds) for all the actions to be completed. When completed, you will see a green banner like this one:

![banner](/assets/use-case-decommission/banner.png)

If everything went well, Use Case Owners will receive an email like this one:

![capture4](/assets/use-case-decommission/successful-decommission.png)

## In case of failure
-   If the action failed and a red banner pops up:  
    -   If error says 'Timeout error' execute the action again and it should work  
    -   In any other case, please raise an issue in the Foundry Issues App 
-   If the action succeeded but UC is not moved to 'Decommissioned' status  
    -   UC owner will recieve a notification informing the process failed  
    -   Operations team will recieve a notification with the detailed checks that have failed  
    -   Failed checks can be consulted in a new section of the UC Portal Admin page 'Failed Decommission'

![capture5](/assets/use-case-decommission/decommission-failure.png)

![capture6](/assets/use-case-decommission/decommission-failure-ops.png)

## Dependency handling in Decommissioning

When a Use Case (UC1) expires and is scheduled for decommissioning, but it is still being used by another Use Case (UC2), the decommissioning will be temporarily paused.

As the Owner of the consumer Use Case (UC2):

- You will see a red alert banner in the Use Case Portal:

![capture7](/assets/use-case-decommission/expired_uc_button.png)  

- By clicking on this alert, an overlay window will open. This overlay lists all expired Use Cases that your Use Case depends on.

![capture8](/assets/use-case-decommission/take_action.png)  

- In this overlay, you can take the following actions for each expired Use Case:

  - Retain Use Case - Your Use Case needs the resource from the expired Use case.

  - No Longer Needed - Acknowledge that your Use Case no longer requires the expired Use Case. UC1 continues with decommissioning.

  - Do Nothing - If no action is taken, the expired Use Case will remain blocked from decommissioning until an action is taken.

- UC2 owners will **regularly receive reminders** about pending dependencies until they take action.

---

# Use Case Object View

### Overview
Governance object types--such as use cases--have grown increasingly complex and difficult to navigate in their current form. The legacy application Hubble has added to this complexity, highlighting the need for a more modern solution.

To address these challenges, core governance features have been migrated from Hubble to the new Workshop interface. This transition enables the creation of a more intuitive and user-friendly experience, with a redesigned layout that improves information clarity and navigation.

Following the redesign, usability testing will ensure the new interface aligns with user needs, ultimately supporting a more efficient and accessible governance framework.

### Data Access
![Data Accesss](/assets/use-case-object-views/DataAccess.png)
In the updated interface, the previous "Data" and "Data Access" tabs have been merged into a single, streamlined "Data Access" tab. This new view organizes information into separate, clearly labeled tables, each corresponding to a different object type, making it easier to navigate and understand data access elements related to a use case.
The tab includes individual tables for:
- Treasury items linked to the use case
- Treasury items associated with the data ingestion request
- Linked Data Enhancement Requests (DER)
- Linked Data Ingestion Requests (DIR)
- Linked Data Access Requests

Additionally, Action buttons are located at the top of the tab, providing quick access to the following functions:
- Requesting a new Data Ingestion Request (DIR)
- Checking use case consumption metrics
- Accessing the [Data Treasury Portal] directly

#### Use Case Access Request
![Usecase Accesss](/assets/use-case-object-views/usecaseaccessrequest.png)
The Use Case Access Request tab has been migrated to Workshop with its structure and content preserved. While the functionality remains the same, the updated interface offers a more modern and consistent user experience.

**Open Access Requests**
- Displays all open access requests associated with the use case
- Includes a search bar to help locate specific requests
- Also shows legacy open access requests carried over from the previous system

**Completed Access Requests**
- Lists all completed access requests related to the use case

**User Access Overview**
- Displays all users with "Read" or "Edit" access to the use case
- Includes a search field and a button to export the user list in Excel format for further analysis
- Provides a direct link to the full User Access Report

This tab ensures continuity of access management while leveraging the improved usability of the Workshop environment.

### History
![History](/assets/use-case-object-views/historytab.png)
The History tab has been migrated to Workshop, maintaining its structure and content. It continues to provide visibility into the creation and modification history of a use case.
- **Use Case Properties**
    - Displays key metadata, including:
        - Who created the use case and when
        - Who last modified the use case and when

- **Edit History**
    - Lists all changes made to the use case since its creation
    - Entries are shown in reverse chronological order, with the most recent updates at the top

This tab helps users track the lifecycle of a use case and understand how it has evolved over time.

### UC Assessment
![UC Assessment](/assets/use-case-object-views/uc-assessment.png)
The UC Assessment tab has been migrated to Workshop, maintaining its structure and content. This tab is only visible to use case admins and provides insight into the outcomes of assessments conducted by ACE product owners via the Use Case Assessment Tool.

The tab includes the following elements:
- **Assessment Outcomes**
    Displays the results of the latest use case assessment, including the assessment date and the following KPIs:
        1. **Priority** : Calculated as Value × Ease of Implementation (EoI).
        2. **Value** : A weighted combination of several factors, including:
        Revenue Potential, Innovativeness, Cost Saving, Affected Users Applicability, Time Saving, Margin Potential, Product Portfolio Synergies, Number of Potential Unique Monthly Users, Stakeholder Job and Process Impact, Learning Potential, Brand Image, Strategic Fit, and Analytical Maturity.
        3. **Ease of Implementation (EoI)** : Based on technical and organizational complexity, including Problem Understanding, Scalability, Data Model Complexity, Data Availability and Freshness, Product Portfolio Integration Effort, Analytical Complexity, Frontend Efforts, Post-Implementation Effort, Regulatory and Ethical Considerations, and Use Case Type.

- **Admin Actions**
    - A button allowing use case admins to initiate or update an assessment

- **Support Contact** 
    - Contact details for inquiries related to the use case or its assessment

This tab helps admins evaluate and prioritize use cases based on strategic value and implementation feasibility.
        
### Additional files
![Additional files](/assets/use-case-object-views/additional-files.png)
The Additional Files tab has been migrated to Workshop, maintaining its structure and content. It serves as a central place to **upload and store files** that are related to the use case or may provide additional context or value.

Users can attach supporting documentation, reference materials, or any other relevant files to keep all use case information in one accessible location.

### Data Externalization
![Data externalization](/assets/use-case-object-views/DXR.png)
The Data Externalization tab has been migrated to Workshop, maintaining its structure and content. This tab is only visible to use case admins and is used to manage data externalization requests.
The tab includes the following functionality:
    - Request a new data externalization directly from the interface.
    - View any pending externalization requests associated with the use case.

The page also reminds users to review existing pending requests before submitting a new one, to help avoid duplicate externalization efforts.

### Product Enhancement Request
![Product](/assets/use-case-object-views/productenhancement.png)
The Product Enhancement Request tab has been migrated to Workshop, maintaining its structure and content. It is only visible for use cases in the healthcare sector.
This tab provides:
    - The ability for users to submit enhancement requests related to the use case.
    - A list of all enhancement requests previously submitted for the use case.

Before proposing a new use case enhancement, users are encouraged to review the existing enhancement requests listed on the page. This helps ensure that the enhancement being considered has not already been initiated.

---

# Use Case Compliance Badge
The goal of the Use Case Compliance Badge is to give Use Case owners a quick, easy, and clear way of checking the compliance of their Use Case resources. A Use Case consists of several resources that all need to be compliant in order for the whole Use Case to be deemed compliant. Most notably, a Use Case will usually have at least one Project linked to it, which itself has User Groups linked.
The information about the Use Case compliance is captured by the Ontology Object Type of the same name. This Object is linked to the original Use Case as well as to Project Compliance Objects if there are any Projects linked to the Use Case.
The Compliance Badge is displayed in the Use Case Portal, which is where Use Case Owners will generally interact with their Use Cases. It is displayed in the top right corner of the Use Case View and shows one out of three statuses:

Green "Compliant" → All checks are passing
Red "Non Compliant" → At least one check is not passing in the Use Case or any linked Project
Yellow "Check Compliance" → Compliance has never been checked. This should only be the case for newly created Use Cases until the daily pipeline updating the Compliance Objects is run the next time.
![overview](/assets/use-case-lifecycle/use-case-compliance-badge.png)
The Badge is only visible to Use Case Owners of a specific Use Case or MDO admins. Clicking on the three dots next to the Badge will reveal more information, especially a summary of failing checks if there are any. This summary is created using a TypeScript function.
![overview](/assets/use-case-lifecycle/use-case-compliance-info.png)
From here, the Detailed Compliance Report can be reached by clicking the respective button. This report allows users to get even more details for each individual check and how to fix anything that is failing.
![overview](/assets/use-case-lifecycle/use-case-compliance-details.png)

---

# AI Governance for Use Cases in Foundry

The EU Artificial Intelligence Act (AI Act) is the European Union's comprehensive regulatory framework designed to ensure that AI systems placed on the EU market or used within the EU are safe, trustworthy, and respect fundamental rights. Adopted in 2024, it represents the world's first major horizontal AI regulation, setting clear obligations based on the risk level associated with an AI system. The Act applies not only to organizations established within the EU, but also to providers and deployers outside the EU whose AI systems affect people within the EU. This broad territorial scope ensures accountability throughout the AI value chain, regardless of geographic location.

## AI self-asessment
This self-assessment is designed to help users to:

* Identify their role under the EU AI Act (i.e. provider or deployer). 
* Determine the risk classification of their AI system.
* Understand the compliance obligations that may apply.

## AI Governance Tool
To get an overview of all the AI Use Cases and GEAR applications in Merck or to the ones you are responsible for, you can use the [AI Governance Tool](https://palantir.mcloud.merckgroup.com/workspace/module/view/latest/ri.workshop.main.module.6a01df64-68aa-4f54-9ebc-8e336b907c3e/user) and switch to either "Dashboard" or "Personal View".

### When do I need to take the self-assessment?
**Use Cases**
During the creation and transition to each stage in the lifecycle of Use Case, you will be asked to answer a question on if your Use Case uses AI and the type of AI. **If anwsered "Yes" to AI usage**, the Business Owner of the Use Case will recieve a link to fill the self-assessment form.

**GEAR Applications**
If a GEAR application has AI Flag set to true then the Service Delivery Manager should get the mail with the link to the self-assessment. In case there is no Service Delivery Manager assigned, the mail will be sent to the Business Owner.

The notification for Use Cases is sent out immideately whereas for the GEAR applications, it is a daily run.

### How can I get to the self-assessment from the Use Case portal?
To go to the self-assessment for your AI Use Case, you can go to your Use Case and switch to the "AI Assessment" tab. If you would like to get an overview of all your Use Cases, then you also use the AI Governance Tool application mentioned in previous section.

### What if we decide to no longer use AI?
If you set the AI Flag to False, the status for the self-assessment will be set to "Not Required" in case of both Use Cases as well GEAR applications. For Use Cases, in addition to this, the "AI Assessment" tab is hidden(also if it is Decommissioned).

### Who can submit the self-assessment?
**Use Cases**
Any of the Use Case owner can submit the assessment

**GEAR Application**
The self-assessment can be submitted either by Service Delivery Manager or Business Owner.

> **Important Notes:**<br> 1. Monthly reminders will be sent out to the Business Owner/ Service Delivery Manager if the self-assessment has not begun.<br>2. In case you need support with the self-assessment, reach out to your business partner or SDAO in case of Use Cases and Service Delivery Manager/Business Owner or contact the supplier of the solution in case of GEAR Application. If it's a bug with the self-assessment or the AI Governance Tool, raise a Foundry issue.

---

# Use Case Price Tag

### Introduction
As part of the Cost Transparency initiative, a new feature has been introduced in the Use Case Portal to display the monthly costs associated with each use case. This feature is designed to provide use case owners and SDAOs with a clear understanding of their costs, promoting better financial decision-making. Additionally, we are introducing the Foundry Daily Cost, which shows the cumulative cost month to date only for foundry. Access to the Price Tag feature is restricted to use case owners and SDAOs. If others wish to view the data, they must submit an access request for the selected preset.

### Overview of the Price Tag feature
![overview](/assets/use-case-pricetag/price_tag_daily-overview.png)
In the Use Case summary view, a cost tag is displayed, offering a quick reference to the previous month's cost. Users can click the tag to open a detailed overlay that provides comprehensive cost information.

### Detailed Overlay Information
![overlay](/assets/use-case-pricetag/price_tag_overview_updated.png)
The detailed overlay consists of several tabs:
1.	Overview Tab: Displays a summary of costs.
2.	Platform Tabs: Each platform (e.g., Foundry, AWS, Snowflake, App Service, AI/ML) has its own tab.
3.	Use Case Cost Distribution Tab: Compares the use case cost with all other use cases on the platform.

### 1. Overview Tab
The Overview tab is divided into two sections:
- Monthly Trend Tab: Displays the cost trend across all platforms.
- Cost per Platform Tab: Shows how the total cost is distributed across each platform without further detail.

### 2. Platform Cost Breakdown
![platfrom](/assets/use-case-pricetag/platfrom_cost_breakdown.png)
Each platform tab includes the following sub-tabs:
- Cost Category: Displays the cost breakdown for categories used in the platform for the use case.
- Service: Shows the cost generated by each service used in the platform. Users can filter the cost breakdown by category and project (or account) and compare service costs for two different months.
- Projects/Accounts: Provides the cost breakdown per project or account associated with the use case.

### 3. Cost Comparison Chart
![comparison](/assets/use-case-pricetag/costcomparision.png)
The final tab of the Price Tag Overlay helps use case owners understand how their use case ranks relative to others in terms of monthly cost. It categorizes spending into discrete cost segments, giving an overview of how much their use case consumes compared to others on the platform.

### Currency Selection
Users can select the currency in which they want to view the data, currently available in USD and EUR for a more personalized experience.

### Month Selection
By default, the data shown in the Price Tag Overlay corresponds to the previous month. Users have the option to select a different time period.

### Resource Management Integration
In the Foundry tab, a button labeled "View in Resource Management" allows owners to select the use case project and view detailed cost explanations in the Resource Management application.

![currency](/assets/use-case-pricetag/price_tag_month.png)

### Conclusion
The Price Tag feature is a significant enhancement to the Use Case Portal, providing essential cost insights and analytical tools. By utilizing this feature, use case owners can improve their understanding of costs and make informed financial decisions. For more information, please refer to the Cost Transparency initiative.

---

# Use Case Enhancement

This feature allows defining enhancements for Use Cases that are already in Industrialization status. It can be used to track additional developments done to the core Use Case logic and that do not require an additional Use Case to get created. It adds visibility and transparency on additional improvements and new functionalities added to a Use Case once it is industrialized.

## Enhancement Lifecycle

![Enhancement Lifecycle Diagram](/assets/use-case-enhancement/UC_Enhancement_Full_Workflow.png)

The lifecycle for an enhancement goes through several phases reflecting the enhancement development status. When moved to any of the statuses, automated notifications are configured as described in the diagram to keep the requestor and owners informed about the lifecycle changes.
The diagram shows how these statuses are interconnected. Further details on each status can be found below.

#### Creation

Each user with editor access to a Use Case can submit a Use Case Enhancement Request. To do so, they must open the desired Use Case in the Use Case Portal, go to the "Use Case Enhancements" tab and click on "Request Use Case Enhancement" button. After fulfilling the provided information in the form, a notification will be sent to the Use Case Owners to review the request.

The form allows defining new owners for the enhancement (by default, the Use Case owners will be used), and after the enhancement gets approved, they will be responsible for managing the enhancement through its lifecycle.

Additionally, the requestor needs to submit whether a new project is required to develop this enhancement. By selecting Yes, a new project request will be submitted automatically but following the project request procedure after approval. The new project will be linked to both the Use Case and the Enhancement and will use the enhancement name as a suffix. If no porject is requested at this stage, enhancements development must be hnadled in the existing parent Use Case projects.

#### Approval/Rejection

After enhancement creation, Use Case owners decide whether they want to approve the request. If they approve the request, a notification will be sent to the designated Enhancement owners (Use Case owners by default) informing them about the approval. If a project was requested for this Use Case Enhancement, a new Project Request will be submitted, SDAO members will be notified, and they will be able to approve the corresponding project creation. The created project will use the enhancement name as a suffix and will be linked to the original Use Case too.

If the request gets rejected, the requestor user will be notified, including a comment about the rejection.

For EL Use Cases, approval needs to be handled by the EL Portfolio team, and therefore, they will be notified after the enhancement is submitted. For rejecting, both UC owners or EL Portfolio team members can do so.

#### Work In Progress

Once the request gets approved, and the project gets created in case it was requested, owners can move the enhancement to Work In Progress status. This effectively means that developments to achieve the enhancement's goal are ongoing.

#### On Hold

While the enhancement is in Work In Progress status, owners can move it to "On Hold" status to indicate a pause in the enhancement development works. While being in this status, the enhancement can always be moved back to Work In Progress status.

#### Released

This status indicates that the developments covered by the enhancement are completed and the outcomes have been released. After moving to this status, a Product Outcome can be linked to the enhancement by owners.

#### Discarded

Moving to this status means that the goal of the enhancement is no longer needed or is not going to be fulfilled.

#### Closed

This is a special status only for Electronics Use Case Enhancements, which can only be set by the EL Portfolio team for Approved or WIP Enhancements and that is needed before moving to released or discarded these enhancements. It indicates that the FTE allocation to this enhancement is no longer allowed.

## Use Case Product Outcome Integration

When an enhancement reaches Released status, owners can define a new Product and link it to both the Enhancement and the Use Case.
The product form mirrors the existing one for Use Cases. Once the product is added it will appear in the Use Case Outcomes section, additionally tagged to the specific Enhancement.

## Project Request Integrations

At request creation, users can select whether to leverage the existing Use Case project or request a new one.
If a new project is requested, the project request is created only after Use Case owners approve the enhancement.
Project creation follows the standard process and requires SDAO approval.
Governance remains unchanged: Use Case owners submit requests; SDAO teams approve project creation.

## UI Details

All existing enhancements, as well as their current statuses, can be viewed in the Use Case Enhancements tab in the Use Case View.

![Use Case Enhancements Tab View](/assets/use-case-enhancement/uc-enhancements-view.png)

Each item in the list displays the enhancement's details when clicked. On top of the lifecycle section, buttons to move the enhancement through the lifecycle will be appearing depending on the status. Linked outcomes after release can also be found in the enhancement's view:

![Enhancement Details View](/assets/use-case-enhancement/uc-enhancement-object-view.png)

Linked outcomes after release can also be found in the enhancement's view:

![Enhancement Linked Outcomes](/assets/use-case-enhancement/uc-enhancement-product-outcome.png)

## Business Value

- Improves visibility of connected Use Cases and their various implementations.
- Prevents duplication of information while maintaining the relationship between original Use Cases and their enhancements.
- Enables better tracking of Use Case evolution and implementation across different sites.
- Provides a more organized structure for managing complex Use Cases with multiple enhancements.
- Allows for proper resource planning and allocation for enhancement work, which requires separate tracking from the original Use Case.
- Ensures consistent resource management across both Use Cases and their enhancements within the UPTIMIZE ecosystem.

---

# How to get data into your use case

<ld-notice headline="Information">
  The following rules will be fully implemented by <b>end of March 2026</b> as part of closing a crucial audit finding on strengthening use case life cycle security and comliance. While all rules are already valid today, not all enforcement mechanisms will be in place.<br>

  This page serves therefore as a heads up for use case owners.


</ld-notice>

## From Data Treasury 
The most straightforward and safe way for use case owners to obtain data is via

* [Data Access Requests (DAR)](foundry/access-management/dti/request-access/) for existing data or
* [Data Ingestion Requests (DIR) and Data Enhancement Requests (DER)](foundry/data-treasury-portal/data-ingestion-enhancement/DIR-DER/) for new data

out of our curated Data Treasury.

<ld-notice headline="Access without DAR" mode="error"> It is not allowed to use treasurized data <b>without</b> DAR. This also includes importing treasurized data of another use case using treasurized data. </ld-notice>

<table>
<thead>
<tr>
<th>Action</th>
<th style="white-space: nowrap;">Permission</th>
<th>Consequence</th>
</tr>
</thead>
<tbody>
<tr>
<td>Dataset from DTI with Access Request (DAR)</td>
<td style="white-space: nowrap;">✅ Allowed</td>
<td>Safe and compliant access to data</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>Dataset from DTI without Access Request (DAR)</td>
<td style="white-space: nowrap;">🚫 Forbidden</td>
<td>Use case becomes incompliant. After two weeks reference will be removed.</td>
</tr>
</tbody>
</table>

## From manual upload 

You can upload directly into your data folder: Use Case Owners are responsible that they have
the rights to use this data in their use cases: In particular, they need to be aware that anyone having acess to the use case, may then access this data.

<table>
<thead>
<tr>
<th>Action</th>
<th style="white-space: nowrap;">Permission</th>
<th>Consequence</th>
</tr>
</thead>
<tbody>
<tr>
<td>Upload data directly into your data folder</td>
<td style="white-space: nowrap;">✅ Allowed</td>
<td>Use case owner is responsible for data rights and compliance with intended purpose of source data.</td>
</tr>
</tbody>
</table>

##  From another Use Case 

It is possible to directly import data of another use case. This comes with certain risks that the use case owners need to accept, when proceeding with this:

1. There is no formal access management process. Use case owners are responsible that this is compliant with the intended use of the data.
1. There is no guarantees for data quality, specifically data quality necessary for the needs of your use case.
1. The data producing use case may expire or get decommissioned at any time, since there is no obligation for the producing use case to maintain their use case indefinitely. This means, that your use case may use *stale, inconsistent or incomplete* data, when this happens.

<table>
<thead>
<tr>
<th>Action</th>
<th style="white-space: nowrap;">Permission</th>
<th>Consequence</th>
</tr>
</thead>
<tbody>
<tr>
<td>Import data from an expired or decommissioned use case</td>
<td style="white-space: nowrap;">🚫 Forbidden</td>
<td>Use case becomes incompliant; direct references removed automatically at decommissioning.</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>Import data from a non-Industrialized use case</td>
<td style="white-space: nowrap;">⚠️ Discouraged</td>
<td>Compliance warning raised on your use case</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>Import data from an incompliant (*) use case</td>
<td style="white-space: nowrap;">🚫 Forbidden</td>
<td>Compliance issue raised on your use case: Your use case becomes incompliant.</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>Import data from a compliant Industrialized use case</td>
<td style="white-space: nowrap;">⚠️ Allowed with risks</td>
<td>Use case owner accepts risks of other use case getting decommmissioned.</td>
</tr>
</tbody>
</table>


(*) Not all incompliancy issues are inheritable (e.g. wrong namespace incompliancy is not inherited), however mission-critical issues such as No or Failing Health Checks, Missing Access Request are inheritable and will result in downstream use cases failing.

## From a data source or transform project 

It is **discouraged** for use cases to directly use data from

* a data source- or
* transform-

project, since it circumvents the governance procedures that are in place for DTIs.
Instead, the data is supposed to be used via the finished data treasury item / Data Access request.

<table>
<thead>
<tr>
<th>Action</th>
<th style="white-space: nowrap;">Permission</th>
<th>Consequence</th>
</tr>
</thead>
<tbody>
<tr>
<td>Use data directly from a data source project</td>
<td style="white-space: nowrap;">⚠️ Discouraged</td>
<td>Compliance warning raised on your use case</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>Use data directly from a transform project</td>
<td style="white-space: nowrap;">⚠️ Discouraged</td>
<td>Compliance warning raised on your use case</td>
</tr>
</tbody>
</table>

Foundry Platform Infrastructure use cases are exempt for this rule.

#  <font size =6> Automated Role Assignment for Use Case Driven Objects </font>

**<i><span style="color:#0F69AF">What is Automated Role Assignment for Use Case driven Objects?</span></i>**

<div style="text-align: justify">Automated Role Assignment for Use Case (UC) driven Objects does the following by running a periodic scheduled script: for a Use Case driven object, UC project user groups are assigned corresponding ontology roles on the Object. The editor user group is assigned the ontology editor role, the viewer user group is assigned the ontology viewer role and the owner user group is assigned the ontology owner role.  Also, any existing Object level specific user access is revoked to ensure the access to the Object is maintained through UC user groups only. Any other existing user group access on the Object is not changed and remains as it is.</div>

<div style="text-align: justify">Once the role assignment is completed for an Object, an email notification is sent to the users whose specific user access was revoked. Also, an email notification is sent to the UC owner summarizing the role assignment & specific user access revocation details at the end of the day.</div>

The role assignment process is scheduled to run every 3 hours.

**<i><span style="color:#0F69AF">How does the Automated Role Assignment Process help?</span></i>**

- It's a scheduled role assignment process, so any Object created for a use case is assigned owner, editor, viewer groups in an automated manner with no manual intervention.
- Sector admin owners and editors inherit access rights from sector_use_case_member groups (e.g. ls-use-case-editor-member) enabling them to administrate all the Objects at the sector level.
- Object Access is governed by UC User groups via the Use Case Portal, so no manual access maintenance is needed at the Object level. 
- No more being blocked in editing an Ontology Object when the Object Owner is out of office, as all members of the Use Case editor group will have Editor access to the Ontology Object.

**<i><span style="color:#0F69AF">What is a Use Case driven Object?</span></i>**

A Use Case driven Object is an Ontology Object for which the backing dataset is located in the Use Case Project space.

**<i><span style="color:#0F69AF">Role Assignment Example:</span></i>**

Following is an example of security detail of an Object Type after the Role assignment process is completed. <br></br>
![object_type_roles](https://docs.uptimize.merckgroup.com/docs-assets/foundry/Images/automated_roles/object_type_roles.png)

<div style="text-align: justify">In the screenshot above, '[EF] Backing Dataset' is an Object Type with backing dataset located in the UC Project space of the UC 'Ontology Objects Metadata Analytics'. The role assignment process identifies the Object Type as a UC driven Object and assigns the UC User groups corresponding roles on the Object. The editor user group is assigned the Ontology editor role, the viewer user group is assigned the Ontology viewer role and the owner user group is assigned the Ontology owner role.</div>

 **<i><span style="color:#0F69AF">Object Type - Role Assignment Process</span></i>**<br></br>
![Object Type - Role Assignment Process](assets/ontology/ObjectType_RoleAssignment.png)

**<i><span style="color:#0F69AF">Link Type - Role Assignment Process</span></i>**<br></br>
![Link Type - Role Assignment Process](assets/ontology/LinkType_RoleAssignment.png)

**<i><span style="color:#0F69AF">Action Type - Role Assignment Process</span></i>**<br></br>
![Action Type - Role Assignment Process](assets/ontology/ActionType_RoleAssignment.png)

**<i><span style="color:#0F69AF">Things to note</span></i>**

- When the process is released, first run will consider all existing UC driven object types, link types, action types (OT/LT/AT) in Foundry and flag them as Roles assigned after successful Role assignment.
- Subsequent runs will consider OT/LT/AT for which Roles have not been assigned yet.
- Only following OT/LT/AT are considered for the Role assignment process:
  - OT/LT/AT that have been migrated to roles. For the OT/LT/AT not migrated to roles yet, those will be considered in the next scheduled run of the Role assignment once they are migrated to roles.
  - OT/LT/AT with only Active or Experimental status. Objects in Deprecated status are not considered.
- For OT with OSV2 storage type - Project spaces of all the backing datasets are considered for the Role assignment process. For e.g. If there are two separate project spaces for the datasets, then 6 UC user groups (3 for each project space) are assigned.
- Only the Project space where the OT backing dataset(s) is located is considered for the Role assignment process even if there are other Projects in the UC. This is to ensure only the UC User groups for required Project space from the UC have access to OT.
- In case, Project space for the backing dataset of an OT changes, the OT will be considered in the next Role Assignment run for revised assignments.
- For LT Role assignment, in case the 2 OTs are from different UC, User groups from both UC will be assigned to LT.
- For AT Role assignment, in case the associated OTs are from different UC, User groups from all UC will be assigned to AT.

**<i><span style="color:#0F69AF">Additional Rules implemented for the SDOs</span></i>**

Following additional rules have been implemented as requested by the SDO Admins:

| **Sector**    |**Rules**|
|:--------------------------------------------------------------------|:---------------|
| Life Science | Exclude from Automated Role Assignment for OT/LT/AT if they belong to use case  - "Regulatory & Compliance Data Validation and Feasibility Assessment status".
| MDAO  | Exclude from Automated Role Assignment for OT/LT/AT if they belong to use cases - "Data Treasury" & "Use Case Portal 2"
|Electronics|Role Assignment process to also add the el-ontology-(objects/actions/links)-owner (el-ontology-objects-owner, el-ontology-actions-owner, el-ontology-links-owner) group as owner of the object/action/link type respectively.
|Enabling Functions|If the use case project space backing the OT/LT/AT starts with 'mgf-po', exclude those Objects from Automated Role Assignment and assign following groups<br>mgf-po-ontology-team -> owner</br><br>foundry-gov-team -> owner</br><br>global-audit-viewer -> viewer</br><br>Excluded from Automated Role Assignment for MGF Finance use case - Only one project exists "mgf-use-case-mc4f-grip-dashboard". Object types: "[EF-FI-POC] Build Status Test" & "[EF-FI-POC] Resource Capacity Tracker".<br><br>New groups created for above 2 OTs - "ef-ontology-owners" & "ef-finance-ontology-editors" .<br><br>Assigned "ef-ontology-owners" group to object type's OWNER Role and "ef-finance-ontology-editors" group to object type's EDITOR Role.

In case of any questions related to the process, please create an issue in the [Foundry Issue App](https://palantir.mcloud.merckgroup.com/workspace/issues-app/). You can also reach out to Neerav Kumar <neerav.kumar@milliporesigma.com> or Thiagarajan Nagalingam <thiagarajan.nagalingam@merckgroup.com>.

For questions related to additional rules implemented for SDOs, please reach out to the SDO Admins.

# Employee Ontology Toolkit

An ontology provides a shared source of truth that allows easy discovery and understanding of data within Merck, while reducing complexity of managing transformation for each use case. The Foundry Ontology is not linked to any open standards, however, as Merck develops a true business driven ontology which may be linked to open standards, it we should be able to map the Foundry specific Employee objects to the Merck ontology.  

The decision to introduce an Employee ontology at this point was driven by business demand and the need to replace an existing Employee ontology that was created based on a dataset from an old HR data warehouse that is due to be decommissioned. 

## Overview / Introduction for Employee and HR organizational objects

The Ontology was developed in close collaboration with business sectors, especially with Life Science consumers of the data, as Life Science has many existing use cases that utilise the Ontology. 

Other sector needs were considered and included as part of the requirements and the HR ontologies were developed with the FAIR principles. 

**Key Considerations and Challenges from HR governance perspective**

How do we structure the data in a general enough way to meet sector needs while considering "need to know"/data privacy needs 

To address this we have created 2 Ontology objects 
- Employee object - providing key Employee Profile information
- HR Organizational object - providing details about the HR organizational structure.  Can be linked to the Employee object using department code.

**Data Privacy**

We have introduced Policy based column and row level security allowing us to provide users with access to the information they need to develop their use case, without having to create separate data sets by sector. This has been enabled largely through support from the ACE team in Life Science, who researched and implemented this with our requirements and supported us through the implementation. 

- **Column level security**, by
    - Sensitivity 
    - Access to columns is driven by classification of data attributes by the Employee Profile data owner, classifying data into the following categories  
    - PII non-sensitive, non-sensitive internal, Merck-sensitive and PII sensitive. 
- **Row level security**, by 
    - Sector (LS, HC, EL, EF (LF included in EF) and 
    - Country (Germany/ Non-Germany based on Country of Location) 
        - This is driven by the need to obtain additional approval for use of data for German based employees a local co-determination body (ITK/ITC) 

 ## Employee Ontology Object

 The scope of the employee object currently includes only employees that are directly employed by Merck (external users are excluded as these are not available in our underlying system of record HR4Y/SAP Successfactors/EC) and only active users. (This means employees that are classed as dormant - I.e. longer term leave, such as maternity/paternity leave are also not included). 

Data is currently updated on a monthly basis, around the 4th business day.  

The following attributes are included in the Employee Ontology object. The underlying dataset is not currently linked to a data treasury item. The Employee object can be linked to HR Organizational Unit by Department ID. Employee links to itself via Line Manager ID as every Line Manager is also an employee.  

| **Attribute**  |**Sample**|**Data Sensitive**|
|:--------------------------------------------------------------------|:----------------------------|:----|
| Muid  | M220590 | Non-Sensitive PII 
| foundry_id  | 58b3aa06-c775-4bb2-8a8a-394717d7a2c1 | Non-Sensitive PII 
| foundry_id_ad_set   | []  | Non-Sensitive PII 
| position_id   | 1025318  | Non-Sensitive Internal 
| full_name  | JOAO COSTA  | Non-Sensitive PII 
| business_email | joao.costa@merckgroup.com  | Non-Sensitive PII

[Link to Employee Ontology](https://palantir.mcloud.merckgroup.com/workspace/ontology/object-type/employee/overview)

For users migrating from the Employee object set-up by Life Science team, it should be noted that the following attributes are no longer available 

- **HR Region** - There is currently a project in HR - R&A ecosystem is creating a new Regional Hierarchy based on Department structure. Enabling functions also provide access to Regional Hierarchies.  
- **Global Identifier 1, 2 and 3** - these attributes were level of an org structure encoded in an HR data warehouse to be decommissioned. The HR - R&A ecosystem is creating a new Organizational Hierarchy based on Department structure.  
It is anticipated to be included in the Organizational Unit Ontology object once available.  
- **Team Role** - this attribute is derived by Life Science and is not under ownership of HR. Life Science team will create this as an enrichment for their use cases. 

![ontologies](https://docs.uptimize.merckgroup.com/docs-assets/foundry/Images/hr_ontologies1.png)

## Understanding the requirements around protection/approvals required for Employee/Org Info Ontologies

Merck values the importance of protecting individuals' rights when processing their personal data. To ensure compliance and safeguard personal rights, Merck has effective privacy rules in place for collecting, using, and disclosing personal data. 

Data Privacy refers to protecting the interests of individuals and managing their personal data during collection, use, and disclosure. Personal data can be referred to as Personal Information (PI), Private Personal Information (PPI), or Personally Identifiable Information (PII). Data protection laws have two key elements; the rights of the individual and rules surrounding the processing of personal data. 

Further and more detailed information on the processes in place in Merck to support the compliance with Data Privacy Regulations and Internal policies can be accessed on the following sites. We would recommend to reach out to the HR Data Governance team, as we can consult and help guide consumers of HR data through the processes of gaining approval 

- [**Entitements/Data Access/Approval processes, ROPA/ITK**](https://mdigital.sharepoint.com/sites/HR_DataGovernance/SitePages/Data-Entitlements.aspx)
- [**UPTIMIZE - data availability/access/guidelines for developers**](https://mdigital.sharepoint.com/sites/HR_DataGovernance/SitePages/UPTIMIZE%20Request%20DTI%20Access.aspx)
- **Data Privacy - Contact details**
    - [Data Privacy Eva room](https://evarooms.merckgroup.com/Organization/LE-C/about)
    - Contacts - Presentation page 12 & 13
- [**Group Data Privacy Policy**](https://evarooms.merckgroup.com/Organization/LE-C/Pictures%20%20Documents/Data%20Privacy/01.%20Policies/Framework/Group%20Data%20Privacy%20Policy.pdf)
- You also need to check if **IT Security approval** is needed directly with [GPSEC_Consulting](mailto:GPSEC_Consulting@merckgroup.com)
- **ITK/ITC - Information Technology Kommittee** - co-determination  body in relation to processing of employee data where German employee data is concerned
    - [Link](https://evarooms.merckgroup.com/topic/itk/home)
- **OneTrust tool** to register use of data
    - [Link](https://app-de.onetrust.com/auth/login)

Please note that while the process may seem overwhelming, HRDG team has many templates available and experience in consulting and guiding teams through the process.  
However, if ITK is needed, the process to gain approval can take a while, since the ITK only meets on a monthly basis and documentation has to be submitted approximately 2 weeks prior to the actual meeting. 

## Access Requests process/additional information RBP

Access will initially managed by direct email request to the HRDG responsible team member for Foundry - [Ivonne Appleyard](mailto:ivonne.appleyard@merckgroup.com). 

This is due to the additional processes around providing access to Row and Column level security and the additional approval considerations ensuring that we comply with external and internal processes to protect PII and Merck sensitive data. 

Consumers should provide the following information. 

- Use Case/Business Need 
- Any approvals already existing (Data Privacy Approval, IT security, ITK). 
- Actual data attributes required - to support providing access to the correct attributes  
- If any mappings or enrichments are required or planned so that we can track these (we may be able to support provision or these). However, if we are not able to support provision, we would like to track these, so that we can inform users of impacts if there are changes planned to the underlying attributes. 

The information will then be reviewed by the HRDG team along with the business data owner/data steward and relevant access will be provided once all the required approvals have been gained. 

Usage will also be recorded in the HR Employee Data & Technology Approvals Repository for auditing purposes and easy access to relevant documentation. This is available internally on [SharePoint](https://mdigital.sharepoint.com/sites/HR_DataGovernance/SitePages/Employee-Data-&-Technology-Approvals.aspx)

## Data Quality

The HR Data Governance team has been working with HR data owners and data stewards to establish processes to manage data quality to increase trust in Employee data. 

Data Quality is measured for the most critical attributes for HR processes and details available to internal Merck employees. Data Quality issues can be reported directly to HR/MBS or through the standard UPTIMIZE foundry processes. 

More details about the processes in place to manage data quality can be accessed in the [HR Data Governance SharePoint](https://mdigital.sharepoint.com/sites/HR_DataGovernance/SitePages/Data-Quality.aspx)  and the Data Quality Health Dashboard can be access directly in [Tableau](https://mtableau.merckgroup.com/#/site/GFHumanResources/views/HRDataQualityHealthReporting_16512379378480/LandingPage?:iid=1).

## Working with the data

Use case owners must obtain appropriate data privacy approvals for use cases requiring personally identifiable information, while ensuring access rights, protections, and handling of HR data meet data retention and regulatory expectations. They are accountable for limiting data access, not sharing data beyond the specified use case, and reviewing user access bi-annually. Inactive use cases must be actively removed from Foundry, and ideation lasting for over a year will be reassessed. Data users with approved access must not download, share, or use HR data outside of the specific use case without proper approval. They must follow all guidelines for handling HR data documented in the policy. 

For further details, please refer to the best practices for handling HR data which is available [here](https://mdigital-my.sharepoint.com/:b:/g/personal/m306793_one_merckgroup_com/EUrBljvBGk9Ane3IHvjPQQ4BqH0r5aHpoAmQaRoJOHzdqw?e=3JFJoS). 

## Enhancement Requests

Enhancement requests can be requested through the Foundry tools or addressed directly to the HR Data Governance team via the team [email](mailto:HRDataGovernance@merckgroup.com). 

These will then be reviewed and assessed, and feedback provided to the requestors. Please note that we have very limited resources available for development. 

## Links - HR Data Governance

- [HR Data Governance Sharepoint - Entitlement Information](https://mdigital.sharepoint.com/sites/HR_DataGovernance/SitePages/Employee-Data-&-Technology-Approvals.aspx)
- [HR Data Governance - Data on UPTIMIZE Foundry](https://mdigital.sharepoint.com/sites/HR_DataGovernance/SitePages/UPTIMIZE%20DTI%20Approach.aspx)

- [HR Data governance email](mailto:HRDataGovernance@merckgroup.com)
