# Wrapper Groups

Wrapper groups, also often called capability or elevated groups give administrative access to the Foundry platform.

These are either managed by the

* SDAOS
* the Foundry platform team
* Palantir vendor teams.

## Continuous Monitoring

Wrapper groups are reviewed by the sectors every six months to ensure that only authorized individuals have access.

## Project Bootstrapper Functionality

When a project is created via the Project Bootstrapper App, e.g. during the use case lifecycle, when creating a DTI etc., wrapper groups are automatically added to the project's groups (owner/editor/viewer/discoverer) according to the project's type. 

## How to get access to a wrapper group

See our [tutorial](/request-access/).

## List of wrapper groups

For all sectors EF (as MGF), LS, EL, HC, global, there are the following types of groups.

### Use Case
* ``<sector>-use-case-viewer-member``,
* ``<sector>-use-case-editor-member``
* ``<sector>-use-case-owner-member``

having the respective access for all of the sector's use cases.


### Data Source 
* ``<sector>-data-source-viewer-member``
* ``<sector>-data-source-editor-member``
* ``<sector>-data-source-owner-member``

having the respective access for all of the sector's data source projects.


### Transforms 
* ``<sector>-transform-viewer-member``
* ``<sector>-transform-editor-member``
* ``<sector>-transform-owner-member``

having the respective access for all of the sector's transform projects.


### Ontology projects 

* ``<sector>-ontology-viewer-member``
* ``<sector>-ontology-editor-member``
* ``<sector>-ontology-owner-member``

having the respective access for all of the sector's ontology projects.


### Ontology objects

* ``<sector>-ontology-objects-viewer-member``
* ``<sector>-ontology-objects-editor-member``
* ``<sector>-ontology-objects-owner-member``

managing secturity access to all the sector's  object types.

### Sector-wide 

* ``<sector>-viewer-member``
* ``<sector>-editor-member``
* ``<sector>-owner-member``

having the respective access to **all** projects within this sector.

### Governance

* ``<sector>-governance-team``

are members of all the ``<sector>-owner-manage-permissions`` and may therefore manage permissions.

For HC, this is ``healthcare-governance-team``and for LS, this is ``ls-ace-platform-admins``.

### Manage Membership and Permissions

For all ``-member`` groups, there are also ``-manage-membership``, ``-manage-permissions`` groups, which we have omitted for readibility.

Manage Membership means that members of these groups may add or remove members to a group, whereas managing permissions allows giving other users the manage membership priviledge.


### Special wrapper groups


* ``global-audit-viewer``
* ``Foundry_Operations_Project_Viewer``
* ``<sector>-governance-team``


**Ressource Manager App**

* ``resource-management-viewer-restricted``: See Ressource Manager App, but not with currency.
* ``resource-management-viewer-non-restricted``: See Ressource Manager App, but not with currency.

Note: In order to see the the RMA App, the user needs to be part of the "Resource Management Viewer" group

**Foundry Support**

* ``UPTIMIZE_Foundry_PLATFORM`` contains Merck Foundry support. Allows users in this group to read, mutate issue and their status - For Operations team. 
* ``UPTIMIZE_Foundry_L1_L2`` contains Merck employees working on Foundry support. 

Legacy groups are described [here](https://wiki-nregprod.merckgroup.com/spaces/DAP/pages/239801716/User+Access+Management).


**Palantir (vendor) groups**

* ``mcloud-palantir``, ``mcloud-admin``: This team is for all members of Palantir that require admin privileges to the stack in order to keep the platform running smoothly.  <a href="https://palantir.mcloud.merckgroup.com/workspace/settings/groups/41150e62-3277-4fd6-9e55-0e5d2d6b19fc">Group Link</a>
* ``Foundry Support``
* ``Palantir Client Support``

---

# Platform Resource and Cost Management

This section provides tools and insights for monitoring, analyzing, and optimizing
resource consumption and associated costs within Palantir Foundry.

## Foundry cost model

Starting in 2025, Merck has a consumption contract in place with sector target commitments that will be established annually. 
This means, that each year, Merck sectors are billed the amount or their target commits as well as potential over-consumption. 

There are three dimensions of Foundry costs:

| Cost type | Cost description | Approx. Ratio |
| -- | -- | -- |
| **Foundry compute**	| compute seconds - represent a unit of computational work in the platform	| 90% (Transform ~50%, Vector ~15%, Contour ~10%, Ontology Query ~5%) |
| **Foundry storage**	| GB-month - how much disk space a single dataset consumes |	5% (Phonograph ~2%, Highbury ~2%) |
| **Ontology volume** |	GB-months	| 5% (mainly Catalog Storage) |

More information on the usage types can be found in [Palantir's Documentation](https://www.palantir.com/docs/foundry/resource-management/usage-types#compute-usage-with-aip).

### Cost of a dataset

Calculation of costs of a dataset (job duration): number of executors*min(number of core cpu, membory+overhead/7.5g)* time to build a code.
Note that usage is based on **allocated** vCPUs, not the actual utilization of those cores. Therefore, it is recommended to request only the necessary resources for your jobs.



## Cost Tracking

There are several ways of tracking costs and/or potential for over-consumption of use cases in Foundry.

| Method | Description |
| -- | -- |
| [Foundry Resource Manager](resource-manager/) | In-built application in Foundry to track Foundry usage. |
| [Use Case Price Tag](https://docs.uptimize.merckgroup.com/foundry/use-case-portal/use-case-price-tag/) | MDAO-managed application to track cost of use cases. |
| DTI Price Tag | MDAO-managed application to track cost of data treasury items. |
| [Foundry Linter](https://palantir.mcloud.merckgroup.com/workspace/linter/resource-savings) | The Linter application checks the state of Foundry for anti-patterns and suggests ways to move resources to a better state. You can use these recommendations to reduce cost, optimize your ontology, and increase pipeline stability and resilience. |




## Best practices

Establishing efficient consumption patterns of Foundry resources is crucial for the viability of UPTIMIZE Foundry. We collected a few tips and tricks for efficient use.

---

# Resource Management - User Documentation

## Overview
The **Resource Management** app in Palantir Foundry provides users and administrators with comprehensive tools to understand, monitor, and manage the utilization of platform resources. It is designed to offer actionable insights into compute and storage usage, costs, and billing, as well as to enable effective resource allocation across Projects and Organizations.

### Key Features

#### 1. Usage Visibility
**Monitor Resource Usage**: Track how Foundry resources (compute, storage, ontology volume) are consumed across Projects and usage accounts.
**Analyze Costs**: View detailed breakdowns of resource consumption and associated costs for billing and optimization purposes.
**Transparency Reports**: Access reports that show compute and storage resources consumed by Projects and Ontologies for greater transparency.

#### 2. Resource Allocation
**Define Resource Consumption**: Administrators can set policies for how Projects consume shared resources, including placing limits on usage.
**Resource Queues**: Manage and assign resource queues to Projects to control compute allocation and prioritize workloads
**Budgets**: Set and monitor budgets for resource usage to ensure spending stays within defined limits.


## 1. Overview

![RMA-overview](/assets/resource-manager/overview.png)

The **Overview** tab provides a high-level summary of key usage metrics, it gives users the opportunity to understand their usage at a glance, then drill into points of interest. Specifically, this tab gives an overview of:

- **Business Metrics Panel**: Displays high-level organizational metrics, including: *Average Daily Users*, *Number of Use Cases*, *Number of DTIs*, *Total Count of Users*.
- **Usage Panel**: Shows a time-series graph of **Foundry's core usage metrics**: *Foundry Compute* (measured in compute seconds), *Ontology Volume* (measured in GB/month), *Foundry Storage* (measured in GB/month)

Users can filter data for custom date ranges, by default last 30 days data is shown.

Additional breakdowns include:
- **Top Usage Accounts** e.g., *Life Science, Electronics, MDAO, Healthcare, Group Functions*  
- **Top Projects by Consumption**  
- **Top Sources** e.g., *Transforms, Contour, Code Workbook*  
- **Top Resources** e.g., *Workshop, Dataset, Contour*

---

## 2. Analysis

![RMA-analysis](/assets/resource-manager/analysis.png)

The **Analysis** section enables advanced filtering and segmentation of usage data. It gives users the opportunity to explore their usage data in more depth. Here, users can explore their usage by usage accounts, Project labels, Projects, Ontologies, sources, and more. Usage can be grouped together and explored in aggregate.

- **Date range**: The date range scopes the data displayed in the analysis to the specified date period.
- **Bucket period**: How data is bucketed for display in the usage chart.
  - Only complete buckets will be returned. Therefore, weekly or monthly bucket periods should only be used with aligned date ranges to ensure that the total usage values are correct.
  - Data loading will be slower for daily bucket periods than for weekly or monthly bucket periods.
- **Filtering**: Specifying a Project Label *(Transform, Data source, Use Case, ...)*, Usage Account *(Electronics, Group Functions, Healthcare, ...)*, Project or Ontology scopes, or Source *(GPT, Contour, Transform, Phonograph, ...)* the data displayed in the analysis to that area of the data hierarchy.
- **Group by**: Specifying a grouping allows users to group the data presented in the analysis by the selected criteria. Usage can be aggregated by *Usage Account*, *Project*, *Source*, *Resource*.


All of these selection mechanisms work in tandem to refine an analysis to a user's desired set of data, enabling visualization of *Foundry Compute*, *Ontology Volume*, and *Foundry Storage* for any selected filter combination.

---

## 3. Reports

![RMA-reports](/assets/resource-manager/reports.png)

The **Reports** tab allows users to download pre-generated usage reports for each **quarter** or **month** of the year.

---

## 4. Manage

![RMA-manage-usage](/assets/resource-manager/manage-usage.png)

Within the Manage section of the left navigation panel, users can access three subsections: Usage Accounts, Project Labels, and AIP Usage & Limits.

- **Usage Accounts**: The Usage Accounts subsection displays the projects associated with each usage account (e.g., Electronics, Healthcare, MDAO) as well as the corresponding user folders.
- **Project Labels**: The Project Labels subsection categorizes projects based on their assigned labels, such as Data Source, Transform, or Ontology projects.
- **AIP Usage and Limits**: The AIP Usage and Limits subsection monitors the consumption of AIP technologies (e.g., Charged GPT, Cloud-based LLM models). Users can view usage either globally or at the project level, with flexible time-based filters such as Last 24 Hours, Last 3 Days, or Last 7 Days. At the bottom of the subsection, a table displays the top projects by AIP consumption.

![RMA-aip-usage](/assets/resource-manager/aip-usage.png)

---

## 5. Optimize

Within the **Optimize** section of the left navigation panel, users can access three subsections: Resource queues, Trashed resources & Linter.

### 5.1 Resource Queues


A **Resource** refers to a compute unit, such as a virtual CPU (vCPU) or virtual GPU (vGPU), required to run workloads within a project.
A **Resource Queue** is a first-in, first-out (FIFO) queue that manages requests for these service-level resources. Resource Queues are used to control and limit the number of compute resources that can be utilized concurrently.

![RMA-resource-queues](/assets/resource-manager/resource-queues.png)

The **Resource Queues** view provides real-time monitoring of Foundry's compute infrastructure, displaying:

- Total virtual CPUs available (e.g., 4,875 vCPUs)
- Current active jobs
- Percentage of queue utilization

Available queue types include:

- Default Queue - the primary queue, supporting ~10,000 projects
- GPU Queue
- User Home Folder Queue
- Jail Queue
- LS Air Ingestion Queue

### 5.2 Trashed Resources

The **Trashed Resources** subsection lists projects and resources that have been moved to the trash and are pending permanent deletion.

![RMA-trashed-resources](/assets/resource-manager/trashed-resources.png)

At the top-right corner, users can access the *Manage Retention Policies* option, which allows configuration of how long trashed items are retained before deletion.
Retention periods can be customized by sector (e.g., *Electronics, Global, Tool Functions, Healthcare, Life Science*).

### 5.3 Linter
Opens the **Linter** application in a separate tab.  
**Purpose**: Identifies Foundry anti-patterns and recommends improvements to reduce costs and enhance pipeline stability.

---

# Foundry Cost Split

The general rule is: Foundry cost is allocated to the sector producing this cost. 

A sector in the Foundry cost sense can be:

* LS
* EL
* HC
* EF (currently still named MGF in Foundry)
* MDAO


## Cost sharing 

There are also shared costs called **Global** costs which are attributed monthly to the sectors according to their remaining usage of the platform. (E.g. if LS was responsible for 60% of the overall monthly Foundry platform cost, then they will get attributed 60% of the global costs.)

This cost sharing is done on a monthly basis at the beginning of each month for the previous month. These are the costs that will be billed to the sectors.

## Use Cases

For use cases, the defining attribute is the usage account (`usageAccountName`) defining the namespace of their projects. These are assigned based on the use case's business sector at the time of creation of the projects.

This information is accessible by accessing the project:

![RMA-overview](/assets/foundry/namespace.png)

**Exception: MDAO** 

The core app and other MDAO use cases are assigned to MDAO itself, not to Enabling Functions. Examples are Use Case Portal or Data Treasury.

If use cases fulfill

* namespace/sector equal to "Global"
* business unit division equal to "GF: Merck Data & AI Office (MDAO)"

then they are considered belonging to MDAO and projects will be considered as part of the MDAO-sector for cost purposes.


## Data Treasury Items (DTIs)

Similar to use cases, DTIs get their sector attribution from the project's `usageAccountName` which corresponds to the namespace except for MDAO.

## Personal Folders

Costs associated to personal folders is allocated to users' sector.

## Everything else

All other folders will be considered global and shared among the sectors (see Cost sharing).

---

# Resource Consumption Guidelines

It's important to recognize that there are numerous options available, and no single solution will lead to success. Instead, a holistic approach is essential by combining various strategies. 

## Decommissioning Strategies

* **Decommission Inactive or Unused Content**: Identify and remove inactive or unused use cases/ projects / data to immediately reduce consumption.
* **Proof of Value Assessment**: Evaluate the value of each use case over a defined period to determine whether to keep it live or decommission it.

<ld-notice headline="Hands-on guide">

* Simply clean up your project and delete those files not more needed.
* You can use for example Linter to check it or quickly go trough all your files.
* Deleting will move those artefacts to trash and remove the schedules. Take care also delete your trash as well from time to time

</ld-notice>



## Update Frequency Management

**Locate your Foundry schedules**: Start by [finding your Foundry schedules](https://palantir.mcloud.merckgroup.com/workspace/scheduler/find?v=1&uid=c869abfe-2493-43d4-b6c4-3c4cd8b42837&s=LAST_UPDATED_DATE&dir=DESCENDING) to start your analysis. Consult the [Palantir documentation]((https://palantir.mcloud.merckgroup.com/docs/foundry/building-pipelines/find-manage-schedules/)
).

**Change Frequency of Updates on Data Assets**: Adjust the frequency of updates for data assets to reduce resource consumption, ensuring that updates are made only when necessary.



<ld-notice headline="Hands-on guide">

**Review the frequency of the update**:

* Is its really needed to run the schedules hourly or daily if the data are anyhow only updated weekly? Change it.
* Do you have more than one input dataset? Check if the frequency is really needed for every dataset is been refreshed or only for the important once.
* Consolidate jobs that run on similar datasets.
 
**Find the best timing for your schedules**: Use the [Schedule Time Proposer](https://palantir.mcloud.merckgroup.com/workspace/slate/app/scheduling-timeframe-proposer/home). 


**Review best practices**: Check the [Palantir documentation on Scheduling best practices](https://palantir.mcloud.merckgroup.com/docs/foundry/building-pipelines/scheduling-best-practices/).


</ld-notice>





## Monitoring and Analysis

**Resource Usage Monitoring**: Use monitoring tools to analyze and track resource usage for each space, identifying areas for improvement.



<ld-notice headline="Hands-on guide">

As a use case owner, [review](https://docs.uptimize.merckgroup.com/foundry/resource-and-cost-management/) your use case's resource consumption regularly, at least on a monthly, better on a weekly basis.

</ld-notice>



## Performance Optimization

**Performance Tuning**: Optimize existing use cases/projects to reduce unnecessary resource consumption in the following areas:

### Pipelines

Streamline processes to enhance efficiency.


<ld-notice headline="Hands-on guide">

**Disable schedules on non-master branches**

* Non-master branches are rather development pipelines and should be used for productive purposes. Remove the schedules.
* Remove also unused branches to clean all data history.


**Evaluate whether all columns and rows in your pipeline are truly required** 

* Do you use millions of rows and hundreds of columns and only in the analytics solutions your are filtering? Change it and only add the once you needed in.
* Evaluating whether all columns and rows in your pipeline are truly required

**Move away from Contour to Pipeline Builder**
* Are you using contour for simple filtering, union or joining of data → move to Pipeline Builder as the costs are 20% only.
* Use the migration button and check out the Foundry documentation [here](https://palantir.mcloud.merckgroup.com/docs/foundry/pipeline-builder/overview/).

</ld-notice>

### Data processing and Transformation effiency

* Avoid persisting data in every transformation unless certain datasets are needed. For intermediate files, consider using a Python file with logic/functions to maintain readability without impacting compute resources.
* Before processing, filter out unnecessary rows and columns to minimize data movement and processing time. This ensures only relevant data is loaded into memory, significantly reducing execution time and resource consumption.

<ld-notice headline="Hands-on guide">

* **Column management** Bring only necessary columns to transformations and avoid array columns in objects. Also, avoid derived columns on the UI.
* **Aggregation Logic** Avoid on-the-fly aggregations and searches; instead, move the logic to the backend to enhance performance. See the [Palantir documentation](https://palantir.mcloud.merckgroup.com/docs/foundry/building-pipelines/considerations-pb-cr/).

</ld-notice>



<!-- ## Enhancing Code Efficiency

Refactor code to improve performance. TODO
-->

### Performance & Memory Optimization

* **Broadcasting datasets**: In Spark, datasets smaller than 10MB are automatically broadcast. If datasets are under 100MB and memory issues arise, consider broadcasting them manually to speed up join operations.
* **Data Partitioning**: Partition large datasets based on relevant keys (e.g., date, geography, or business unit) to improve query performance and facilitate parallel processing. See [Hive-style partitioning](https://palantir.mcloud.merckgroup.com/docs/foundry/optimizing-pipelines/hive-style-partitioning/).
* **Column Indexing**: Implement indexing on frequently queried columns to speed up data retrieval, especially in large tables, minimizing full table scans. See [Ontology indexing](https://palantir.mcloud.merckgroup.com/docs/foundry/ontologies/compute-usage/).
* **Memory Profile Review**: Regularly review memory profiles and make necessary adjustments to optimize resource. See [Spark Profile reference](https://palantir.mcloud.merckgroup.com/docs/foundry/optimizing-pipelines/spark-profiles-reference/).
* **Local Execution**: Enable local execution for transformations with input and output datasets smaller than a specified threshold using settings like the KUBERNETES_NO_EXECUTORS Spark profile. See [Spark concepts](https://palantir.mcloud.merckgroup.com/docs/foundry/optimizing-pipelines/spark-concepts/).



### Selecting Appropriate Computational Resources 

Be mindful to choose the right type and size of resources to match use case requirements. Consider using [DuckDB](/foundry/development-guidelines/duckdb-compute-engine/) as a compute engine instead of Apache Spark.


## Data Quality and Format

* **Primary key management**: Ensure that primary keys are deterministic by combining multiple columns, avoiding randomly generated keys. Check out the Palantir documentation on [streaming keys](https://palantir.mcloud.merckgroup.com/docs/foundry/building-pipelines/streaming-keys/).
* **Data Type Optimization**: Always store data in the most appropriate data type. For example, use date/time data types for date and time values instead of strings, as this enhances querying, sorting, and indexing efficiency.
* **Date Storage:** Store date and timestamp columns in their respective data type formats, not as strings.


## Regular Reviews and Audits

* **Conduct Regular Audits**: Perform regular audits of resource usage and costs to identify inefficiencies and areas for improvement.
* **Establish a Review Cycle**: Set up a regular review cycle for all use cases to assess their performance and cost-effectiveness.


## Use Case Checklist

LS has created a [checklist](https://wiki-nregprod.merckgroup.com/download/attachments/529475752/Checklist.xlsx?api=v2) of best practices. By adhering to these best practices, you can significantly enhance the efficiency and performance of your data processing workflows!

## Foundry Cost Optimization Community 

There is a Teams community dedicated to share best practices, known antipatterns, as well as tips and tricks. 

* [Teams Channel](https://teams.microsoft.com/l/channel/19%3A61f963dac81c424fb1ccf3bb1a982296%40thread.skype/Cost%20Optimization?groupId=35e1aa5a-f62f-4250-88bb-55618501f343&tenantId=db76fb59-a377-4120-bc54-59dead7d39c9)
* Do you have a specific question concerning your use case? Join the Foundry [office hours](https://docs.uptimize.merckgroup.com/foundry) and ask Merck's Foundry experts.

  * <ld-icon name="calendar"></ld-icon> Every Wednesday: 9 AM CEST on [MS Teams](https://palantir.mcloud.merckgroup.com/blobster/api/salt/ri.blobster.main.blob.70857a17-c4d6-4617-89be-12c709b4853f).
  * <ld-icon name="calendar"></ld-icon> Every Wednesday: 4 PM CEST on [MS Teams](https://palantir.mcloud.merckgroup.com/blobster/api/salt/ri.blobster.main.blob.9c60430b-22e5-4efe-adb5-aac8f9613235).

# Security
Please familiarize with the overall [Foundry Security Concept](https://palantir.mcloud.merckgroup.com/docs/foundry/security/overview/).

## Roles

In general, Roles are sets of permissions that grant different levels of access to resources. Roles are discretionary permissions assigned to users /user groups for particular resources and expand access (unlike Organizations and Markings, which are granted globally and restrict access) .

## Markings
In case, the RAW project space contains secured data (that's PII level), the user should be restricted from the View Access to this secured data. This is done by applying Markings on that resource that restricts in all or nothing fashion Foundry. A common use case for Markings is restricting access to **personally identifiable information (PII)**.

For example, you might have a group of users who are only eligible to access sensitive PII data after fulfilling a series of trainings. A platform administrator could create a Marking PII and apply it to the sensitive datasets. This ensures that access to PII is restricted to the appropriate users/groups and cannot be shared beyond that group.

## Roles vs. Markings

## Attention!

It is not allowed to add a Group to a Marking. Only add single users to a Marking!
**Markings** are a mandatory control while **Role(s)** are a discretionary control. Discretionary permissions are granted to users through data sharing workflows: for instance, creating a report and share it with a colleague, grants her view permissions on the report.

Discretionary controls expand a user's access. Mandatory controls -- on the other hand -- restrict access by requiring a user to have a particular Marking. Even if a colleague shares the report, if the dataset backing the report was marked with the **PII Marking**, access to the report is not granted unless the user is cleared for **PII** level data.

## Security in Pipelines

Please refer to the Palantir Documentation for best practices on [Security in Pipelines](https://palantir.mcloud.merckgroup.com/docs/foundry/building-pipelines/security-overview/)

---

# Tokens

No matter what token you use in your repository, no one else should be able to see it. **A token can be used by only having the token information**.

This is a big security issue and that's why we need to take care on how to handle tokens.

## Warning!

The change log of the repository will always remember the token if you used it in the repository once. Mark the used token as expired or delete it in the token manager if you used it in the code.

## Warning!

Tokens do expire! Be aware that you will have to renew your token depending on the expiration time you set.

## Solution:

Create a separate token for your repositories and add a clear description to it. This way you can always remove the token if a leak might have happened. Put your token inside a config_dataset inside the config folder of your project. Add a marking to the config_dataset, which only the editors and builders of the repository have as well. You can create this config_dataset using a fusion_sheet for example. Please make sure to also add the marking to the fusion_sheet in this case.

This way we have the project governance model first, but even more restricted using security markings.

Do not store tokens in a general token dataset and share it with multiple projects.

## Example:

If one has the marking to have access to an s-user token. One can still not access the dataset because it is still governed by the project access rules. As soon as one gets access to the project, one will have access to the token.

On the other hand, as long as one is not having the s-user token, but the access to the project. One can not see the token.

# How to Use Tokens:

## Code Example:

```bash

#...

def getToken(df):
    return df.dataframe().filter(F.col('attribute_name') == F.lit('token')).select(F.col('attribute_value')).collect()[0][0]  # noqa

@transform(
    out=Output("ri.foundry.main.dataset.17bfbef7-f720-4512-8175-ee018fa86c06"),
    config=Input(
        "ri.foundry.main.dataset.581b887c-c6ff-4fcf-aea0-4fa0200e90ff",
        stop_propagating=Markings(
            ['acf2b34d-1d11-4273-a818-d6fd7c9357bb'],
            on_branches=['master']
        )
    )
)

def compute(out, config, ctx):
    user_token = getToken(config)

#...
```

## Folder Structure:

```
├── analysis
├── config
│   └── config_dataset
├── data
│   ├── clean
│   ├── preprocessed
│   └── raw
├── logic
│   └── code_repository
└── playground
```

## Dataset Example:

![Picture 1](https://docs.uptimize.merckgroup.com/docs-assets/foundry/Foundry/Security/How_to_use_tokens/token_dataset.png)

## Fusionsheet Example:

![Picture 2](https://docs.uptimize.merckgroup.com/docs-assets/foundry/Foundry/Security/How_to_use_tokens/token_fusionsheet.png)

# Markings
In general, **Markings** are used to add an additional layer of permission management to resources. No matter what access rights a user has, as long as a file is flagged with a **Marking** the user does not have, the user cannot see or access the file.

Get more information about markings in the Palantir documentation [here](https://palantir.mcloud.merckgroup.com/docs/foundry/security/markings).

## Info!
In most cases, you do not need markings and normal access management is enough. By default, a Palantir group is assigned to the Marking as well. This is needed in order to help you recover your data in case you loose the Marking. In special cases, you can remove Palantir from the Marking as well.

## Example:
If you have sensitive data in your repository no one should access. But due to the standard Discoverer Role, everyone can see which files are in your repository (they can still not access it content). In order to avoid this, you can use Markings. Another example for using Markings is described in the [Token](https://palantir.mcloud.merckgroup.com/docs/foundry/security/markings/#use-markings) handling.

## How to request a Marking:
If you need a Marking on any of your folders or files, please reach out to your SDOs Marking Manager.

## Naming Convention:
Markings can be used to mark files and folders. Whereas a project is a folder and a repository is a file as well as all datasets are files. Therefore we devise the naming conversion into two different general topics.

`
<project-name>-<purpose>
`

<strong>Keep in Mind:</strong>`project-name` already includes the sector!


| **Purpose**                                       |**Value**|
|:--------------------------------------------------------------------|:---------------|
| Token or other credentials| `credentials`
| Compliance topics |  `internal, confidential`

## Examples:
- `global-mdo-use-case-operations-credentials`
- `mgf-super-important-data-internal`
- `hc-some-patents-data-secret`

## Category Overview:

| **Category Name**|**Purpose**|**Manager**
|:--------------------------------------------------------------------|:---------------|:---------|
| Governance Credentials | Holds Markings for governance related topics in general|*Florian Grzonka*
| Life Sciences |Holds Markings for Life Sciences related topics|*Carsten Goepp, Simon Heckmann, Nicolas Renkamp*
| Healthcare  | Holds Markings for Healthcare related topics|*Hannah Luksch, Sylvain Cecilio*
| Electronics | Holds Markings for Electronics related topics |*Daniel Stoeckel, Deniz Ertogrul*
|Group Functions|Holds Markings for Group Functions related topics|*Azmat Javed Arif*

## How to use:
If you want to use Markings, you need to be assigned to a **Markings Category**, in which you then can create your new **Markings**, set the permissions you need and afterwards apply them to your resources. Permissions for **Markings** are quite strict and after creating them you do not have any permissions to apply, change or have them. You need to set this permission separately after creating.

---

# Best Practices to Create Security Groups

## Permissions

### Grant Project access to Groups, Not Users

### Note:
Permissions will be more transparent and auditable if access is granted to Groups rather than Users.  
**Important:** Only Sector Data Office admins can create new groups. For Use Cases and any other project tpye, the groups are getting created automatically

- `Bad` - User X is granted view access to the Sensitive Financials project. It is not clear why this user receives this access.
- `Good`- User X is added to the Finance/Pricing Team, which has view access to the Sensitive Financials/pricing project. The reason for the user's access is now transparent: it results from membership in the Finance/Pricing Team, which can be readily validated.

Ensure that the Security groups *like owner, editor & viewer* are set up on the project level by your Sector Data Office based on the project requirements.

Naming concention examples for groups:

`<sector>-<projectname>-viewer`

`<sector>-<projectname>-editor`

`<sector>-<projectname>-owner`

### Assign Group membership to match the existing Organizational Structure

### Info

Group assignments are more easily understood if they correspond to a known organizational map.

- `Bad` - User X on the Customer Service team is added to the Sales Group to gain access to Sales datasets, which are required for a project.
- `Good` - The Customer Service Group is granted view access to a project containing Sales datasets that are required for common Customer Service workflows.

# Specific Module Guidelines

Browse the following pages to learn about Specific Module Guidelines

---

# Workshop Naming Conventions

Workshop modules are based in four kind of elements: pages, sections, widgets and variables. This page intents to provide some guidelines on how to name each of those elements.

As a summary, the naming conventions are:


| **Element**|**Name convention**|**Example**
|:---------|:---------------|:---------|
| Page | `Name-of-page (Overlay)`|Filters Overlay
| Section  | `Section Type-of-section - Name-of-section`|Section Rows - DTIs
| Widget |`Type-of-widget - Name-of-widget`|Button group - DTIs filters
| Variable | `[Page] Way-to-obtain - Name-of-variable`|Multipass - User Name

## Pages

Pages are not mixed with the sections and widgets, so there is no need to add any prefix. In the next screenshot we can see that the black rectangle highlights the pages and the purple one the sections.

![pages](https://docs.uptimize.merckgroup.com/docs-assets/foundry/Images/Specific_Module_Guidelines/wnc_pages.png)

Therefore, it is only needed to indicate if it is an overlay, which will be done with the Overlay sufix.

ⓘ Convention: Name-of-page (Overlay)

### Examples

Following the example of the screenshot, let's say the first page is the welcome page, the second one is where we will have information about use case objects and the overlay is for filters. Then good names could be, respectively, *Welcome, Use Case and Filters Overlay*.

## Sections

Sections are mixed with the widgets, so in this case one of both should be explicitly indicated.

There are different type of sections: columns, rows, tabs, flow and toolbar.

![sections 1](https://docs.uptimize.merckgroup.com/docs-assets/foundry/Images/Specific_Module_Guidelines/wnc_sections.png)

We will specify the type too, so we can identify the section kind directly in its name.

ⓘ Convention: Section Type-of-section - Name-of-section

### Examples

In the last screenshot example, if we decide to set a toolbar section which will contain filters for the use cases table, a proper name would be *Section Toolbar - UC filters*. The section above is a rows container for both use cases filters and table. A proper name in this case would be *Section Rows - UC*.

![sections 2](https://docs.uptimize.merckgroup.com/docs-assets/foundry/Images/Specific_Module_Guidelines/wnc_sections_2.png)

## Widgets

Since we use Section prefix for sections, we do not need to do the same for the widgets:

ⓘ Convention: Type-of-widget - Name-of-widget

### Examples

In the previous screenshot, inside the toolbar section we set a button group widget, so a proper name would be *Button group - UC filters*.

![widget](https://docs.uptimize.merckgroup.com/docs-assets/foundry/Images/Specific_Module_Guidelines/wnc_widgets.png)

## Variables

They are located in a different division, so there is no need to include Variable in the naming. Each variable has an icon indicating its type: string, object set, etc.

When we add a new variable, we firstly chose the type of it, and then the way to obtain it: static, by a function, an object property, etc.

![variable 1](https://docs.uptimize.merckgroup.com/docs-assets/foundry/Images/Specific_Module_Guidelines/wnc_variables.png)

Since we identify the type with the icon but there is no way do to the same with the way to obtain it, only the second one would be included in the name.

Lastly, we will add a prefix identifying the page where the variable is used. If it is a general one, used in several of them, no prefix will be added.

ⓘ Convention: [Page] way-to-obtain - name_of_variable

### Examples

If a string variable is containing the user name (obtained by multipass attribute) and used notjust in one page but more generally, a proper name would be *Multipass - User Name*.

![variable 2](https://docs.uptimize.merckgroup.com/docs-assets/foundry/Images/Specific_Module_Guidelines/wnc_variables_2.png)

---

# UPTIMIZE AI-ML API Usage Documentation

## Connecting UPTIMIZE AI-ML APIs from Foundry

UPTIMIZE AI-ML API hosted within the AWS factory environment offers a range of scalable APIs for information extraction from text. These APIs are either pretrained models or trained from scratch for specific use cases using popular NLP libraries such as Spark NLP, Spark OCR, and Hugging Face. AI-ML APIs are now accessible from the Foundry code repositories. Users of Foundry can access APIs using 'requests' python library.

The API token can be requested using this [form](https://palantir.mcloud.merckgroup.com/workspace/module/view/latest/ri.workshop.main.module.42365df1-f320-4c65-af29-c6f840a9d9da).

Foundry transformation function can be applied to a column of dataset as shown below.

## Pandas Based Transformation

```bash
@transform_pandas(
    Output("output_dataset"),
    source_df=Input("input_dataset"),
)
def compute(source_df):
    source_df['output_column'] = source_df['text_column'].apply(get_api_response)
    return source_df
```

## Spark Based Transformation with UDF

```bash
@transform_df(
    Output("output_dataset"),
    source_df=Input("input_dataset"),
)
def compute(source_df):
    get_pke_udf = F.udf(get_api_response, StringType())
    source_df = source_df.withColumn('output_column', get_pke_udf(F.col('text_column')))
    return source_df
```

For high throughput processing with APIs, we recommend partitioning the dataset. This can be done using following where `x` represents the number of partitions. Partitioning does not necessarily guarantee `x` defined parallel executors. For more information refer to [pyspark repartition](https://spark.apache.org/docs/latest/api/python/reference/api/pyspark.RDD.repartition.html).

`source_df = source_df.repartition(x)`

The response code is assigned to a new column in the same dataset.

## Spark Based Transformation with RDD

Spark UDFs are not optimal from performance point of view. It is recommended to use Spark internal functions whenever possible or use RDDs in the place of UDFs.

```bash
@transform_df(
    Output("output_dataset"),
    source_df=Input("input_dataset"),
)
def compute(source_df):
    source_df = source_df.select(col_1).rdd.map(lambda x: my_func(x)).toDF(["new_col1"])
    return source_df
```

## Procedure for accessing AI-ML APIs

**For connecting AI-ML APIs with from Foundry, you need to create a Data Connection Source with the base URL of the AI-ML APIs.**

### Data Connection Source

1.	Go to [Data Connection](https://palantir.mcloud.merckgroup.com/workspace/data-ingestion-app/splash)
2.	Click on "New Source"
3.	Select "REST API" under Protocol Sources
4. Overview - Click on Continue
5. Connection Type - Select "Direct connection"
6. Name and Location
    - For Life Science, please click here to follow the specified naming convention
    - For other sector, please click here to follow the suggested naming convention
    - For source type in the naming convention, please write "ai-ml"
7. Source Setup
    - Domain Base URL: api.nlp.{env}.uptimize.merckgroup.com ('dev' - DEV and 'p' - PROD).
    - Additional Secrets: You may use this to store multiple API keys for calling the AI-ML APIs, project or secret keys from Langfuse and MLflow credentials.
    - Network Connectivity: Please select the required policy.
        - api.nlp.dev.uptimize.merckgroup.com (Port 443) - DEV
        - api.nlp.p.uptimize.merckgroup.com (Port 443) - PROD
8. It is suggested to create two separate sources for DEV and PROD APIs rather than incorporating them within the same source.
9. For "Export Configuration" and "Code Import Configuration", please raise a Foundry support ticket and state the configurations that needs to be enabled for connecting your code repo with the AI-ML APIs. Below mentioned configurations are required to be enabled for successful connection. Other configurations than the ones mentioned below would depend upon your requirement and usage. The SDO Admin are responsible for enabling the below configurations. In the current flow, please click on 'Continue' and complete the steps.
    - Export Configuration: Enable exports to this source and Enable exports to this source without markings validations (optional)
    - Code Import Configuration: Allow this source to be imported into code repositories
10.	Please raise a Foundry support ticket and share the name and RID of your source.


### Import Source to Repo

To access the AI-ML APIs, the repo must have the permission to use external transforms. Three steps are needed to enable it:

1. Add the transforms-external-systems library to your code repository.

2. Please look for the world wide web symbol on the left side which has the label "External systems".

3. Search for the Source that you created and import it to the code repository.
    
### Code Example

You can then use the egress policy and credentials in order to place network calls against AI-ML APIs. Code such as the example below is then able to securely access the AI-ML APIs:

```python
from transforms.api import Output, Input, transform_pandas
from transforms.external.systems import external_systems, Source, ResolvedSource
import requests
import pandas as pd
import json


@external_systems(
    refresh_source=Source("ri.magritte..source.xxxxxxxx-xxxx-xxxx-xxxx-xxxxxxxxxxxx")
)


@transform_pandas(
    Output("ri.foundry.main.dataset.xxxxxxxx-xxxx-xxxx-xxxx-xxxxxxxxxxxx"),
    df=Input("ri.foundry.main.dataset.xxxxxxxx-xxxx-xxxx-xxxx-xxxxxxxxxxxx")
)


def compute(df, refresh_source):

    token = refresh_source.get_secret("additionalSecretApikey")  # please copy the key name as displayed in your source and this can be different for you
    df['output_column'] = df.apply(lambda x: get_api_response(x['text_column'], token), axis=1)

    return df


def get_api_response(text, token):
    url = "https://api.nlp.{env}.uptimize.merckgroup.com/{endpoint_name}"
    # Json request payload
    payload = json.dumps({
        <json-content>
    })
    # if headers required
    headers = {
        'x-api-key': token,
        'Content-Type': 'application/json'
    }
    response = requests.request("POST", url, headers=headers, data=payload)
    return response.text
```

{env} = dev if you are using APIs on the development environment.

{env} = p if you are using APIs on the production environment.


## Code Example for calling the GPT API

```python
def get_gpt_response(text):

    # Suppose a user wants to translate the text into English
    url = "https://api.nlp.{env}.uptimize.merckgroup.com/openai/deployments/gpt-4o-mini/chat/completions?api-version=2024-02-01"
    prompt = "Translate the text given after the newline into English"
    payload = json.dumps({"messages": [{"role": "user", "content": prompt+"\n"+str(message)}]})
    headers = {
        'x-api-key': '{API key goes here}',
        'Content-Type': 'application/json'
    }
    response = requests.request("POST", url, headers=headers, data=payload)

    return response.text
```

**Note:** API tokens are provisioned for use cases. We recommend using dedicated token for each use case. Since tokens are confidential in nature, it is advised to use [Foundry Markings](https://palantir.mcloud.merckgroup.com/docs/foundry/security/markings) to secure and restrict access to the provisioned tokens.

For any further details about UPTIMIZE AI-ML APIs, please contact [R138791@merckgroup.com](https://palantir.mcloud.merckgroup.com/workspace/documentation/R138791@merckgroup.com)

# UPTIMIZE NLP API Interactive Usage Documentation

In order to use UPTIMIZE NLP API interactively on Foundry frontend applications like Workshop, some more steps are necessary with respect to an implementation in a Python Code Repository.

## Defining the connection to UPTIMIZE NLP APIs from Foundry

The first step consists in creating a new model adapter library.
* Create a new Code Repository.
* Select the `Model` option.
* Select `Model Adapter Library`.

Once the repository has been initialized, and create a new file named e.g. `uptimize_nlp.py`. The following example can be changed and expanded depending on the specific needs.

```python
import palantir_models as pm
import openai


class UptimizeAdapter(mp.ExternalModelAdapter):
    def __init__(self, base_url, api_type, api_version, model, api_key):
        openai.api_base = base_url
        openai.api_type = api_type
        openai.api_version = api_version
        openai.api_key = api_key
        self.model = model
        self.client = openai.AzureOpenAI(
            azure_endpoint=base_url,
            api_key=api_key,
            api_version=api_version,
        )

    @classmethod
    def init_external(cls, external_context) -> 'pm.ExternalModelAdapter':
        base_url = external_context.base_url
        api_type = external_context.connection_config['api_type']
        api_version = external_context.connection_config['api_version']
        model = external_context.connection_config['model']
        api_key = external_context.resolved_credentials['api_key']
        return cls(base_url, api_type, api_version, model, api_key)

    @classmethod
    def api(cls):
        inputs = {'df_in': pm.Pandas(columns=[('prompt', str)])}
        outputs = {'df_out': pm.Pandas(columns=[('prompt', str), ('prediction', str)])}
        return inputs, outputs

    def predict(self, df_in):
        predictions = []
        for _, row in df_in.iterrows():
            payload = [{
                'role': 'user',
                'content': row['prompt']
            }]
            response = client.chat.completions.create(
                messages=payload,
                model=self.model,
            )
            predictions.append(response.choices[0].message.content)
        df_in['prediction'] = predictions
        return df_in
```

For this code to be usable, it's necessary to tag it after committing the changes.

No special permissions are necessary for this repository.

## Managing the connection

The next step consists in the creation of a new Model.
* Select `Connect an externally hosted model`.
* Select the `api.nlp.dev.uptimize.merckgroup.com` egress policy. If you don't have permission to assign this egress policy, issue a ticket to request it.
* Select the model adapter repository, then the desired version, and finally the desired adapter class.
* Add the base URL.
* In the custom model connection area, add the values of `api_type`, `api_version`, and `model`.
* In the credentials area, add the value of `api_key`.

Once the model is created, from inside it create a new Modeling Objective. In order to be able to use the model, release it to staging.
* From the Modeling Objective, release the Model to staging.
* Create a new deployment. Make sure to set the deployment as live.
* Set an API name for the deployment, e.g. `UptimizeStaging`.

### Notes and suggestions

* Once the model is released to staging, it will consume resources. If you don't need a model, remember to disable its deployment.
* The Python code provided above is a simple example that manages a single model. If more than one model is required, it is better to have a single class able to manage all the necessary models (e.g. through the use of an additional column `model`in `df_in`), than multiple classes.

### Model adapter upgrade

The following steps detail how to upgrade a model.
* Change the code in the model adapter library. Commit and tag the new version.
* Create a new model, following the steps above. As of mid July 2024, Foundry allows only to update models trained locally. This may change in the future.
* Add the new model to the modeling objective.

## Using the connection

The connection cannot be used directly in Workshop and similar apps. Instead, it's necessary to create TypeScript functions to manage them.
* In a TypeScript repository, import the Modeling Objective(s) created before.
* Create two new files named e.g. `types.ts` and `external_services.ts`, and adapt the following code to your needs:

```typescript
export interface UptimizeModel {
    predict: (prompt: string) => Promise<UptimizeResponse>
}

export interface UptimizeRequest {
    prompt: string
}

export interface UptimizeResponse {
    prompt: string
    prediction: string
}
```

```typescript
import { UptimizeStaging } from "@foundry/models-api/deployments"
import { UptimizeRequest, UptimizeResponse } from "./types"


export class UptimizeStagingModel {
    public async predict(prompt: string): Promise<UptimizeResponse> {
        const request: UptimizeRequest = {
            'prompt': prompt,
        }
        return await UptimizeStaging
            .transform([request])
            .then((output: any) => output[0]) as UptimizeResponse
    }
}
```

Finally, to be able to perform calls to the API, you can use the following code template in any other `ts` file:

```typescript
import { UptimizeStagingService } from "./external_services"
import { UptimizeModel, UptimizeResponse } from "./types"


export class APICalls {
    UptimizeStagingService: UptimizeModel = new UptimizeStagingModel

    public async apiCall(prompt: string) => string {
        const response: UptimizeResponse = UptimizeStagingService.predict(prompt)
        return response.prediction
    }
}
```

## Modeling adapter in a Python repository

The modeling adapter repository can be released as a Python library. This means that it can be imported and used inside other Python repositories.

Using the model adapter in this way requires that the Python repository has all the necessary rights to perform calls to external APIs.

## Contact information

For questions, please send an email to [pinwheel@merckgroup.com](mailto:pinwheel@merckgroup.com).

# Uptimize Foundry Custom Widgets

## Overview

Custom widgets enable application builders to securely extend Foundry applications with custom frontend code. Currently, custom widgets are only supported in Workshop.

With custom widgets, technical builders can implement functionality not available out-of-the-box and provide a tailored experience for application users without needing to create a whole standalone custom application from scratch.

Examples that could be built with custom widgets:
- A custom chart visualization such as a candlestick chart
- An industry-specific view of an ontology object such as a flight plan
- A signature entry widget

## Official Documentation

For detailed information on creating and managing custom widgets, refer to the [official Foundry custom widgets documentation](https://palantir.mcloud.merckgroup.com/docs/foundry/custom-widgets/).

## Enabling Ontology SDK

To enable Ontology SDK in a custom widget, due to technical limitations, users should:

1. Raise a [**Foundry Issue**](https://palantir.mcloud.merckgroup.com/workspace/issues-app/)
2. Share the **URL of the custom widget set**
3. Provide their **sector**

The support team will then enable Ontology SDK usage for the widget set.

# AIP

[UPTIMIZE Foundry](https://palantir.mcloud.merckgroup.com) offers AIP (Artificial Intelligence Platform), a generative AI toolkit, which supports a wide range of generative AI use cases. Seamlessly integrated into UPTIMIZE Foundry, AIP enables the rapid development of generative AI applications and the easy enhancement of existing use cases with advanced AI features. This integration is particularly advantageous when the entire use case, including its data, is already stored within UPTIMIZE Foundry, allowing for streamlined development on a single platform.

Prime use cases consist of integration of agents in business workflows to e.g. summarize available information from related object types, analyze documents, find and treat risks etc. 

Checkout the [Gen AI guidelines](https://docs.uptimize.merckgroup.com/guidelines/gen_ai/gen_ai-guideline-overview/) for an overview over the toolset available in UPTIMIZE.

By using modules of AIP, you agree to adhere to the [Foundry AIP terms and conditions](https://docs.uptimize.merckgroup.com/foundry/aip/aip-terms-and-conditions/).

## Modules

### [AIP Logic](https://palantir.mcloud.merckgroup.com/docs/foundry/logic/overview/)
No-Code tool for LLM-Powered functions that offers an easy-to-use platform for developing LLM powered functionality, enabling the straightforward creation of complex logic blocks. With prompt adaptation seamlessly integrated with UPTIMIZE Foundry's data and ontologies, along with intuitive chain-of-thought debugging, this environment facilitates the rapid development of generative AI features. Users can efficiently build and refine Gen AI capabilities without the need for extensive coding, leveraging UPTIMIZE Foundry's robust and secure infrastructure for streamlined and effective AI solution creation.

### [AIP Agent Studio](https://palantir.mcloud.merckgroup.com/docs/foundry/agent-studio/overview/)
Create reusable agents on specific data and tools (chat focused).

### [Automate AIP Integration](https://palantir.mcloud.merckgroup.com/docs/foundry/logic/aip-logic-integration-automate)
AIP Logic can now be automated such that Ontology edits can be automatically applied or staged for human review. These automations can be triggered on existing objects or when new objects are created.

### [OSDK AIP Integration](https://palantir.mcloud.merckgroup.com/docs/foundry/ontology-sdk-react-applications/overview)
Build an fully fledged web-app accessing the ontology now also including AIP integration.

### [AIP Evals](https://palantir.mcloud.merckgroup.com/docs/foundry/aip-evals/overview/)
A testing environment to evaluate the performance of your AIP Logic, AIP Agent or code-authored functions.

### [AIP Observability](https://palantir.mcloud.merckgroup.com/docs/foundry/aip-observability/overview/)
Overview over AIP workflow executions, helping users to understand performance of agents, functions, language models, automation, Actions and Ontology.

### [AIP Model Catalog](https://palantir.mcloud.merckgroup.com/docs/foundry/model-catalog/overview/)
Helps with discover and orientation of all LLM models provided by Palantir.
 
### [AIP Assist](https://palantir.mcloud.merckgroup.com/docs/foundry/assist/overview/)
LLM-powered support tool designed to help users navigate and understand the Foundry platform.

## Support

In case of questions, you can join:
* [MS Teams Foundry User Community](https://teams.microsoft.com/dl/launcher/launcher.html?url=%2F_%23%2Fl%2Fchannel%2F19%3Aa1464290282642f1bdd5af154cc8a1aa%40thread.skype%2FGeneral%3FgroupId%3D35e1aa5a-f62f-4250-88bb-55618501f343%26tenantId%3Ddb76fb59-a377-4120-bc54-59dead7d39c9&type=channel&deeplinkId=45cf0f19-8549-427e-b934-03c6d28b6ed1&directDl=true&msLaunch=true&enableMobilePage=true&suppressPrompt=true)
* Foundry Office Hours: [Wednesdays 9AM CEST](https://palantir.mcloud.merckgroup.com/blobster/api/salt/ri.blobster.main.blob.70857a17-c4d6-4617-89be-12c709b4853f) and [4PM CEST](https://palantir.mcloud.merckgroup.com/blobster/api/salt/ri.blobster.main.blob.9c60430b-22e5-4efe-adb5-aac8f9613235)

# AIP Terms and Conditions

UPTIMIZE Foundry is the central data and analytics platform in UPTIMIZE, which is Merck's transformative ecosystem empowering all Merck users to convert data into actionable insights to support various business functions. UPTIMIZE Foundry is made available by Merck KGaA, Frankfurter Straße 250, 64293 Darmstadt and its associated group companies (**"Merck"**). 

In UPTIMIZE Foundry, users may create and maintain use cases to contain the data and analytics products they want to develop. As a Merck user, AIP allows you to leverage AI tooling and models for your use case - consisting of different modules and features of the Artificial Intelligence Platform in UPTIMIZE Foundry (**"AIP"**). In using **AIP** for a use case, you must acknowledge these terms (**"Terms"**), and respect them at all times. 

### What is AIP in UPTIMIZE Foundry?
AIP contains various tools and features leveraging Artificial Intelligence (AI) to support Merck employees with data use cases on the UPTIMIZE Foundry platform. They can create their own generative AI applications within their use cases using natural language (**'prompts'**). These applications may then leverage predefined semantic connections (or **'ontologies'**) within UPTIMIZE Foundry to help users gain insights and/or create workflows to support their business processes.

Different AI models are available within AIP provided via Palantir's secure cloud infrastructure and are hosted in different platforms depending on the specific LLM selected (AWS Bedrock, Azure OpenAI, GCP Vertex) or hosted by Palantir for the open-source Llama and Mistral models. You can check the model provider for all available models, as well as the geographical restrictions [here](https://palantir.mcloud.merckgroup.com/docs/foundry/aip/supported-llms#llm-availability-by-geography).

For the AIP Assist feature (chat assistant within UPTIMIZE Foundry), Azure OpenAI models are used.

### What capabilities does it offer?

AIP includes features such as:

*	no-code LLM-powered functions running on Foundry data and/or ontologies (AIP Logic)
*	reusable, chat-focused agents on specific data and tools similar to myGPT assistants that can also access and operate on Foundry ontologies and data (AIP Agent Studios)
*	assistance with Foundry platform questions (AIP assist)
*	integration of agents and generative AI in Foundry workflows (AIP integration with Foundry Automate)
*	and a testing environment for generative AI applications (AIP Evals).  

### Do I need an approval to use AIP?
AIP has been approved for general use by Data Privacy, IT Security and ITK. **As long as your use of the AIP is compliant with these Terms in **full**, then the usual data approval rules for UPTIMIZE Foundry apply**. Specific approval is however needed for any use of AIP that does not comply with these Terms. For example, if the primary focus of your use case involves the processing of Personal Identifiable Information (PII), then additional approvals by Data Privacy, IT Security and ITK must be obtained **in advance**. When in doubt about whether your use case or assistant needs additional approvals, please reach out to Andreas Kubicki via [ITK@merckgroup.com](mailto:ITK@merckgroup.com).

## 1.     Access
**AIP** is available to anyone permissioned on UPTIMIZE Foundry with a valid MUID including externals. 

## 2.     Responsible use

**AIP** is to be used strictly for legitimate work-related purposes only and must be used responsibly at all times. In particular, output from solutions based on LLMs and AI technology can be prone to errors, inaccuracies, and 'hallucinations' - meaning false, misleading or totally invented information is presented to users. Further, the available models may not have been trained specifically on our data sets.

As such, each user is responsible for verifying and amending any content or output produced through **AIP**, especially before further redistributing or relying upon it, or in misrepresenting it as having been produced by yourself. **AIP** is generally not intended to replace individual responsibilities and tasks, but rather as a complement and potential efficiency gain when carrying them out.

For further guidance regarding copyright questions and concerns, please see our  [AI Governance Group Standard](https://mango.merckgroup.com/cara/drl/mango_document/6274273).

## 3.      Unauthorised Use

*	**Prohibition of Harm**<br>
**AIP** must not be used in any way in which a service interruption, defect, error, or other failure could result in the death, harm or serious bodily injury of any person, nor any physical or environmental damage or harm.
*	**Prohibition of Use with or related to Medical Devices**<br> 
**AIP** must not be used as a medical device(s), or as a substitute for professional medical advice, diagnosis, treatment, or judgment. 
* **Any Use contrary to the terms of the AI Governance Standard**

Please also note **AIP** must not be used in the following ways especially.

* As a substitute or part of any GxP-related process or task.
* In ways that might breach applicable laws and regulations, our company policies and code of conduct, or generally, in any way that might jeopardize the company's values and interests.
* To damage, disable, overburden, or impair the service, or use the service in excessive ways.
* For any purposes that could lead to any discrimination against certain people or characteristics, including gender or gender identity, culture or national origin, ethnic origin, race, color, religion or beliefs, disabilities, age, sexual orientation, family or marital status, or military or veteran status.
* Behavior or language that encourages an offensive or hostile working environment.

Further, be aware that Merck may face legal and financial liability from any such unauthorized use.

Merck reserves the right to reasonably monitor the usage of **AIP** to protect against any suspected violations of the above, including the right to remove or stop access to offending content without notification, or to suspend or terminate user access immediately.

In addition, any information provided by **AIP** does not replace legal advice. While **AIP** uses advanced algorithms and data analysis, any outputs from it cannot replace the professional judgment of qualified legal counsel nor a thorough legal review. In case of legal questions or concerns, please reach out to your legal business partner.

Azure OpenAI Models are the sole LLMs powering **AIP** "native" features including Assist. Please note turning off Azure Open AI as an enabled model will disable significant **AIP** functionality.|

## 5.     Intellectual Property Protections and Considerations
Output created through **AIP** may not be protected by copyright or other intellectual property rights (IP).

Help protect the company's interest by ensuring the following.

*  Avoid infringements: Do not upload or process any third-party content through **AIP** unless you are absolutely sure that we have the relevant rights to use, including reproduce, and create derivative works in such a way.
* No exclusive rights: Do not use **AIP** to contribute to or create work (e.g. images, texts,  software, codebase, source code, marketing materials, product packaging, product design, interview text, etc.) for which Merck wishes to obtain exclusive rights by way of IP protections, such as copyright, trademark rights, design rights, utility models or patent rights.
* Internal documentation: **If you use or include output generated throught myGPT, in particular visual assets and images, into other materials or works that are used externally, ensure to internally document those elements that are AI-generated.**  

For further guidance regarding copyright questions and concerns, check out the [new Group Copyright Standard](https://evarooms.merckgroup.com/Organization/Legal-Compliance/Pages/News/Navigating-the-new-age-of-creativity-How-we-deal-with-copyright-in-the-times-of-AI.aspx) or the corresponding [Copyright Assistant on myGPT](https://evarooms.merckgroup.com/Organization/Legal-Compliance/Pages/News/Navigating-the-new-age-of-creativity-How-we-deal-with-copyright-in-the-times-of-AI.aspx).

## 6.    Confidential Information

Do not use **AIP** to process information marked (or reasonably evident) as secret, meaning whose publication could result in serious reputational, economic or legal consequences for the company.

**By default, all information shared or created through **AIP** will be considered confidential and should not be shared** outside Merck without respecting our relevant policies and approval processes. More information on how such information is classified can be found in the [Merck Cyber Security Hub](https://evarooms.merckgroup.com/Topic/cybersecurityhub/Pages/Home.aspx).

Data subject to NDA/CDA or other third-party confidentiality obligations (collectively referred to as "CDA Terms") may only be stored, processed, or used in accordance with these terms.

Before inserting such data, ensure that the CDA Terms authorize the storage, processing, and intended use (including with AI or cloud technologies), and that all necessary safeguards and restrictions set forth in the CDA Terms are implemented

## 7.     Personal Information (PII)
By default, **AIP** should not be specifically used to process PII - meaning any information (such as name, email, title, DOB or even addresses) capable of identifying individual people. Any use case intending to use personally identifiable information needs approval by the [ITK](https://evarooms.merckgroup.com/topic/itk/Pages/Home.aspx) (IT Commission).

Further, **AIP** must not be used to process more sensitive data such as the health information of patients, employee records, or characteristics such as race, nationality or gender. Always respect the privacy of others when using the tool and our company Data Protection principles and safeguards - more information on which can be found on the [Data Privacy EVA page](https://evarooms.merckgroup.com/Organization/LE-C/data-privacy/data-privacy-program/risk-assessment-documentation).

## 8.     Monitoring by Merck
Merck reserves the right to reasonably monitor usage of **AIP** to ensure our legal obligations, and that these Terms are respected. This may be, for example, to investigate potentially unauthorized behavior and interactions from users, but also to better understand how certain features are being used and to help improve features and functionalities where appropriate.

Prompts submitted to **AIP** are not stored or retained by third party-hosted model service providers. All data in prompts and completions is immediately discarded after processing, and no third-party personnel have access to this data. This is enforced by contract restrictions between Palantir and third-party model providers. All data transmitted to the underlying services are immediately discarded after prompt completion.

Within Palantir **AIP** itself, the platform provides robust auditing and governance capabilities. This includes generating detailed audit trails and maintaining historical lineage for AI operations, which can include records of prompt interactions, especially in the context of workflow executions, functions, or actions. These audit trails help ensure transparency, explainability, and accountability in AI workflows. This information could eventually be accessed by the Foundry platform admin teams.

## 9.     Data storage and location

When using AIP, user prompts may be processed by third party-hosted large language model (LLM) services in different geographic regions, including the US, UK, and EU. **AIP** is designed to leverage regional endpoints wherever available, helping to minimize latency and support data residency requirements. The specific region used for processing depends on the technical capabilities and restrictions of the third-party model service selected, and may change over time. 

Geo-restrictions are defined by enrollment, and therefore, only models available in that region will be available to users, and all LLM requests will be processed in that region. You can check all available models and regional geo-restriction options [here](https://palantir.mcloud.merckgroup.com/docs/foundry/aip/supported-llms#llm-availability-by-geography).

Importantly, no customer data contained in prompts or completions is stored or retained by third party-hosted model service providers. All data transmitted to these services is immediately discarded after processing, and no third-party personnel have access to this data. Palantir secures strict technical and contractual guarantees to ensure these privacy and security standards are upheld.

## 10. Responsibility of the use case owner
Use case owner are responsible for all **AIP** components in their use case and for compliance with these terms

## 11.     Language, capacity and performance limitations
Although **AIP** has multi-lingual capabilities, the overall platform, including menus, icons, and other interface elements, is generally based on the English language.

Limitations with **token length / context window** size are associated with each LLM. Based on the selected LLM and the size/length of the message history in a particular conversation, the model might omit messages from that conversation's message history to better fit subsequent requests. If you exceed this limit, you will receive an error and may need to start a new session or reduce the input size. 

Some of the offered LLMs also carry time-bound rate limits, meaning that a user can only generate a certain number of answers during a given time period. If a rate limit is reached, a user must wait for the time period to end until they can use that specific LLM again or switch to a different LLM in the meantime. 

Due to how they are built and trained, LLMs may have so-called knowledge cut-off dates, meaning they may access information or provide responses that are no longer up to date. For example, the knowledge cut-off date of the LLM "GPT-4o mini" is October 2023, meaning it may not have knowledge of events or information beyond that date. 

When using **AIP** Assist functionality, please consider that Azure OpenAI LLMs are being used, so all restrictions applicable to these models are present here too.

## 12.  Modification, suspension, and termination

# Foundry Beta Testing

The Foundry platform is continuously improved by the platform developer team "Foundry Wizzards". In order to make sure that all new features are also aligned with all sectors, we use the following beta testing procedure.

## Beta testers

The Foundry product owner maintains a list of beta testers. 

Within Foundry, access to new features is given via the preset_group `global-use-case-uptimize-foundry-beta-features-custom-group-upcoming-wizzards-features`. To request access to this group, you can follow these steps :

1. Open [UPTIMIZE Foundry Application Access and Beta Features](https://palantir.mcloud.merckgroup.com/workspace/module/view/latest/ri.workshop.main.module.cfbd54d9-5f5e-4c67-a94d-37fc842812cc?pageId=shared&useCaseId=6262f6a2-f974-46be-9b8e-49c5f0dc2c90) Use Case.
1. Click on "Request Access to Use Case".
1. In the form, select "Upcoming Wizards Features" under Preset field. 
1. Fill the rest of the form and Submit your request.


<img src="/assets/foundry/foundry-beta-testing-access.svg">


Announcements are made in the Teams Channel [**UPTIMIZE Foundry User Group: Foundry Beta Testing Mages**](https://teams.microsoft.com/l/channel/19%3A1643a2a90a594cdf87cc2b277415ea1a%40thread.skype/Foundry%20Beta%20Testing%20Mages?groupId=35e1aa5a-f62f-4250-88bb-55618501f343&tenantId=db76fb59-a377-4120-bc54-59dead7d39c9&ngc=true).

Please contact the Foundry product owner or your SDAO to be added to beta testing.

## Feature testing

Once a feature becomes ready for testing, the leading developer will perform the following steps:

1.	Add the the Beta-Testing preset to the feature.
1.	Write short summary in the Teams group and asks beta testers to review. Give a timeframe for beta-testing, by default a week.
1.	Take note of any discussion and adds it into the user story in DevOPS.
1.	Beta Testing should be completed and feedback implemented before a system demo to general audience.
